## Assistant (2026-04-19 14:37:46)

I’m pushing on the actual one-pair geometry now rather than just repackaging the finite-core statement. The key question is whether the draft already gives enough derivative control on \((\alpha,\beta,\gamma/\beta)\) to force genuine space-curve nondegeneracy, because that would kill the new collinear/coplanar configurations directly.

_Thought for 4m 46s_

Here is the cleanest next push I think is actually solid.

The right move is to stop trying to kill finite cores directly, and instead isolate the **one-pair local space-curve invariants** that would kill them.

On a patch where
\[
v_5\neq 0,
\]
set
\[
a(h):=\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad
s(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)}.
\]
Then the lifted curve is
\[
Q_v(h)=(a(h),x(h),s(h)).
\]

This is the right local object, because in the defect-free order-\(\le 7\) model a bad finite core gives
\[
\sum_j b_j=0,\qquad
\sum_j b_j\,a(h_j)=0,\qquad
\sum_j b_j\,x(h_j)=0,\qquad
\sum_j b_j\,s(h_j)=0,
\]
with \(b_j=a_jc(h_j)\). So the points \(Q_v(h_j)\) are affinely dependent.

That means:

- a bad 2-point core gives a **coincidence** on \(Q_v\),
- a bad 3-point core gives a **collinear triple** on \(Q_v\),
- a bad 4-point core gives a **coplanar quadruple** on \(Q_v\).

So the next real one-pair problem is:

> show that on the relevant patches, \(Q_v\) has no three collinear points and no four coplanar points.

And there is a very clean local criterion for that.

Since on an ECT interval we already know
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0,
\]
the coordinate \(x=v_5/c\) is a valid local parameter. So write locally
\[
a=A(x),\qquad s=S(x),
\]
and view the space curve as
\[
Q_v(x)=(A(x),x,S(x)).
\]

Then two local invariants appear naturally.

First,
\[
\mathcal C_v(x):=S''(x).
\]

Second,
\[
\mathcal T_v(x):=A''(x)S'''(x)-A'''(x)S''(x).
\]

These are the right curvature/torsion-type quantities for the lifted curve.

Why they matter:

If \(\mathcal C_v(x)\neq 0\) on an interval, then the planar graph
\[
x\longmapsto (x,S(x))
\]
is strictly convex or strictly concave there. Any three collinear points on the space curve \(Q_v\) would project to three collinear points on that planar graph, which is impossible. So:

> If \(S''\neq 0\) on a patch, then \(Q_v\) has no three collinear points on that patch.

That kills the 3-point branch locally.

More importantly, if \(\mathcal T_v(x)\neq 0\), then the four functions
\[
1,\quad A(x),\quad x,\quad S(x)
\]
form a local ECT system of order \(4\). Indeed their Wronskian is
\[
W_x(1,A,x,S)
=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & A & x & S\\
0 & A' & 1 & S'\\
0 & A'' & 0 & S''\\
0 & A''' & 0 & S'''
\end{pmatrix}
=
A''S'''-A'''S''
=
\mathcal T_v(x).
\]
So if \(\mathcal T_v\neq 0\), every affine plane equation
\[
\lambda_0+\lambda_1A(x)+\lambda_2x+\lambda_3S(x)=0
\]
has at most three zeros counting multiplicity. Equivalently:

> If \(\mathcal T_v\neq 0\) on a patch, then no affine plane meets \(Q_v\) in more than three points there.

That kills the 4-point branch locally.

So the whole finite-core issue on a \(v_5\neq0\) patch reduces to the one-pair local invariants
\[
\mathcal C_v=S''(x),
\qquad
\mathcal T_v=A''S'''-A'''S''.
\]

In the original \(h\)-parameter, these are

\[
\mathcal C_v(h)
=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
x'(h) & s'(h)\\
x''(h) & s''(h)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
up to the harmless factor \(x'(h)^3\), and

\[
\mathcal T_v(h)
=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
a'(h) & x'(h) & s'(h)\\
a''(h) & x''(h) & s''(h)\\
a'''(h) & x'''(h) & s'''(h)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
up to the harmless factor \(x'(h)^6\).

Explicitly,
\[
a(h)=\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad
s(h)=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}.
\]

So these are canonical local determinants built from the strengthened one-pair package.

That gives the exact next theorem to aim for:

**Local lifted nondegeneracy theorem on \(v_5\neq0\) patches.**  
On every relevant generic patch with \(c\neq0\), \(M\neq0\), \(W\neq0\), and \(v_5\neq0\),
\[
\mathcal C_v\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal T_v\neq 0.
\]

If that theorem holds, then on each such patch:

- no 3-point defect-free bad core can live there,
- no 4-point defect-free bad core can live there.

That is already a major reduction.

There is a parallel \(u_5\neq0\) patch version. Define
\[
t(h):=-\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)u_5(h)},
\qquad
Q_u(h)=\left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{v_5}{c},t(h)\right),
\]
and then the corresponding invariants are
\[
\mathcal C_u,\qquad \mathcal T_u.
\]
So globally the finite-core problem gets reduced to proving nondegeneracy of the lifted one-pair curve on the two local gauges.

This is the strongest honest push I see right now, because it converts the vague minimal-core theorem into a concrete local analytic target.

What I do **not** think we can currently claim is that the draft already proves \(\mathcal C_v\neq0\) or \(\mathcal T_v\neq0\). The existing ECT machinery proves nonvanishing for the planar curve
\[
\Gamma(h)=\left(\frac{v_5}{c},\frac{\Delta_7}{c}\right),
\]
which is a different object. So the draft does not yet control the lifted torsion invariant. That is the real next missing one-pair theorem.

So the mathematical gain is:

- the finite-core obstruction is now reduced to a one-pair lifted curve problem,
- the right one-pair invariants are \(\mathcal C_v,\mathcal T_v\) and their \(u\)-patch analogues,
- proving their nonvanishing would kill local 3-point and 4-point defect-free cores.

The next push, if you want to keep going, is to try to express \(\mathcal C_v\) and especially \(\mathcal T_v\) in terms of the already-existing invariants \(M,N,W\) plus one new strengthened Wronskian, and see whether the direct \(q^{(7)}\) slice gives a nonzero leading term.
## User (2026-04-19 14:43:38)

## Assistant (2026-04-19 14:43:42)

I’m tracing the lifted-torsion quantities back into the draft’s existing one-pair invariants now. The key thing is to see whether \(\mathcal C_v\) and \(\mathcal T_v\) can be expressed through the already-controlled planar data plus one new strengthened Wronskian, rather than needing a completely new geometry.

_Thought for 4m 34s_

Yes. There is a real theorem-strength push here, and it is cleaner than the old minimal-core statement.

What we can attack **now** is the local \(v_5\neq 0\) patch by introducing the canonical lifted scalar
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad
\sigma_v(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)}.
\]

This is the right object because on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch the gauge \(v_7=0\) makes
\[
u_7=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
\frac{u_7}{c}=\sigma_v.
\]
So \((x,\sigma_v)\) is the planar shadow of the lifted space curve \(Q_v\).

The key fact is that \(\sigma_v\) is **not affine in \(x\)** on any connected interval where \(c\neq 0\) and \(v_5\neq 0\).

Indeed, if
\[
\sigma_v(h)=A\,x(h)+B,
\]
then multiplying by \(c(h)v_5(h)\) gives
\[
\Delta_7(h)=A\,v_5(h)^2+B\,c(h)v_5(h).
\]
The right-hand side is built only from the cubic/quintic layers \(c,v_5\), so it has no direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. But by the existing direct-septic result in the draft, \(\Delta_7\) has generically nonzero direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice on such an interval. Contradiction.

So there is a precise analogue of the existing “\(\rho_2\) is not affine in \(\rho_1\)” proposition:

> On any connected interval in \(\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\), the lifted scalar \(\sigma_v=\Delta_7/(c v_5)\) is not affine in the coordinate \(x=v_5/c\).

That is already useful.

Now define the derivative numerator for \(\sigma_v\):
\[
P_v(h):=c(h)v_5(h)\Delta_7'(h)-\Delta_7(h)\bigl(c(h)v_5(h)\bigr)'.
\]
Then
\[
\sigma_v'(h)=\frac{P_v(h)}{c(h)^2\,v_5(h)^2}.
\]
Together with
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2},
\qquad
M(h)=c(h)v_5'(h)-c'(h)v_5(h),
\]
this gives
\[
\frac{d\sigma_v}{dx}
=
\frac{\sigma_v'}{x'}
=
\frac{P_v}{M\,v_5^2}.
\]

Now form the curvature numerator of the lifted planar curve \(h\mapsto (x(h),\sigma_v(h))\):
\[
K_v(h):=x'(h)\sigma_v''(h)-\sigma_v'(h)x''(h).
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
K_v(h)
=
\frac{v_5(h)\bigl(M(h)P_v'(h)-M'(h)P_v(h)\bigr)-2M(h)P_v(h)v_5'(h)}
{c(h)^4\,v_5(h)^3}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
K_v(h)
=
\frac{M(h)^2}{c(h)^4}\,
\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{P_v(h)}{M(h)\,v_5(h)^2}\right).
\]
That is the exact lifted curvature bridge.

And now the same logic as in the planar \(\Gamma\)-curve applies:

If \(K_v\equiv 0\) on a connected interval where \(c\neq 0\), \(M\neq 0\), and \(v_5\neq 0\), then
\[
\frac{P_v}{M v_5^2}
\]
is constant, hence
\[
\frac{d\sigma_v}{dx}
\]
is constant, so \(\sigma_v\) is affine in \(x\), contradicting the non-affinity just proved.

So we get a genuine new theorem:

**Lifted planar non-affinity theorem on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch.**  
On every connected interval with
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
the curvature numerator \(K_v\) of the lifted planar curve
\[
h\longmapsto \left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right)
\]
is not identically zero.

That means the triple
\[
(1,\ x,\ \sigma_v)
\]
is an ECT triple on every subinterval where \(x'\neq 0\) and \(K_v\neq 0\). Equivalently, every affine line in the lifted \((x,\sigma_v)\)-plane meets such a subinterval in at most two points.

This has a concrete finite-core consequence:

On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, a defect-free **3-point** bad core would force three points of the lifted curve
\[
(x(h),\sigma_v(h))
\]
to be collinear. But on any lifted ECT subinterval that is impossible. So the 3-point branch is killed locally on each such patch.

That is a real advance. It does not finish the 4-point case, but it cleanly disposes of one whole branch.

For the **4-point** branch, the right next invariant is the local torsion / 4-function Wronskian
\[
T_v(h):=
W_h\!\left(1,\ \frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\ \frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\ \frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right).
\]
If \(T_v\neq 0\) on an interval, then the four functions
\[
1,\quad \frac{u_5}{c},\quad \frac{v_5}{c},\quad \frac{\Delta_7}{c v_5}
\]
form a local ECT system of order \(4\), and no affine plane can meet the lifted space curve \(Q_v\) in four points there. That would kill the 4-point defect-free branch locally.

What we can honestly say **right now** is weaker but still useful:

- \(T_v\) is the exact quantity that controls coplanar quadruples on the \(v_5\neq 0\) patch.
- If \(T_v\equiv 0\) and if \(1,u_5/c,v_5/c\) are linearly independent on the interval, then \(\sigma_v\) would be affine in \((u_5/c,v_5/c)\), i.e.
  \[
  \frac{\Delta_7}{c v_5}
  =A\frac{u_5}{c}+B\frac{v_5}{c}+C,
  \]
  hence
  \[
  \Delta_7
  =A\,u_5v_5+B\,v_5^2+C\,c\,v_5,
  \]
  whose right-hand side again has no direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. That would contradict the direct-septic nonvanishing result.

So the only extra hypothesis still missing for the full \(T_v\)-attack is a good theorem saying
\[
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
are locally linearly independent, or at least that any dependence among them is already excluded on the relevant generic region.

That is the next sharp algebraic subproblem.

So the real state after this push is:

- we now have a **new lifted planar curve**
  \[
  \left(\frac{v_5}{c},\frac{\Delta_7}{c v_5}\right)
  \]
  with an exact curvature bridge and a direct-septic non-affinity obstruction;
- this kills the defect-free **3-point** branch locally on \(v_5\neq 0\) lifted ECT intervals;
- the **4-point** branch is controlled by the torsion/Wronskian \(T_v\);
- the remaining missing ingredient is to control the lower triple
  \[
  1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c}
  \]
  well enough to force \(T_v\not\equiv 0\).

That is the strongest honest push I see from the current draft without overclaiming.

The next best thing to attack is exactly that last point: whether the existing first-order / quintic structure is already enough to rule out affine dependence of
\[
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
If it is, then the local 4-point branch on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch collapses too.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 14:49:37)

I’m checking the actual current notation around \(u_5/c\), \(v_5/c\), the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice, and the strengthened one-pair section. The point is to see whether the affine dependence of \(1,\ u_5/c,\ v_5/c\) can be ruled out from what the draft already proves, rather than inventing a new assumption.

_Thought for 5m 1s_

Yes. I think there is a real theorem here.

The right thing to prove next is:

\[
1,\quad \frac{u_5}{c},\quad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
are locally linearly independent on every connected interval where
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0.
\]

If that goes through, then the lifted order-\(7\) Wronskian
\[
T_v(h):=
W_h\!\left(
1,\ \frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\ \frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\ \frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}
\right)
\]
cannot vanish identically on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, because otherwise
\(\Delta_7/(cv_5)\) would be affine in \((u_5/c,v_5/c)\), which would force
\[
\Delta_7=A\,u_5v_5+B\,v_5^2+C\,c\,v_5
\]
and that has no direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice, contradicting the direct-septic result already in the draft.

So the real bottleneck is exactly the linear independence of
\[
1,\ u_5/c,\ v_5/c.
\]

I think this can be attacked from the existing quintic witness.

Here is the clean argument.

Assume on a connected interval \(J\) with \(c\neq 0\) and \(M\neq 0\) that there is a linear relation
\[
A+B\frac{u_5}{c}+C\frac{v_5}{c}\equiv 0.
\]
Multiplying by \(c\),
\[
A\,c+B\,u_5+C\,v_5\equiv 0.
\]

Now split into cases.

If \(B=0\), then
\[
A\,c+C\,v_5\equiv 0.
\]
Since \(c\neq 0\), this says
\[
\frac{v_5}{c}\equiv -\frac{A}{C}
\]
is constant. But
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
and \(M\neq 0\) on \(J\). Contradiction.

So necessarily \(B\neq 0\), and after renormalizing we get
\[
u_5=\alpha\,v_5+\beta\,c
\]
for constants \(\alpha,\beta\).

Now use the graded quintic witness from the draft.

The monomial
\[
\kappa(h)\,\eta_2(h)\,q^{(5)}(h)
\]
occurs with nonzero coefficient in the quintic trace witness. Since trace on the fixed sector is exactly twice the \(I\)-coefficient, this means that this monomial occurs nontrivially in \(u_5\).

By contrast:

- it cannot occur in \(c\), because \(c\) is the cubic coefficient and carries no quintic \(q^{(5)}\)-slice;
- and it should not occur in \(v_5\).

The reason for the second point is the same parity/slice mechanism already used in the proof of the quintic trace witness. On the graded slice
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}),
\]
the \(q^{(5)}\)-input enters only through the diagonal part of \(X_3\), while the \(\eta_2\)-slice of \(X_1\) is off-diagonal. In the explicit quintic fixed-sector formula
\[
u_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}
=
v(\gamma-\alpha)+\beta(u-w),
\qquad
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}
=
\gamma u-\alpha w,
\]
the \(I\)-component can see the off-diagonal/diagonal pairing, but the \(S\)-component needs diagonal entries \(u,w\) from the \(\eta_2\)-slice, and those are zero. So the tagged monomial contributes to \(u_5\), not to \(v_5\).

Therefore the identity
\[
u_5=\alpha v_5+\beta c
\]
cannot hold, because the left side has a nonzero \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\)-slice and the right side does not.

So we get the proposition:

\[
1,\quad \frac{u_5}{c},\quad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
are linearly independent on every connected interval where
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0.
\]

That is the key step.

Once you have that, the lifted order-\(7\) attack becomes clean.

On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, define
\[
a:=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
\sigma_v:=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
If
\[
T_v=W_h(1,a,x,\sigma_v)\equiv 0
\]
on a connected interval, then since these functions are real-analytic, vanishing of the Wronskian implies local linear dependence. By the independence of \(1,a,x\), we must have
\[
\sigma_v=A+Ba+Cx
\]
for constants \(A,B,C\). Multiplying by \(cv_5\),
\[
\Delta_7=A\,c\,v_5+B\,u_5v_5+C\,v_5^2.
\]
But the right-hand side is built entirely from cubic/quintic data and therefore carries no genuinely new direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice, while the draft already proves that the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice of \(\Delta_7\) is generically nonzero. Contradiction.

So on every connected interval with
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
the lifted order-\(7\) Wronskian
\[
T_v
=
W_h\!\left(
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},\ \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\right)
\]
is not identically zero.

That is a real advance, because it means the lifted space curve
\[
Q_v(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right)
\]
is not locally planar on any generic \(v_5\neq 0\) patch.

What this gives you immediately is a **local** exclusion of defect-free 4-point cores on any subinterval where \(T_v\) has fixed nonzero sign: there the four functions
\[
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},\ \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
form an ECT system of order \(4\), so no affine plane can meet \(Q_v\) in four points.

The one place I would still treat carefully is this sentence:

> “the tagged monomial contributes to \(u_5\), not to \(v_5\).”

I think it is right, and it follows the same slice/parity analysis already in the draft, but that is the one computation I would still explicitly write out before calling it fully done. Everything after that is clean.

So the best next theorem to isolate is:

**Proposition.** On any connected interval with \(c\neq 0\) and \(M\neq 0\), the functions \(1,u_5/c,v_5/c\) are linearly independent.

And then:

**Corollary.** On any connected interval with \(c\neq 0\), \(M\neq 0\), and \(v_5\neq 0\), the lifted Wronskian
\[
W_h\!\left(
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},\ \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\right)
\]
is not identically zero.

That is the right attack.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 14:55:46)

I’m checking the exact current quintic/septic formulas in the draft before I push further, because the next step hinges on whether the tagged quintic witness really separates \(u_5\) from \(v_5\), not just from \(c\).

_Thought for 3m 30s_

Yes. I think this part really does go through.

The clean theorem is:

\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
are linearly independent on every connected interval \(J\) where
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0.
\]

Here is the proof.

Assume there is a relation
\[
A+B\frac{u_5}{c}+C\frac{v_5}{c}\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Multiplying by \(c\),
\[
A\,c+B\,u_5+C\,v_5\equiv 0.
\]

If \(B=0\), then
\[
A\,c+C\,v_5\equiv 0.
\]
Since \(c\neq 0\), this makes \(v_5/c\) constant. But
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
and \(M\neq 0\) on \(J\). Contradiction.

So \(B\neq 0\), and after dividing by \(B\) we get
\[
u_5=\alpha\,v_5+\beta\,c
\]
for constants \(\alpha,\beta\).

Now isolate the graded quintic slice
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}).
\]

The draft already proves, via the quintic trace witness, that the monomial
\[
\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)}
\]
occurs in \(\operatorname{tr}J_5^{\pair}\) with nonzero coefficient. Since
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5 I+v_5 S
\]
and \(S\) is traceless, this means exactly that the same monomial occurs in \(u_5\) with nonzero coefficient.

So the only thing to check is that this monomial does **not** occur in either \(c\) or \(v_5\).

For \(c\), this is immediate: \(c\) is cubic, so it has no quintic \(q^{(5)}\)-slice.

For \(v_5\), the point is more delicate but still clean.

On the graded slice \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\), the witness proof already shows that only the two \(K_1\)-channels survive:
\[
X_0JX_4-X_4JX_0,
\qquad
X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3.
\]

For the first channel, the \((\eta_2,q^{(5)})\)-slice of \(X_4\) is off-diagonal by the whitening parity lemma, while \(X_0\) is diagonal. Therefore
\[
X_0JX_4-X_4JX_0
\]
is diagonal. But \(v_5\) is the coefficient of the fixed-sector basis element
\[
S=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\1&0\end{pmatrix},
\]
so a diagonal matrix contributes only to the \(I\)-component, not to the \(S\)-component. Hence this channel contributes nothing to \(v_5\) on the target slice.

For the second channel, the explicit fixed-sector formula in the draft is
\[
u_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=v(\gamma-\alpha)+\beta(u-w),
\qquad
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=\gamma u-\alpha w.
\]
On the target slice, the \(q^{(5)}\)-contribution to \(X_3\) is diagonal, so it contributes to \(\alpha,\gamma\) but not to \(\beta\). And the \(\eta_2\)-slice of \(X_1\) is off-diagonal, so it contributes to \(v\) but not to \(u,w\). Hence on the slice \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\),
\[
u=w=0,
\]
and therefore
\[
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=\gamma u-\alpha w=0.
\]

So the monomial \(\kappa\eta_2 q^{(5)}\) occurs in \(u_5\), but in neither \(v_5\) nor \(c\). That makes
\[
u_5=\alpha v_5+\beta c
\]
impossible. Contradiction.

So the proposition is proved.

That is the key step.

Now the lifted order-7 consequence is straightforward.

On a connected interval where
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
define
\[
a:=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
\sigma_v:=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Consider the lifted Wronskian
\[
T_v:=W_h(1,a,x,\sigma_v).
\]

If \(T_v\equiv 0\) on the interval, then because these functions are real-analytic, they are linearly dependent over constants. By the proposition just proved, \(1,a,x\) are already linearly independent, so necessarily
\[
\sigma_v=A+Ba+Cx
\]
for constants \(A,B,C\). Multiplying by \(c\,v_5\),
\[
\Delta_7=A\,c\,v_5+B\,u_5v_5+C\,v_5^2.
\]

But the right-hand side is built entirely out of the cubic/quintic data \(c,u_5,v_5\). So its direct linear \(q^{(7)}\)-slice is zero. The draft, however, already proves that on any interval with \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), the direct septic witness gives
\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv 0
\]
on the quintic-generic region. Contradiction.

Therefore
\[
W_h\!\left(
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},\ \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\right)\not\equiv 0
\]
on every connected interval with
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0.
\]

This is a real new theorem, not just packaging.

What it buys you is:

- on each subinterval where this Wronskian has fixed nonzero sign, the four functions
  \[
  1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},\ \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
  \]
  form an ECT system of order \(4\);

- equivalently, no affine plane can meet the lifted one-pair curve
  \[
  h\mapsto \left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right)
  \]
  in four points on such a subinterval;

- so the defect-free local 4-point bad-core branch is killed on every such patch.

The remaining weakness is only that this proves the lifted order-7 Wronskian is **not identically zero**, not yet that it has a definite sign or no zeros. So the next natural target is a zero-capture / first-zero theorem for this new lifted Wronskian, parallel to what the draft already does for the older planar geometry.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 15:01:55)

_Thought for 15s_

Yes, **probably in spirit, but not automatically as the draft currently stands**.

The right way to say it is:

The new lifted Wronskian
\[
T_v(h)=
W_h\!\left(
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},\ \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\right)
\]
is now in the same general position as the older planar quantities: we’ve shown it is **not identically zero** on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch. So to get the local 4-point exclusion, what remains is to control its zeros.

If you can prove a suitable zero-capture / first-zero theorem for \(T_v\), then yes: on each relevant connected patch, \(T_v\) would have fixed sign on subintervals, the 4-function system would be ECT there, and the local defect-free 4-point branch would be excluded.

But there are two caveats.

First, the existing zero-capture work in the draft is about the older geometric objects, especially the directional kernels across turning boundaries. It does **not** yet directly apply to this new lifted Wronskian \(T_v\). So this is not something you can simply cite “for free.”

Second, \(T_v\) lives one layer higher: it is a new order-7 lifted determinant, not one of the original planar Wronskians \(M,N,W\). So you would need either:

- a direct first-zero / compactness theorem for \(T_v\), or
- a reduction showing that any first zero of \(T_v\) forces one of the already-studied zero-capture bad configurations.

So my honest answer is:

- **conceptually yes** — this looks like it should reduce to the same kind of zero-capture machinery;
- **formally not yet** — you still need to build that bridge for \(T_v\).

The encouraging part is that the shape is now much better: the remaining issue is no longer “what is the right finite-core theorem?” It is a much more concrete question:

> can zeros of the lifted order-7 Wronskian \(T_v\) be controlled by the same first-contact / zero-capture framework already being developed for the paper’s planar geometry?

That is a believable conditional route.

The most likely next clean statement would be something like:

> On a connected \(v_5\neq 0\) patch in the generic region, any first zero of \(T_v\) forces a compact first-contact configuration for the lifted curve, and such a configuration is excluded by the same zero-capture mechanism used for the directional kernels.

That would make the dependence precise, instead of just hand-waving that “zero-capture should handle it.”

## Assistant (2026-04-19 15:03:12)

I’m pulling the exact section boundaries in the current TeX so I can give you insertions that fit the draft’s present structure rather than generic prose blocks.

_Thought for 3m 57s_

Replace the current block starting at

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Minimal bad core rigidity]
```

and ending at the end of

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress]
...
\end{remark}
```

with the following.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Defect-free quintic circuit reduction]
\label{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction}
Let
\[
F_{\core}(z)=\sum_{j=1}^k a_jF_{h_j}(z)+\mathcal I_{\ge 2}(z)
\]
be a normalized finite core, and assume that the multi-pair interaction germ
\(\mathcal I_{\ge 2}(z)\) contributes nothing to the cubic and quintic
coefficients. Write
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5(h)I+v_5(h)S,
\qquad
V(h):=\bigl(c(h),u_5(h),v_5(h)\bigr)\in\mathbf C^3,
\]
and on \(\{c\neq 0\}\) define
\[
\Xi(h):=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}\right)\in\mathbf C^2.
\]
If
\[
F_{\core}(z)\equiv 0,
\]
then
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,V(h_j)=0.
\]
Equivalently, with
\[
b_j:=a_j\,c(h_j),
\]
one has
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,\Xi(h_j)=0.
\]
Thus the points \(\Xi(h_j)\) are affinely dependent.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Taking the cubic coefficient in the identity
\[
F_{\core}(z)\equiv 0
\]
and using the hypothesis that \(\mathcal I_{\ge2}\) contributes nothing at
cubic order gives
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,c(h_j)=0.
\]
Taking the quintic fixed-sector coefficient and using the corresponding
defect-free hypothesis at order \(5\) gives
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_j)=0.
\]
Since
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_j)=u_5(h_j)I+v_5(h_j)S
\]
and \(I,S\) are linearly independent, this is equivalent to
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,u_5(h_j)=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,v_5(h_j)=0.
\]
Together these three identities are exactly
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,V(h_j)=0.
\]
If \(c(h_j)\neq 0\) for all \(j\), dividing the last two identities by
\(c(h_j)\) after setting \(b_j=a_jc(h_j)\) yields
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,\Xi(h_j)=0,
\]
which is the affine dependence statement.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Defect-free minimal quintic circuits have size at most four]
\label{cor:defect-free-minimal-quintic-circuits}
In the defect-free order-\(\le 5\) model of
Theorem~\ref{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction}, every minimal bad
core has size at most \(4\). More precisely:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(k=2\), then \(\Xi(h_1)=\Xi(h_2)\);
\item if \(k=3\), then the three points \(\Xi(h_1),\Xi(h_2),\Xi(h_3)\) are
collinear;
\item if \(k=4\), then the four points \(\Xi(h_1),\dots,\Xi(h_4)\) form an
affine circuit in \(\mathbf C^2\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction}, a minimal
defect-free bad core produces a minimal affine dependence among finitely many
points of the affine plane \(\mathbf C^2\). Such a minimal affine dependent
set has size at most \(4\). The cases \(k=2,3,4\) are the standard affine
configurations in dimension \(2\): coincidence, collinear triple, or
four-point affine circuit.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Lifted \(v_5\)-patch coordinates]
\label{def:lifted-v-patch-coordinates}
On a connected interval \(U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\), define
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
y(h):=\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
\sigma_v(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)}.
\]
The associated lifted planar and space curves are
\[
\Lambda_v(h):=\bigl(x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr)\in\mathbf C^2,
\qquad
Q_v(h):=\bigl(y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr)\in\mathbf C^3.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Defect-free lifted affine dependence on a \(v_5\)-patch]
\label{prop:defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch}
Let
\[
F_{\core}(z)=\sum_{j=1}^k a_jF_{h_j}(z)+\mathcal I_{\ge 2}(z)
\]
be a normalized finite core, and assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item all parameters \(h_j\) lie in one connected interval
\(U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\);
\item the multi-pair interaction germ \(\mathcal I_{\ge2}(z)\) contributes
nothing to the cubic, quintic, or septic coefficients.
\end{enumerate}
Then, after choosing on \(U\) the local septic gauge \(v_7=0\), the vanishing
identity
\[
F_{\core}(z)\equiv 0
\]
implies
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,y(h_j)=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,x(h_j)=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,\sigma_v(h_j)=0,
\]
where \(b_j:=a_jc(h_j)\). Equivalently, the points \(Q_v(h_j)\in\mathbf C^3\)
are affinely dependent.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The cubic and quintic identities are exactly those in
Theorem~\ref{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction}, so after setting
\(b_j=a_jc(h_j)\) we obtain
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,y(h_j)=0,
\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,x(h_j)=0.
\]
On the interval \(U\) we may choose the local septic gauge \(v_7=0\). Then
\[
u_7(h)=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{v_5(h)}=c(h)\,\sigma_v(h).
\]
Since the septic interaction is assumed absent, taking the septic fixed-sector
coefficient of \(F_{\core}\equiv 0\) yields
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k a_j\,u_7(h_j)=0.
\]
Substituting \(u_7(h_j)=c(h_j)\sigma_v(h_j)\) gives
\[
\sum_{j=1}^k b_j\,\sigma_v(h_j)=0.
\]
Hence the points \(Q_v(h_j)\) are affinely dependent.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Linear independence of \(1,u_5/c,v_5/c\)]
\label{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval on which
\[
c\neq 0,
\qquad
M\neq 0.
\]
Then the three functions
\[
1,
\qquad
\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
are linearly independent on \(J\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assume there exist constants \(A,B,C\in\mathbf C\), not all zero, such that
\[
A+B\frac{u_5}{c}+C\frac{v_5}{c}\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Multiplying by \(c\) gives
\[
A\,c+B\,u_5+C\,v_5\equiv 0.
\]

If \(B=0\), then
\[
A\,c+C\,v_5\equiv 0,
\]
so \(v_5/c\) is constant on \(J\). But
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
and \(M\neq 0\) on \(J\). This is impossible.

Hence \(B\neq 0\), and after renormalization we may write
\[
u_5=\alpha\,v_5+\beta\,c
\]
for constants \(\alpha,\beta\).

Now isolate the graded slice corresponding to
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}).
\]
By Lemmas~\ref{lem:quintic-trace-witness}
and~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}, the tagged monomial
\[
\kappa(h)\,\eta_2(h)\,q^{(5)}(h)
\]
occurs with nonzero coefficient in \(\operatorname{tr}J_5^{\pair}(h)\).
Since
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5(h)I+v_5(h)S
\]
and \(S\) is traceless, this means exactly that the same tagged monomial
occurs in the \(I\)-coefficient \(u_5(h)\).

It cannot occur in \(c(h)\), since \(c\) is cubic and carries no quintic
\(q^{(5)}\)-slice. It also cannot occur in \(v_5(h)\). Indeed, on the tagged
slice, the only surviving quintic \(K_1\)-transport channels are those already
isolated in Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}. For the channel
\[
X_0JX_4-X_4JX_0,
\]
Lemma~\ref{lem:whitening-parity} shows that the relevant
\((\eta_2,q^{(5)})\)-slice is diagonal, hence contributes only to the
\(I\)-component. For the commutator channel
\[
X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3,
\]
Proposition~\ref{prop:explicit-quintic-fixed-sector} gives
\[
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=\gamma u-\alpha w.
\]
On the tagged slice the \(\eta_2\)-input in \(X_1\) is purely off-diagonal, so
\(u=w=0\), while the \(q^{(5)}\)-input in \(X_3\) is diagonal. Hence
\[
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=0
\]
on that tagged slice.

Thus the monomial \(\kappa\eta_2 q^{(5)}\) occurs in \(u_5\) but in neither
\(v_5\) nor \(c\), contradicting
\[
u_5=\alpha\,v_5+\beta\,c.
\]
This proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Non-affinity of the lifted septic scalar]
\label{prop:sigmav-not-affine-in-x}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval contained in the quintic-generic region
and in
\[
\{h:c(h)\neq 0,\ v_5(h)\neq 0\}.
\]
Then there do not exist constants \(A,B\in\mathbf C\) such that
\[
\sigma_v(h)\equiv A\,x(h)+B
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\Delta_7(h)\not\equiv A\,v_5(h)^2+B\,c(h)v_5(h)
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
If
\[
\sigma_v(h)\equiv A\,x(h)+B,
\]
then multiplying by \(c(h)v_5(h)\) gives
\[
\Delta_7(h)\equiv A\,v_5(h)^2+B\,c(h)v_5(h).
\]
The right-hand side is built only from the cubic and quintic layers and
therefore has no direct septic \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. But by
Proposition~\ref{prop:direct-q7-total-delta7-nonzero}, the direct
\(q^{(7)}\)-slice of \(\Delta_7\) is generically nonzero on \(J\). This is a
contradiction.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Lifted derivative numerator and curvature numerator]
\label{def:lifted-vpatch-derivative-and-curvature}
On \(\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\), define
\[
P_v(h):=c(h)v_5(h)\Delta_7'(h)-\Delta_7(h)\bigl(c(h)v_5(h)\bigr)'.
\]
Then
\[
\sigma_v'(h)=\frac{P_v(h)}{c(h)^2\,v_5(h)^2}.
\]
Define also the affine curvature numerator of the lifted planar curve
\[
\Lambda_v(h)=\bigl(x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr)
\]
by
\[
K_v(h):=x'(h)\sigma_v''(h)-\sigma_v'(h)x''(h).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Curvature bridge for the lifted \(v_5\)-patch curve]
\label{prop:curvature-bridge-lifted-vpatch}
On \(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\),
\[
\frac{d\sigma_v}{dx}
=
\frac{P_v}{M\,v_5^2},
\]
and
\[
K_v(h)
=
\frac{M(h)^2}{c(h)^4}
\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{P_v(h)}{M(h)\,v_5(h)^2}\right).
\]
In particular, if \(K_v\equiv 0\) on a connected open interval \(J\subset
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\), then \(\sigma_v\) is affine in \(x\) on
\(J\), contradicting Proposition~\ref{prop:sigmav-not-affine-in-x}. Hence
\[
K_v\not\equiv 0
\]
on every such interval.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
x'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\qquad
\sigma_v'=\frac{P_v}{c^2v_5^2},
\]
we obtain
\[
\frac{d\sigma_v}{dx}
=
\frac{\sigma_v'}{x'}
=
\frac{P_v}{M\,v_5^2}.
\]
Differentiating with respect to \(h\) and multiplying by
\[
x'=\frac{M}{c^2}
\]
gives
\[
K_v
=
x'^2\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{d\sigma_v}{dx}\right)
=
\frac{M^2}{c^4}\,
\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{P_v}{M\,v_5^2}\right).
\]
If \(K_v\equiv 0\) on a connected interval with \(M\neq 0\), then
\[
\frac{P_v}{M\,v_5^2}
\]
is constant there, so \(d\sigma_v/dx\) is constant and \(\sigma_v\) is affine
in \(x\). This contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:sigmav-not-affine-in-x}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Local defect-free three-point exclusion on lifted ECT subintervals]
\label{cor:local-three-point-exclusion-lifted-vpatch}
Let \(J\subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\) be a connected interval on
which \(K_v\) has fixed nonzero sign. Then the triple
\[
1,\qquad x,\qquad \sigma_v
\]
is an ECT system on \(J\). In particular, no affine line meets the lifted
planar curve
\[
\Lambda_v(h)=\bigl(x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr)
\]
in three points of \(J\). Hence the defect-free three-point branch is excluded
on such a subinterval.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The Wronskian of \(1,x,\sigma_v\) is exactly \(K_v\). If \(K_v\) has fixed
nonzero sign on \(J\), the ECT criterion applies.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Lifted order-\(7\) Wronskian is not identically zero]
\label{cor:lifted-vpatch-wronskian-not-identically-zero}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval contained in the quintic-generic region
and in
\[
\{h:c(h)\neq 0,\ M(h)\neq 0,\ v_5(h)\neq 0\}.
\]
Then
\[
T_v(h):=
W_h\!\left(
1,\ \frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\ \frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\
\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)}
\right)
\]
is not identically zero on \(J\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\sigma_v:=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
If \(T_v\equiv 0\) on \(J\), then by analyticity the four functions
\[
1,\ y,\ x,\ \sigma_v
\]
are locally linearly dependent on \(J\), hence linearly dependent on all of
the connected interval \(J\). By
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}, the first
three are linearly independent, so there exist constants \(A,B,C\) such that
\[
\sigma_v=A+By+Cx.
\]
Multiplying by \(c\,v_5\) gives
\[
\Delta_7=A\,c\,v_5+B\,u_5v_5+C\,v_5^2.
\]
The right-hand side is built entirely from the cubic/quintic layers and
therefore carries no direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. This contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:direct-q7-total-delta7-nonzero}, which gives
\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv 0
\]
on \(J\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Local defect-free four-point exclusion on lifted ECT subintervals]
\label{cor:local-four-point-exclusion-lifted-vpatch}
Let \(J\subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\) be a connected interval on
which \(T_v\) has fixed nonzero sign. Then the quadruple
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
is an ECT system on \(J\). Equivalently, no affine plane meets the lifted
space curve
\[
Q_v(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)}\right)
\]
in four points of \(J\). Hence the defect-free four-point branch is excluded
on such a subinterval.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The Wronskian of the displayed quadruple is exactly \(T_v\). If \(T_v\) has
fixed nonzero sign on \(J\), the ECT criterion applies.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: interaction defects and zero-capture for the lifted order-\(7\) geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The results above isolate the correct local one-pair obstructions for the
finite-core endgame, but two ingredients are still open.

First, the actual multi-pair interaction germ
\[
\mathcal I_{\ge2}(z)
\]
has not yet been rewritten explicitly in the corrected finite-order model
through orders \(3,5,7\). Thus the genuine finite-core argument still needs
the defect terms
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)}.
\]

Second, Corollaries~\ref{cor:local-three-point-exclusion-lifted-vpatch}
and~\ref{cor:local-four-point-exclusion-lifted-vpatch} are local ECT
consequences on subintervals where the new lifted determinants \(K_v\) and
\(T_v\) keep fixed nonzero sign. To globalize these exclusions one still needs
a zero-capture / first-contact theorem for the lifted order-\(7\) geometry,
parallel to the turning-boundary zero-capture work elsewhere in the draft.

The same discussion has a parallel \(u_5\neq 0\) version obtained from the
local gauge \(u_7=0\), but the \(v_5\neq 0\) patch is the natural first
setting because \(x=v_5/c\) is already the distinguished ECT coordinate in
the one-pair planar geometry.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\]
play the analogous role for defect-free three-point and four-point branches on
\(v_5\neq 0\) patches; the missing global ingredient there is likewise a
zero-capture theorem.
```

And in the later “Current state of the argument” remark, I would add one sentence saying that the finite-core endgame is now reduced locally to interaction-defect extraction plus zero-capture for the lifted order-7 determinants \(K_v\) and \(T_v\).

I’m checking the actual TeX to see what made it in, what didn’t, and whether the new \(W=0\) material changes the best way to package the lifted order-7 story. Then I’ll give you a concrete verdict: incorporated, missing, and newly useful connections.

_Thought for 1m 32s_

I checked `proof_of_rh(112).tex` directly.

The short answer is:

1. **Yes, the core of the recent lifted order-7 work is now in the draft.**
2. **The new \(W=0\) work is genuinely useful, and it changes the way I would think about the remaining lifted zero-capture problem.**

Here is the clean status.

Your recent work is incorporated at the important places.

The new finite-core / lifted section is present and coherent:
- defect-free quintic circuit reduction at **8209**
- minimal quintic circuits \(\le 4\) at **8286**
- lifted \(v_5\)-patch coordinates at **8310**
- defect-free lifted affine dependence on a \(v_5\)-patch at **8326**
- linear independence of \(1,u_5/c,v_5/c\) at **8386**
- non-affinity of \(\sigma_v=\Delta_7/(cv_5)\) in \(x=v_5/c\) at **8481**
- lifted curvature bridge \(K_v\) at **8538**
- local 3-point exclusion on lifted ECT subintervals at **8601**
- lifted order-7 Wronskian \(T_v\not\equiv 0\) at **8622**
- local 4-point exclusion on lifted ECT subintervals at **8673**
- the correct WIP remark leaving interaction defects and lifted zero-capture open at **8696**

So the main mathematical spine of the recent attack is there.

The later status remarks also now reflect it correctly:
- the “Current geometric bottleneck” remark at **8724** now explicitly mentions the new lifted determinants \(K_v\) and \(T_v\)
- the “Current state of the argument” remark at **8767** now says the finite-core endgame is locally reduced to interaction-defect extraction plus zero-capture for \(K_v,T_v\)

That is good. It means the draft’s high-level status language has mostly caught up with the new local theory.

What I think is still missing, or at least not yet captured as explicitly as it could be:

The main missing “goodie” is a short formal consequence of Proposition `defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch` saying:

- defect-free 2-point cores on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch force **coincidence** on \(Q_v\),
- defect-free 3-point cores force a **collinear triple** on \(Q_v\),
- defect-free 4-point cores force a **coplanar quadruple** on \(Q_v\).

That is already implicit, but it is not stated as a standalone corollary. I would probably add it eventually, because it makes the geometric meaning of the lifted section much more transparent.

A second optional goodie that is still only implicit is the explicit 4-point determinant form:
\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & u_5/c & v_5/c & \Delta_7/(cv_5)
\end{pmatrix}=0
\]
for a defect-free four-point configuration on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, or its multiplied canonical version. You do not need it immediately, but it is a useful concrete restatement.

A third optional goodie is the parallel \(u_5\neq 0\) patch story. The current remark says it exists, which is fine. I do not think you need to write it out now unless you actually need symmetry later.

The main stale sentence I would flag is this one in the multi-pair section just before the two-pair decomposition:
at about **8029–8031**, the draft still says:

> “the behavior across boundaries of type \(W=0,\ M\neq 0\) remains the main unresolved global issue.”

That is now too stale. The later remarks are more accurate: the remaining issue is the **global propagation / recurrence problem**, not specifically the old raw \(W=0\) local obstruction. I would either delete that sentence or rewrite it to match the later “Current geometric bottleneck” remark.

Now to your second question: the new \(W=0\) story is useful, and there are indeed some real goodies there.

The strongest new \(W=0\) gains are these.

First, the draft now cleanly isolates the local \(W=0,\ M\neq 0\) geometry as an **affine inflection problem**, not as some mysterious hidden singularity. The remark at **6789** computes the cubic inflection coefficient and shows it is proportional to \(W'(h_b)\). That is a good normalization insight.

Second, the theorem at **7685** is very good:
**finite-order \(W=0\) boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth.**
That is stronger and cleaner than the older “maybe \(W'(h_b)=0\)” line of thought. It means the local \(W=0\) problem is no longer about creating new nearby secant branches. That is a major simplification.

Third, the remarks at **7634**, **7805**, and **7815** correctly reframe the whole \(W=0\) side:
the remaining issue is not local birth, but **global continuation / recurrence** of determinant-zero or tangent-slope data across multiple intervals.

Fourth, the draft now explicitly says that the exact identities for \(W\) and \(W'\) still show the residual obstruction is encoded by the **canonical order-7 package**, not a genuinely new order-9 primitive. That is extremely useful philosophically, because it supports the idea that the lifted \(K_v,T_v\) story really belongs to the same order-7 geometry rather than opening a new hierarchy.

Why this matters for the lifted order-7 section:

The new \(W=0\) story suggests a strong template for the next step.

For the old planar geometry, you now know:
- no open-interval \(W\equiv 0\),
- no local pair-pair birth at finite-order isolated \(W=0\) boundaries,
- so what remains is recurrence / re-entry.

For the new lifted geometry, you now have analogous local determinants \(K_v\) and \(T_v\), and you already proved:
- \(K_v\not\equiv 0\),
- \(T_v\not\equiv 0\),
- local ECT exclusion on sign-definite subintervals.

So the natural next conjectural theorem is the lifted analogue of the finite-order \(W=0\) sterility theorem:

> if \(K_v\) or \(T_v\) vanishes to finite order at an isolated boundary on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, then that boundary is locally sterile for the corresponding lifted 3-point or 4-point configuration.

That is where the new \(W=0\) goodies help. The proof style at **7685** uses local graph coordinates and divided differences. That same method looks potentially portable to the lifted graph
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad \sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5},
\]
at least for the \(K_v\) side, and maybe with a higher-order divided-difference / ECT argument for \(T_v\).

So the real value of the new \(W=0\) section is not just that it closes old audit remarks. It also gives you a **method template** for the lifted zero-capture work:
translate first zero / finite-order vanishing into a local graph model, then prove local sterility rather than trying to prove immediate global nonvanishing.

My overall verdict is:

- **Yes**, the recent lifted order-7 work is mostly incorporated.
- The only notable missing pieces are optional clarifying corollaries, not core math.
- **Yes**, the new \(W=0\) work is genuinely useful to the next stage.
- The biggest conceptual upgrade from the new \(W=0\) story is that it pushes the remaining problem away from local birth and toward **global recurrence / propagation**, and that same reframing is exactly what the lifted \(K_v,T_v\) section now wants.

The one concrete edit I would still make right now is to remove or rewrite the stale sentence near **8029**. Everything else is in pretty good shape.

If you want, the next thing I would do is try to formulate the lifted analogue of `finite-order W=0 boundaries are locally sterile`, first for \(K_v\), because that one looks closest to the existing divided-difference argument.

_Thought for 42s_

Yes. Here are the exact LaTeX edits I would make in `proof_of_rh(112).tex`.

First, **replace** the stale paragraph immediately after

```latex
\end{remark}
```

for `rem:two-normalizations-geometric-vs-projective` and immediately before

```latex
\begin{definition}[Two-pair decomposition]
```

Replace

```latex

on ECT intervals and across generic turning-point boundaries, but the behavior
across boundaries of type $W=0,\ M\neq 0$ remains the main unresolved global
```

with

```latex

on ECT intervals and across generic turning-point boundaries. The remaining

global propagation / recurrence problem for the determinant-zero and tangent
configurations that survive the local sterility results proved later in the
paper.
```

Second, **insert the following block immediately after** the proof of

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Defect-free lifted affine dependence on a $v_5$-patch]
\label{prop:defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch}
```

and **immediately before**

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Linear independence of $1,u_5/c,v_5/c$]
```

Use this:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Geometric meaning of defect-free lifted affine dependence]
\label{cor:geometric-meaning-defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch}. Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(k=2\), the two points \(Q_v(h_1)\) and \(Q_v(h_2)\) coincide;
\item if \(k=3\), the three points \(Q_v(h_1),Q_v(h_2),Q_v(h_3)\) are
collinear in \(\mathbf C^3\);
\item if \(k=4\), the four points \(Q_v(h_1),\dots,Q_v(h_4)\) are coplanar in
\(\mathbf C^3\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch}, the
points \(Q_v(h_j)\) are affinely dependent. For \(k=2\), affine dependence of
two points is exactly coincidence. For \(k=3\), affine dependence of three
points is exactly collinearity. For \(k=4\), affine dependence of four points
is exactly coplanarity.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Explicit four-point determinant form on a \(v_5\)-patch]
\label{cor:explicit-four-point-determinant-form-vpatch}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch} with
\(k=4\). Then the coplanarity of the four lifted points is equivalent to
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & y(h_1) & x(h_1) & \sigma_v(h_1)\\
1 & y(h_2) & x(h_2) & \sigma_v(h_2)\\
1 & y(h_3) & x(h_3) & \sigma_v(h_3)\\
1 & y(h_4) & x(h_4) & \sigma_v(h_4)
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & \dfrac{u_5(h_1)}{c(h_1)} & \dfrac{v_5(h_1)}{c(h_1)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_1)}{c(h_1)\,v_5(h_1)}\\[1.2ex]
1 & \dfrac{u_5(h_2)}{c(h_2)} & \dfrac{v_5(h_2)}{c(h_2)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_2)}{c(h_2)\,v_5(h_2)}\\[1.2ex]
1 & \dfrac{u_5(h_3)}{c(h_3)} & \dfrac{v_5(h_3)}{c(h_3)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_3)}{c(h_3)\,v_5(h_3)}\\[1.2ex]
1 & \dfrac{u_5(h_4)}{c(h_4)} & \dfrac{v_5(h_4)}{c(h_4)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_4)}{c(h_4)\,v_5(h_4)}
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
\]
Multiplying row \(j\) by \(v_5(h_j)\) gives the canonical determinant identity
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
v_5(h_1) & u_5(h_1) & \dfrac{v_5(h_1)^2}{c(h_1)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_1)}{c(h_1)}\\[1.2ex]
v_5(h_2) & u_5(h_2) & \dfrac{v_5(h_2)^2}{c(h_2)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_2)}{c(h_2)}\\[1.2ex]
v_5(h_3) & u_5(h_3) & \dfrac{v_5(h_3)^2}{c(h_3)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_3)}{c(h_3)}\\[1.2ex]
v_5(h_4) & u_5(h_4) & \dfrac{v_5(h_4)^2}{c(h_4)} &
\dfrac{\Delta_7(h_4)}{c(h_4)}
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
\]
Equivalently, multiplying instead row \(j\) by \(c(h_j)v_5(h_j)\) gives the
fully polynomial version
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c(h_1)v_5(h_1) & u_5(h_1)v_5(h_1) & v_5(h_1)^2 & \Delta_7(h_1)\\
c(h_2)v_5(h_2) & u_5(h_2)v_5(h_2) & v_5(h_2)^2 & \Delta_7(h_2)\\
c(h_3)v_5(h_3) & u_5(h_3)v_5(h_3) & v_5(h_3)^2 & \Delta_7(h_3)\\
c(h_4)v_5(h_4) & u_5(h_4)v_5(h_4) & v_5(h_4)^2 & \Delta_7(h_4)
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For \(k=4\), Corollary~\ref{cor:geometric-meaning-defect-free-lifted-affine-dependence-vpatch}
shows that the four lifted points
\[
Q_v(h_j)=\bigl(y(h_j),x(h_j),\sigma_v(h_j)\bigr)
\]
are coplanar. This is equivalent to the vanishing of the affine \(4\times4\)
determinant with first column \(1\). The displayed reformulations follow by
substituting the definitions of \(x,y,\sigma_v\) and multiplying rows by the
indicated nonzero factors.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Parallel \(u_5\)-patch version]
\label{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}
There is a completely parallel local story on any connected interval in
\(\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}\), obtained by choosing the local septic gauge
\(u_7=0\) instead of \(v_7=0\). Then one defines
\[
\tau_u(h):=-\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,u_5(h)},
\qquad
Q_u(h):=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\tau_u(h)\right),
\]
and the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions hold with \(Q_v\)
replaced by \(Q_u\). Since the present one-pair geometry already uses
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
as the distinguished ECT coordinate, the \(v_5\neq 0\) patch is the natural
first setting and will be used below.
\end{remark}
```

That captures the two geometric “goodies,” the explicit 4-point determinant form, and the parallel \(u_5\neq 0\) patch statement.

One small note: the determinant form you asked for,
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & u_5/c & v_5/c & \Delta_7/(cv_5)
\end{pmatrix}=0,
\]
is exactly the middle displayed determinant in the new corollary above.

I would not add anything else for this package right now. The new \(u_5\)-patch remark plus the existing WIP remark at the end of the lifted order-7 section is enough.

The crucial new facts in the paper are:

- open-interval \(W\equiv 0\) is gone,
- finite-order isolated \(W=0,\ M\neq 0\) boundaries are **locally sterile** for pair-pair birth,
- so the remaining old planar obstruction is no longer local creation but **global recurrence / re-entry**,
- and the exact \(W,W'\) identities show the residual obstruction is still encoded by the canonical order-7 package, not by some new order-9 object.

That is a very strong template for the lifted story.

So the cleanest route to attack now is:

## Attack the lifted zero-capture problem, starting with \(K_v\), not the interaction defects

Why this is the best route:

The paper itself now says the finite-core endgame is locally reduced to two tasks:
- extract the interaction defects,
- prove zero-capture for \(K_v,T_v\).

Of those two, the new \(W=0\) material gives you a **method** for the second one right now. It does not yet give you a method for the interaction-defect extraction.

And among \(K_v\) and \(T_v\), the cleanest next target is **\(K_v\)**.

Why \(K_v\) first:
- \(K_v\) is the curvature numerator of the lifted **planar** curve
  \[
  \Lambda_v(h)=\left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right),
  \]
  so it is structurally the closest analogue of the old \(W\)-story.
- You already proved \(K_v\not\equiv 0\), exactly as the older planar story first proved \(W\not\equiv 0\).
- The existing finite-order \(W=0\) sterility theorem is based on local graph coordinates and divided-difference / first-contact reasoning. That same architecture should port most naturally to \(\Lambda_v\).

So the next theorem to aim for is:

> **Finite-order \(K_v=0\) boundaries are locally sterile for lifted 3-point birth.**

Concretely: if \(K_v\) vanishes to finite order at an isolated boundary of a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, then no new nearby 3-point collinear configuration of the lifted curve \(\Lambda_v\) is born there.

That is the exact lifted analogue of the theorem you now have for finite-order \(W=0\) boundaries.

If you get that, then the 3-point defect-free finite-core branch is pushed into the same “not local birth, only global recurrence” box as the old pair-pair planar problem.

Then the next step is to do the same for \(T_v\):

> **Finite-order \(T_v=0\) boundaries are locally sterile for lifted 4-point coplanar birth.**

That one is harder, because \(T_v\) is a 4-function Wronskian / space-curve torsion-type quantity, so the divided-difference argument becomes one order higher. But once \(K_v\) is understood, the model is clear.

So my cleanest attack order is:

1. Prove finite-order local sterility for \(K_v=0\).  
   This is the nearest analogue of the new \(W=0\) theorem and should use the same graph/divided-difference method.

2. Then prove finite-order local sterility for \(T_v=0\).  
   This is the lifted 4-point version.

3. Then repackage the remaining lifted problem as a **global recurrence / re-entry** theorem for the lifted line/plane incidence data, exactly parallel to how the planar endgame is now phrased.

Only after that would I prioritize extracting the interaction defects \(E_{\ge2}^{(3)},E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)}\), unless you specifically want to clean the algebraic side first.

So the real answer is:

**The best next move is to port the new finite-order \(W=0\) local-sterility machinery to the lifted planar curve \(\Lambda_v\), starting with \(K_v\).** That is the shortest path to turning the new finite-core section from a local reduction into a real global theorem.

If you want, I’ll now try to formulate the exact statement and proof strategy for the lifted \(K_v\)-local-sterility theorem in the same style as the paper’s new finite-order \(W=0\) boundary theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 15:50:34)

I’m mapping the new \(K_v\) problem onto the paper’s existing finite-order \(W=0\) sterility argument. The main thing is to identify the exact lifted analogue of “pair-pair birth” and then see what first-contact/divided-difference object plays the same role.

_Thought for 59s_

Good. The \(K_v\) step looks close enough that I would treat it as the next real theorem, not just a heuristic.

Here is the exact statement I would push.

Let
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad
\sigma_v(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)},
\]
on a connected \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, and define the lifted collinearity determinant
\[
D_v(s,t,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & x(s) & \sigma_v(s)\\
1 & x(t) & \sigma_v(t)\\
1 & x(u) & \sigma_v(u)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the theorem to prove is:

\[
\textbf{Finite-order }K_v=0\textbf{ boundaries are locally sterile for lifted 3-point birth.}
\]

More explicitly:

Suppose \(h_b\) satisfies
\[
c(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad M(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad v_5(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad K_v(h_b)=0,
\]
and assume \(K_v\) has finite vanishing order \(r\ge 1\) at \(h_b\):
\[
K_v(h)=(h-h_b)^r \widetilde K_v(h),\qquad \widetilde K_v(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Then, after shrinking to a small neighborhood \(U\) of \(h_b\), if \(s<t<h_b\) lie in \(U\), the opposite-side function
\[
u\mapsto D_v(s,t,u)
\]
satisfies:
- if \(r\) is even, it has no zero for \(h_b<u\in U\);
- if \(r\) is odd, it has at most one zero for \(h_b<u\in U\).

And symmetrically with left/right exchanged. In particular, no finite-order isolated \(K_v=0\) boundary can support local birth of a lifted 3-point collinearity configuration.

That is the exact analogue of the new \(W=0\) sterility theorem already in the paper.

Why I think this should go through:

Use \(x=v_5/c\) as local coordinate. Since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2},
\]
the hypothesis \(M(h_b)\neq 0\) means \(x\) is a valid local parameter near \(h_b\). After translating and subtracting the tangent line, write
\[
\sigma_v=f(x),\qquad f(0)=f'(0)=0.
\]

Now
\[
K_v=x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v' x''
\]
is exactly the numerator of the second derivative with respect to \(x\):
\[
\frac{d^2\sigma_v}{dx^2}
=
\frac{K_v}{(x')^3}.
\]
Since
\[
x'(h_b)\neq 0,
\]
finite vanishing order of \(K_v\) in \(h\) is the same as finite vanishing order of \(f''\) in \(x\). So
\[
f''(x)=\lambda x^r+O(x^{r+1}),\qquad \lambda\neq 0.
\]

At that point the proof is literally the same divided-difference argument as the \(W\)-theorem:

for fixed same-side points \(x_1<x_2<0\), define
\[
\widehat D_v(x_1,x_2,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & x_1 & f(x_1)\\
1 & x_2 & f(x_2)\\
1 & u   & f(u)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat D_v(x_1,x_2,u)
=
(x_2-x_1)(u-x_1)(u-x_2)\,f[x_1,x_2,u],
\]
where \(f[x_1,x_2,u]\) is the second divided difference.

If \(r\) is even, then \(f''\) has fixed sign near \(0\), so by Hermite–Genocchi the opposite-side second divided difference has fixed sign. No opposite-side zero.

If \(r\) is odd, then \(f'''\) has fixed nonzero sign near \(0\), so the repeated-node divided difference
\[
\partial_u f[x_1,x_2,u]=f[x_1,x_2,u,u]
\]
has fixed sign, hence \(u\mapsto f[x_1,x_2,u]\) is strictly monotone. So there is at most one opposite-side zero.

That is all.

So I would say: the \(K_v\) sterility theorem is basically ready. It is not an invention anymore; it is a transport of an already-proved method to the lifted planar curve \((x,\sigma_v)\).

The real next difficulty is \(T_v\), not \(K_v\).

For \(T_v\), the exact analogue would be:

Let
\[
Q_v(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)}\right)
=(y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)).
\]
Define the lifted coplanarity determinant
\[
E_v(s,t,u,w):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & y(s) & x(s) & \sigma_v(s)\\
1 & y(t) & x(t) & \sigma_v(t)\\
1 & y(u) & x(u) & \sigma_v(u)\\
1 & y(w) & x(w) & \sigma_v(w)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then \(T_v\) is the local 4-function Wronskian controlling coplanarity. The natural theorem would be:

\[
\textbf{Finite-order }T_v=0\textbf{ boundaries are locally sterile for lifted 4-point birth.}
\]

But this one is not as automatic, because the \(W\)- and \(K_v\)-arguments are planar-graph arguments, while \(T_v\) is a space-curve / 4-function problem. You need the third divided difference or order-4 ECT machinery in a normalized chart.

The clean normalization is:

use \(x\) as local coordinate again, and write
\[
y=Y(x),\qquad \sigma_v=S(x).
\]
Then
\[
T_v=W_x(1,Y,x,S)
=
Y''S'''-Y'''S''.
\]
So \(T_v\) is the order-4 Wronskian of the four functions
\[
1,\ Y,\ x,\ S.
\]

That means the right higher analogue of the divided-difference proof is:

- affine-normalize at the boundary point so the osculating plane is removed,
- study the third divided difference of the residual graph data,
- use the finite vanishing order of \(T_v\) to control monotonicity/sign of that third divided difference across the boundary,
- conclude no local opposite-side coplanar quadruple birth.

So the clean attack order is:

1. Prove the \(K_v\) finite-order sterility theorem.  
   This should be a near-verbatim adaptation of the existing \(W\)-theorem.

2. Then formulate the \(T_v\) finite-order sterility theorem in the \(x\)-coordinate chart
   \[
   Q_v(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x)),
   \]
   with
   \[
   T_v=W_x(1,Y,x,S)=Y''S'''-Y'''S''.
   \]

3. Reduce the \(T_v\) theorem to a third divided-difference / order-4 ECT statement for the quadruple
   \[
   1,\ Y,\ x,\ S.
   \]

So the sharpest immediate continuation is:

**Do \(K_v\) now.** It is close enough to the already-proved \(W\)-theorem that it should be the next theorem you can reasonably close.

If you want, I’ll write out the exact proof of the \(K_v\)-local-sterility theorem in the paper’s style, step by step.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 15:55:28)

I’m pushing directly on the \(K_v\) theorem now rather than circling it. The goal is to turn the analogy with the new finite-order \(W=0\) sterility result into an actual argument, not just a template.

_Thought for 1m 7s_

Yes. I think the \(K_v\) theorem is basically ready.

Here is the clean statement and proof.

---

### Theorem
Let \(h_b\) lie in the quintic-generic region and satisfy
\[
c(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad M(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad v_5(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad K_v(h_b)=0.
\]
Assume \(K_v\) has finite vanishing order \(r\ge 1\) at \(h_b\):
\[
K_v(h)=(h-h_b)^r\,\widetilde K_v(h),
\qquad
\widetilde K_v(h_b)\neq 0.
\]

On a small connected \(v_5\neq 0\) patch around \(h_b\), define
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
\sigma_v(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)\,v_5(h)},
\]
and the lifted collinearity determinant
\[
D_v(s,t,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & x(s) & \sigma_v(s)\\
1 & x(t) & \sigma_v(t)\\
1 & x(u) & \sigma_v(u)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then, after shrinking to a sufficiently small neighborhood \(U\) of \(h_b\), the following holds.

If \(s<t<h_b\) lie in \(U\), then:

- if \(r\) is even, the function \(u\mapsto D_v(s,t,u)\) has **no zero** on the opposite side \(h_b<u\in U\);
- if \(r\) is odd, the function \(u\mapsto D_v(s,t,u)\) has **at most one zero** on the opposite side \(h_b<u\in U\).

The same conclusion holds with left and right exchanged.

In particular, no finite-order isolated zero of \(K_v\) can support local birth of a lifted 3-point collinearity configuration.

---

## Proof

Because
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2},
\]
the hypothesis \(M(h_b)\neq 0\) implies that \(x\) is a valid local coordinate near \(h_b\). After translating in the affine \((x,\sigma_v)\)-plane and subtracting the tangent line at \(h_b\), we may write the lifted planar curve as
\[
\sigma_v=f(x),
\qquad
f(0)=f'(0)=0,
\]
with \(x(h_b)=0\).

Now compute the relation between \(K_v\) and the second derivative of \(f\). Since
\[
\sigma_v'(h)=f'(x(h))\,x'(h),
\]
we have
\[
\sigma_v''(h)=f''(x(h))\,x'(h)^2+f'(x(h))\,x''(h).
\]
Therefore
\[
K_v(h)
=
x'(h)\sigma_v''(h)-\sigma_v'(h)x''(h)
=
f''(x(h))\,x'(h)^3.
\]
So
\[
f''(x(h))=\frac{K_v(h)}{x'(h)^3}.
\]

Since \(x'(h_b)\neq 0\), the finite vanishing order of \(K_v\) at \(h_b\) is the same as the finite vanishing order of \(f''\) at \(x=0\). Thus
\[
f''(x)=\lambda x^r+O(x^{r+1}),
\qquad
\lambda\neq 0.
\]

Now fix two same-side points
\[
x_1<x_2<0
\]
sufficiently close to \(0\), and define
\[
\widehat D_v(x_1,x_2,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1 & x_1 & f(x_1)\\
1 & x_2 & f(x_2)\\
1 & u   & f(u)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then the standard determinant factorization gives
\[
\widehat D_v(x_1,x_2,u)
=
(x_2-x_1)(u-x_1)(u-x_2)\,H_{x_1,x_2}(u),
\]
where
\[
H_{x_1,x_2}(u):=f[x_1,x_2,u]
\]
is the second divided difference of \(f\).

Now split by parity of \(r\).

### Case 1: \(r\) even

Then
\[
f''(x)=\lambda x^r+O(x^{r+1})
\]
has fixed sign near \(0\). By the Hermite–Genocchi formula for second divided differences, the quantity
\[
H_{x_1,x_2}(u)=f[x_1,x_2,u]
\]
has that same fixed sign for all sufficiently small \(u>0\). Hence
\[
\widehat D_v(x_1,x_2,u)\neq 0
\]
for all sufficiently small \(u>0\). So there is no opposite-side zero.

### Case 2: \(r\) odd

Then
\[
f'''(x)=\lambda r\,x^{r-1}+O(x^r)
\]
has fixed nonzero sign near \(0\), since \(r-1\) is even. Differentiate the second divided difference in the repeated node:
\[
\partial_u H_{x_1,x_2}(u)=f[x_1,x_2,u,u].
\]
By the Hermite–Genocchi formula for repeated-node divided differences,
\[
f[x_1,x_2,u,u]
\]
has the same fixed nonzero sign for all sufficiently small \(u>0\). Therefore the function
\[
u\longmapsto H_{x_1,x_2}(u)
\]
is strictly monotone on the opposite side, so it has at most one zero there. Hence \(\widehat D_v(x_1,x_2,u)\) has at most one opposite-side zero.

Finally, since
\[
D_v(s,t,u)=\widehat D_v(x(s),x(t),x(u)),
\]
the same zero-count conclusions hold for the original determinant \(D_v(s,t,u)\). The left/right exchanged statement is identical.

This proves the theorem.

---

## What this buys you

This is already enough to say:

- finite-order isolated \(K_v=0\) boundaries are **locally sterile** for lifted 3-point birth;
- so the remaining lifted 3-point issue is no longer local creation at a \(K_v\)-boundary;
- it is now, just as in the newer \(W=0\) story, a problem of **global recurrence / continuation** or possibly infinite-order flatness.

So the lifted 3-point branch is now in the same conceptual box as the old planar pair-pair branch after your new \(W=0\) theorem.

---

## The next theorem after this

Once this is inserted, the natural next target is the \(T_v\) analogue:

- define the coplanarity determinant
  \[
  E_v(s,t,u,w):=
  \det\!\begin{pmatrix}
  1 & y(s) & x(s) & \sigma_v(s)\\
  1 & y(t) & x(t) & \sigma_v(t)\\
  1 & y(u) & x(u) & \sigma_v(u)\\
  1 & y(w) & x(w) & \sigma_v(w)
  \end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  y=\frac{u_5}{c},
  \]
- and prove that finite-order isolated zeros of
  \[
  T_v=W_h(1,y,x,\sigma_v)
  \]
  are locally sterile for lifted 4-point coplanar birth.

That one is harder because it is a third divided-difference / order-4 ECT problem, but the \(K_v\) theorem above is the right first step.

If you want, I’ll now push the \(T_v\) theorem in the same way.
