_Thought for 4m 14s_

Yes. After checking the notes and the current logic, I think there is one theorem I can certify now, and one important caution.

The theorem is this:

On a compact good \(v_5\)-patch
\[
P\Subset \{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}.
\]

For exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits, define
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&x_3&S(x_3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)
=
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)\,S[x_1,x_2,x_3],
\]
where \(V_3\) is the Vandermonde and \(S[\cdot,\cdot,\cdot]\) is the second divided difference. As \(x_1,x_2,x_3\to x_*\),
\[
S[x_1,x_2,x_3]\longrightarrow \frac12 S''(x_*).
\]
Since \(K_v\) is \(S''\) up to a nowhere-zero factor in the \(x\)-coordinate, it follows that any shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit can accumulate only at
\[
K_v=0.
\]
Moreover, if \(P_0\Subset P\) is compact and disjoint from \(\{K_v=0\}\), then there is \(\rho_3>0\) such that no exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_3\). This is a real support-separation theorem for exact lifted triples. It is exactly the shrinking-\(3\)-point blow-up mechanism the other chat was circling around. turn15file10

Likewise, for exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits define
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_1)&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&Y(x_2)&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&Y(x_3)&x_3&S(x_3)\\
1&Y(x_4)&x_4&S(x_4)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then there is the standard factorization
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)
=
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\,\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4),
\]
and as all four nodes coalesce,
\[
\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\longrightarrow \frac1{12}W_x(1,Y,x,S)(x_*)
=\frac1{12}T_v(x_*).
\]
So any shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit can accumulate only at
\[
T_v=0.
\]
And if \(P_0\Subset P\) is compact and disjoint from \(\{T_v=0\}\), there is \(\rho_4>0\) such that no exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_4\). This is the exact bridge from shrinking support to the lifted determinant zero set. turn15file11

So the clean intermediate result is:

- shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\);
- shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\);
- and away from those zero sets, there is uniform small-diameter exclusion.

That part is rigorous now.

The important caution is this:

the full concentration-to-\(K_v=T_v=0\) theorem is **still not proved** from what we currently have. The reason is that the finite-order sterility theorems are still “no birth / at most one crossing branch” statements. They do **not** yet exclude the possibility of an already-existing close branch approaching an odd-order zero. So they are not strong enough by themselves to upgrade
\[
\text{shrinking exact circuits accumulate at }K_v=0\text{ or }T_v=0
\]
into
\[
\text{shrinking exact circuits accumulate only at }K_v=T_v=0.
\]

That is the key check I think needed to be said plainly. The other chat’s roadmap is directionally right, but the jump from “sterile” to “only mixed locus remains” is one theorem too fast. turn15file12

So the actual state is:

- the quantitative \(\widehat\Psi\)-theorem and defect-scale closeness for the two-point branch look solid; turn15file8
- the shrinking lifted \(3/4\)-point blow-up lemmas are now solid;
- but the bridge from those lemmas to full concentration at the mixed locus still needs a stronger **compact first-contact / no-preexisting-branch** theorem.

That is where I think I can help next, or alternatively on the other independent branch:

For the **two-point** regime, the sharpest next target is still the superlinear defect estimate
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
=o(|h_1-h_2|),
\]
or ideally \(O(|h_1-h_2|^2)\), on good patches. If that goes through, the two-point branch dies immediately by the quantitative \(\widehat\Psi\)-estimate and the lower Lipschitz bound from \(x=v_5/c\). The best concrete route there is still to check whether the corrected interaction defects vanish on the diagonal and are even in the separation variable \(s=h_2-h_1\), because that would force quadratic vanishing. turn15file5

So the strongest thing I can add right now is:

> We now have a rigorous shrinking-core concentration theorem into the zero sets of \(K_v\) and \(T_v\), and a rigorous uniform small-diameter exclusion theorem away from those zero sets. The missing bridge to “only the mixed locus remains” is not the blow-up step anymore; it is the stronger local theorem excluding preexisting close branches near non-mixed zeros.

That is the cleanest place to continue the attack.

_Thought for 20s_

Yes. Two things jump out.

First, I think the other chat’s **negative result** is genuinely useful and probably correct:

from the mixed normal form
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\ n>m,
\]
you get
\[
r=\ord K_v = m-2,
\qquad
s=\ord T_v = m+n-5,
\]
so
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,
\qquad s\ge 2r.
\]
And the explicit local model
\[
c(x)\equiv 1,\qquad v_5(x)=1+x,\qquad S(x)=x^m,\qquad Y(x)=x^n
\]
really does show that, at the level of **generic smooth lifted geometry**, there is no further parity obstruction beyond \(s\ge 2r\). So trying to kill the mixed locus by a generic parity theorem is a dead end. That is a good negative theorem to know. 

Second, that means the next useful attack is no longer “more generic local geometry.” It has to be **RH-specific jet structure**.

The cleanest place I can help is this:

At a mixed point, use \(x=v_5/c\) as coordinate and write
\[
S(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},\qquad
Y(x)=\frac{u_5}{c}.
\]
After normalizing away the affine span \(\operatorname{span}\{1,x,S\}\), the mixed normal form says
\[
S(x)=a_m x^m+O(x^{m+1}),
\qquad
Y(x)=b_n x^n+O(x^{n+1}),
\qquad n>m.
\]
The generic model shows \(m,n\) are flexible. So the only real hope is that the **actual formulas**
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
force non-generic relations among those jets.

That suggests two independent attacks I can help with immediately.

The first is to formalize the generic negative theorem cleanly, so you can stop spending time on parity at the abstract mixed-model level. The result is:

- generic lifted geometry only forces
  \[
  s\ge 2r;
  \]
- dangerous mixed patterns with \(s-r\) odd are genuinely realizable in smooth local models;
- therefore any exclusion of dangerous mixed patterns must come from special RH-specific identities, not from generic differential geometry. 

The second, and more valuable, is to start computing what an RH-specific mixed-point constraint would have to look like.

Concretely, I would now attack:

1. Expand \(x=v_5/c\) near a mixed point and invert locally, so everything is written in the \(x\)-coordinate.

2. Compute the first nontrivial jets of
   \[
   Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
   \]
   from the actual one-pair algebra already in the paper.

3. Compare those jets after modding out \(\operatorname{span}\{1,x,S\}\). The question is whether the first new coefficient of \(Y\) is forced to vanish to higher order than generic smooth geometry would allow, or whether the order gap
   \[
   n-m=s-2r+1
   \]
   is constrained by the RH-specific formulas.

That is the sharp frontier now.

So my recommendation is:

- treat the parity route as closed off by the negative theorem;
- keep \(s\ge 2r\) as the only generic consistency check;
- move the attack to **actual jet identities for \(u_5,c,\Delta_7,v_5\)** at mixed points.

I can also help on a separate branch: the **two-point branch** still looks killable if the corrected defects are superlinear in separation. That remains the cleanest non-mixed algebraic target.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:12:26)

I’m going to sharpen both branches separately: one into a clean theorem you can safely claim now, and one into a concrete algebraic test that could kill the two-point branch if it comes out right.

_Thought for 1m 50s_

Yes. I think both branches can be pushed a bit further now.

For the **lifted branch**, there is a safe intermediate theorem you can already treat as proved.

Let
\[
P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Then on \(P\), \(x\) is a valid local coordinate because
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
For the lifted planar curve \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), the exact collinearity determinant factors as Vandermonde times the second divided difference of \(S\), so any shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit can accumulate only at \(K_v=0\). For the lifted space curve \(Q_v=(Y,x,S)\), the exact coplanarity determinant factors as Vandermonde times a generalized divided difference converging to a constant multiple of
\[
W_x(1,Y,x,S)=T_v,
\]
so any shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit can accumulate only at \(T_v=0\). That part is rigorous already. turn18file6

From that you get the stronger uniform statement that is worth isolating explicitly:

> If \(P_0\Subset P\) is compact and disjoint from \(\{K_v=0\}\), then there is \(\rho_3>0\) such that no exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_3\).

> If \(P_0\Subset P\) is compact and disjoint from \(\{T_v=0\}\), then there is \(\rho_4>0\) such that no exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_4\).

This is just compactness plus the blow-up lemmas: if such small-diameter circuits existed away from the zero set, a shrinking subsequence would force a limit point with \(K_v=0\) or \(T_v=0\), contradiction. So you really do have **uniform small-diameter exclusion away from the relevant zero sets**. That is cleaner and safer than the full concentration-to-\(K_v=T_v=0\) claim. turn18file6

For the **two-point algebraic branch**, the cleanest next reduction is this:

If you can prove that the corrected two-pair defects satisfy, on a compact good patch,
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
=O(|h_1-h_2|^2),
\]
then the two-point branch dies immediately. Indeed, the quantitative defect-thickened coincidence theorem gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|,
\]
while on a good \(M\neq 0\) patch the coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, so
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim |h_1-h_2|.
\]
Combining them would force
\[
|h_1-h_2|\lesssim |h_1-h_2|^2,
\]
hence \(h_1=h_2\) for sufficiently small separation. So \(O(\delta^2)\) is more than enough, and even \(o(\delta)\) would already suffice. turn18file3

The best concrete check is exactly what you suggested: prove the raw corrected interaction defects are **even in the separation variable** and **vanish on the diagonal**.

Write midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1.
\]
Let the raw corrected interaction coefficients be
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(m,s),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}(m,s),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(m,s),
\]
before any asymmetric normalization by \(a_1\). Then the exact sufficient theorem is:

> If each of these functions is analytic in \(s\), even in \(s\), and vanishes at \(s=0\), then on compacta
> \[
> \mathcal E^{(3)}(m,s)=O(s^2),\qquad
> \mathcal E^{(5)}(m,s)=O(s^2),\qquad
> \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(m,s)=O(s^2).
> \]

The proof is immediate: analyticity plus evenness gives expansions in powers of \(s^2\), and diagonal vanishing removes the constant term.

So the two-point branch is now reduced to two exact checks:

First, **evenness**. This should come from the symmetry under swapping the two support labels:
\[
(h_1,h_2,a_1,a_2)\longleftrightarrow(h_2,h_1,a_2,a_1).
\]
At the level of the raw corrected interaction germ, that swap should leave the total object unchanged. In midpoint/separation variables, that is \(s\mapsto -s\). So the raw interaction coefficients ought to be even in \(s\), provided they are defined in a label-symmetric way.

Second, **diagonal vanishing**. This is the more substantive check. What you want is:
when \(h_1=h_2\), the exact two-pair corrected object collapses to the one-pair corrected object with total amplitude \(a_1+a_2\), so after subtracting the linear superposition of the two one-pair contributions, the interaction remainder is zero. If that is true at the level of the corrected cutoff-dependent object, then every extracted coefficient defect vanishes at \(s=0\).

So the sharpest algebraic target is now:

> Prove that the raw corrected two-pair interaction germ is symmetric under label swap and collapses to zero on the diagonal \(h_1=h_2\).

If that goes through, the quadratic defect estimate follows automatically, and the two-point branch is finished on good patches.

So my honest continuation is:

The lifted side already gives a correct intermediate theorem: shrinking exact lifted \(3\)- and \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into \(\{K_v=0\}\) and \(\{T_v=0\}\), with uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets.

The two-point side now has a very concrete algebraic target: show the corrected interaction defects are even in separation and vanish on the diagonal. If yes, you get \(O(|h_1-h_2|^2)\), and the two-point branch dies.

That is the cleanest place I can help next.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:16:22)

_Thought for 17s_

I think this is right, and it is a useful negative result.

The key point is exactly the one the other chat found: a blanket theorem of the form “near a finite-order nonmixed zero, there cannot be a preexisting close lifted branch” is false in generic lifted geometry. The examples
\[
\Lambda(x)=(x,x^3)
\]
for the \(3\)-point branch and
\[
Q(x)=(x^4,x,x^2)
\]
for the \(4\)-point branch show that finite-order nonmixed zeros can still carry exact shrinking branches. So the generic local sterility theorems only control **birth/crossing**, not existence of a single preexisting branch. That is a real obstruction, and it tells us to stop trying to prove the stronger false theorem. 

What survives, and is still worth formalizing, is weaker but real:

- shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits can only accumulate at \(K_v=0\);
- shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits can only accumulate at \(T_v=0\);
- near a finite-order zero, parity gives the local crossing picture: even order gives no crossing branch, odd order gives at most one crossing branch.

But that does **not** exclude a single preexisting branch approaching a nonmixed odd-order zero. So the roadmap should change accordingly. 

The cleanest next move is the one the other chat recommends at the end: pivot hard to the **superlinear defect estimate** for the two-point branch. That still looks like the cleanest potentially-killable regime:
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
=o(|h_1-h_2|),
\]
or ideally \(O(|h_1-h_2|^2)\), on good patches. If you get that, then the quantitative \(\widehat\Psi\)-coincidence theorem plus the bi-Lipschitz lower bound from
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
kills the whole two-point branch outright. 

The most concrete place I can help next is this exact algebraic reduction:

work with the **raw corrected interaction defects** in midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1,
\]
before any asymmetric normalization by \(a_1\). Then check two properties:

1. **Diagonal vanishing**
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(m,0)=0,\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}(m,0)=0,\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(m,0)=0.
\]

2. **Evenness in separation**
\[
\mathcal E^{(j)}(m,s)=\mathcal E^{(j)}(m,-s)
\]
for \(j=3,5,7\).

If both hold and the defects are analytic in \(s\), then automatically
\[
\mathcal E^{(j)}(m,s)=O(s^2),
\]
which is exactly the quadratic estimate you want.

So the next sharp theorem target is:

> prove that the raw corrected two-pair interaction germ is symmetric under swapping the two pair labels and collapses to zero on the diagonal \(h_1=h_2\).

If that goes through, the two-point branch is basically done on good patches.

One subtle thing to watch carefully: the normalized defects
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\quad E_{12}^{(5)},\quad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
\]
after dividing by \(a_1\) are **not** the right objects for the evenness check, because that normalization breaks the label symmetry. The symmetry should be checked on the raw unnormalized corrected interaction terms first, and only afterwards translated into bounds for the normalized defects. That is probably the single most important technical caution here.

So my recommendation is:

- accept the other chat’s negative result and stop chasing a generic no-preexisting-branch theorem;
- keep the shrinking-circuit concentration lemmas as the safe lifted theorem;
- move the main effort to the superlinear defect estimate for the two-point branch.

If you want, I can now help formulate the exact midpoint/separation lemmas you’d need to prove diagonal vanishing and evenness of the raw corrected interaction defects.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:17:24)

I’m checking the actual two-pair setup in the draft so I can see whether diagonal vanishing and evenness should already be built into the corrected interaction object, or whether the current normalization breaks the symmetry.

_Thought for 5m 2s_

Yes. I think there is a strong abstract theorem here, and if your current two-pair decomposition really means what it appears to mean, then the **two-point branch is basically dead** on good patches.

Here is the clean attack.

Write the raw two-pair decomposition as
\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}(z)
=
a_1F_{h_1}(z)+a_2F_{h_2}(z)+\mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z),
\]
where \(\mathcal I_{12}\) is the raw interaction germ.

Assume the three natural structural properties:

1. **quadratic in amplitudes**  
   \(\mathcal I_{12}\) is quadratic in \((a_1,a_2)\);

2. **pair symmetry**  
   \[
   \mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
   =
   \mathcal I_{12}(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1;z);
   \]

3. **diagonal collapse**  
   when the supports coincide,
   \[
   F_{(a_1,h;a_2,h)}(z)=(a_1+a_2)F_h(z),
   \]
   hence
   \[
   \mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h;a_2,h;z)=0.
   \]

If those hold, then the raw interaction has a factor
\[
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2.
\]

That is the key point.

Why?

Because quadraticity plus vanishing when one amplitude is zero implies
\[
\mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2;z)
\]
for some germ-valued function \(G\). Indeed, the \(a_1^2\) and \(a_2^2\) terms must vanish.

Then pair symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2;z)=G(h_2,h_1;z).
\]
So \(G\) is symmetric in the two support variables.

And diagonal collapse gives
\[
G(h,h;z)=0.
\]

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1.
\]
Symmetry says
\[
G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2;z\right)
=
G\!\left(m+\frac s2,m-\frac s2;z\right),
\]
so as a function of \(s\) it is even. Since it also vanishes at \(s=0\), it has no constant term and no linear term. Therefore
\[
G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2;z\right)=s^2 H(m,s;z)
\]
for some analytic \(H\).

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,a_2,h_1,h_2;z)
}
\]
for some analytic germ-valued \(\mathcal J\).

That is the whole theorem.

Once you have this, every raw coefficient defect extracted linearly from \(\mathcal I_{12}\) inherits the same factor. In particular, if
\[
\mathcal E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad
\mathcal E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}_{12}^{(7;1)}
\]
denote the **raw** cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects, then on compacta
\[
\mathcal E_{12}^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E_{12}^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}_{12}^{(7;1)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\]
where
\[
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]

If the normalized defects in your paper are
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=\frac{\mathcal E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=\frac{\mathcal E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1},\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=\frac{\overline{\mathcal E}_{12}^{(7;1)}}{a_1},
\]
then on any normalized family with \(|a_2|\) bounded,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]

So the total normalized defect
\[
\varepsilon
:=
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
\]
satisfies
\[
\boxed{\varepsilon=O(\delta^2).}
\]

Now combine this with the theorem you already have on good patches:
\[
\delta\lesssim \varepsilon.
\]
Then
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small \(\delta>0\).

So the conclusion is:

> **If the raw corrected two-pair interaction germ is quadratic in amplitudes, symmetric under pair swap, and collapses to zero on the diagonal, then the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches.**

That is a serious result. It is much stronger than merely “superlinear defects would be enough.” It gives a concrete structural criterion that forces the desired \(O(\delta^2)\).

Now the important caveat:

This is only as good as those three structural properties. Of them, the delicate one is not symmetry; it is **diagonal collapse in the corrected model**:
\[
F_{(a_1,h;a_2,h)}=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]

If that identity is literally true for the raw corrected finite-order object you are decomposing, then the argument above goes through.

So the next thing to check in the actual definitions is extremely specific:

1. Is \(\mathcal I_{12}\) really the **raw corrected interaction remainder** before any asymmetric normalization by \(a_1\)?
2. Does the corrected two-point object at \(h_1=h_2\) literally reduce to the one-point object with amplitude \(a_1+a_2\)?
3. Are the extracted cubic/quintic/septic defects linear projections of that raw germ?

If yes, then you get
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2),
\]
and the two-point branch is finished.

So I think the attack has now reduced to a very sharp verification problem, not an open-ended one:

> verify quadraticity, swap symmetry, and diagonal collapse for the raw corrected two-pair interaction germ.

If those are truly built into the present construction, then the two-point branch is already done.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:24:44)

I’m keeping the focus on the two-point branch and treating the other chat’s note as side-context. The clean question is whether the **raw corrected interaction remainder** really has the symmetry/diagonal-collapse structure that forces a quadratic \((h_1-h_2)^2\) factor.

_Thought for 24s_

Yes. The other chat’s new note is useful, but it mostly advances the lifted \(3/4\)-point side. For the **two-point** branch, the best continuation is still the same algebraic target:

prove that the **raw corrected two-pair interaction remainder** vanishes at least quadratically in the support separation.

Here is the cleanest way to attack it.

Let the raw corrected two-pair object be written as
\[
\mathcal F(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z),
\]
and let the one-pair corrected object be
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h;z).
\]
Define the raw interaction remainder by
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
:=
\mathcal F(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1;z)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2;z).
\]

The whole two-point branch dies if you can prove

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
}
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal J\) on compact good patches.

Because then every coefficient-level defect extracted linearly from \(\mathcal I\) satisfies
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
After the normalization used in the paper, this becomes
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2),
\]
assuming the normalized amplitudes stay bounded.

Then your quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
while on a compact good patch
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz because
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Hence
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
impossible for small \(\delta>0\). So the two-point branch is gone.

So the whole issue is: can we justify that factorization?

There is a very clean abstract theorem.

Assume the raw interaction remainder \(\mathcal I\) has these three properties:

1. **swap symmetry**
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1;z);
\]

2. **quadratic onset in amplitudes**
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2;z)=0;
\]

3. **diagonal collapse**
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h;z)=0.
\]

Then automatically
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J.
\]

Proof:

From quadratic onset in amplitudes,
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2;z)
\]
for some analytic \(G\).

Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2;z)=G(h_2,h_1;z),
\]
so \(G\) is symmetric in \(h_1,h_2\).

Diagonal collapse gives
\[
G(h,h;z)=0.
\]

Now go to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1.
\]
Symmetry means
\[
G\Bigl(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2;z\Bigr)
\]
is even in \(s\). Since it also vanishes at \(s=0\), it has no constant term. Hence
\[
G\Bigl(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2;z\Bigr)=s^2 H(m,s;z)
\]
for analytic \(H\). That is exactly the claimed factorization.

So the two-point attack reduces to checking those three structural properties for the **actual corrected object in the paper**.

Now, which of the three is delicate?

Quadratic onset is usually the easiest. If \(\mathcal I\) is defined as “full two-pair corrected object minus the two one-pair corrected objects,” then setting \(a_1=0\) or \(a_2=0\) collapses it to a one-pair object, so the remainder should vanish. That gives the \(a_1a_2\) factor.

Swap symmetry should also be built in, provided the raw corrected two-pair object is defined before any asymmetric normalization by \(a_1\). The unordered pair \(\{(a_1,h_1),(a_2,h_2)\}\) should not depend on the labeling. So this should give
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1).
\]

The truly important one is diagonal collapse:
\[
\mathcal F(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h).
\]

If that identity is literally true for the corrected object you are decomposing, then the two-point branch is basically finished.

So the sharp next move is not broad anymore. It is:

> Verify that the raw corrected two-pair object is label-symmetric, vanishes when one amplitude is zero, and collapses to the one-pair corrected object when \(h_1=h_2\).

That is a very concrete verification problem.

There is one subtle caution that matters a lot:

Do **not** check evenness on the already normalized defects
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
because dividing by \(a_1\) breaks the symmetry under exchanging the two labels. The evenness argument belongs at the level of the **raw unnormalized interaction remainder** \(\mathcal I\), or the raw coefficient defects \(\mathcal E^{(3)},\mathcal E^{(5)},\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}\). Only after obtaining the \(O(\delta^2)\) factor there should you pass to the normalized defects used in the paper.

So the clean theorem to aim for next is:

> **Quadratic interaction remainder theorem.**  
> On compact good patches, the raw corrected two-pair interaction remainder factors as
> \[
> \mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J.
> \]

And then the two-point bad-core branch is dead.

That is, in my view, the sharpest and most promising non-mixed algebraic target left.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:26:36)

I’m checking the exact two-pair decomposition in the current draft, because the whole quadratic-remainder attack turns on whether the raw interaction object is really symmetric and collapses on the diagonal before any \(a_1\)-normalization.

_Thought for 38s_

This update doesn’t change the two-point priority. If anything, it strengthens it: the other chat has now shown the nonmixed lifted route will not give a blanket local exclusion theorem, so the cleanest remaining way to kill the **two-point** branch is still the superlinear defect estimate. 

The strongest thing I can prove on that branch is an abstract factorization theorem. It reduces the whole question to checking three structural properties of the **raw corrected two-pair interaction remainder**.

Let the raw corrected two-pair object be
\[
\mathcal F(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z),
\]
and the corrected one-pair object be
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h;z).
\]
Define the raw interaction remainder by
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
:=
\mathcal F(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1;z)
-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2;z).
\]

Now assume the three natural structural properties:

\[
\text{(i) swap symmetry: }\;
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1;z),
\]
\[
\text{(ii) quadratic onset in amplitudes: }\;
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)=
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2;z)=0,
\]
\[
\text{(iii) diagonal collapse: }\;
\mathcal F(a_1,h;a_2,h;z)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h;z),
\]
equivalently
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h;z)=0.
\]

Then automatically
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
}
\]
for some analytic germ-valued \(\mathcal J\).

The proof is short. From quadratic onset in amplitudes, \(\mathcal I\) must be divisible by \(a_1a_2\), so
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2;z).
\]
Swap symmetry makes \(G\) symmetric in \((h_1,h_2)\). Diagonal collapse gives \(G(h,h;z)=0\). Passing to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1,
\]
symmetry says \(G(m-\tfrac s2,m+\tfrac s2;z)\) is even in \(s\), and diagonal collapse kills the constant term at \(s=0\). Therefore it is divisible by \(s^2\). That is exactly the factorization above.

This is the key attack result.

It immediately implies that every **raw** coefficient defect extracted linearly from \(\mathcal I\) satisfies
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the paper’s normalized defects are obtained by dividing by \(a_1\), then on normalized families with \(|a_2|\) bounded,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]

Once you have that, the two-point branch is gone on compact good patches. The reason is the quantitative \(\widehat\Psi\)-coincidence theorem together with the bi-Lipschitz lower bound from
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\qquad x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2},
\]
which already force
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|.
\]
If the right-hand side is \(O(\delta^2)\), then
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
impossible for sufficiently small \(\delta>0\). That is exactly the sort of superlinear estimate the other chat is recommending as the cleanest next theorem for the two-point regime. turn22file10

So the attack has reduced the two-point branch to a very sharp verification problem:

1. Is the **raw corrected** two-pair object label-symmetric before any \(a_1\)-normalization?
2. Does it literally collapse on the diagonal to the corrected one-pair object with total amplitude \(a_1+a_2\)?
3. Are the extracted cubic/quintic/septic defects linear projections of that raw interaction remainder?

If yes, then the quadratic estimate is essentially automatic, and the two-point branch is finished.

The one important caution is this: you should check symmetry and diagonal collapse on the **raw unnormalized interaction remainder**, not on the normalized defects
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\quad E_{12}^{(5)},\quad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
because dividing by \(a_1\) breaks the label symmetry. This is the technical point that matters most for the proof.

So my current verdict is:

- the other chat’s new note reinforces that the lifted nonmixed branch will not generically solve the two-point problem for you; 
- the best remaining route is exactly this structural factorization of the raw corrected interaction remainder;
- and if those three properties hold in the actual definitions, the two-point branch is basically done.

If you want, the next useful step is for me to help test those three properties against the paper’s current two-pair decomposition and corrected object definitions.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:29:28)

I’m checking the actual two-pair decomposition and corrected-object definitions in the current draft to see whether those three structural properties are really built in, or only morally intended. If they are explicit enough, the quadratic-remainder route may already be available.

_Thought for 59s_

Yes. I think the two-point branch can now be reduced to one very sharp structural theorem.

The clean theorem is this:

Let the **raw corrected two-pair object** be
\[
\mathcal F(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z),
\]
and the corrected one-pair object be
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h;z).
\]
Define the raw interaction remainder by
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
:=
\mathcal F(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1;z)
-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2;z).
\]

If the following three properties hold:

\[
\text{(A) swap symmetry: }\;
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1;z),
\]

\[
\text{(B) one-pair collapse: }\;
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)=
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2;z)=0,
\]

\[
\text{(C) diagonal collapse: }\;
\mathcal F(a_1,h;a_2,h;z)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h;z),
\]
equivalently
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h;z)=0,
\]

then automatically
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2;z)
}
\]
for some analytic germ-valued \(\mathcal J\).

That is the real attack result.

The proof is short.

From (B), \(\mathcal I\) vanishes when either amplitude is zero, so it must be divisible by \(a_1a_2\):
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2;z).
\]

From (A), \(G\) is symmetric:
\[
G(h_1,h_2;z)=G(h_2,h_1;z).
\]

From (C),
\[
G(h,h;z)=0.
\]

Now go to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1.
\]
Then
\[
G\Bigl(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2;z\Bigr)
\]
is an even analytic function of \(s\), and it vanishes at \(s=0\). Therefore it has no constant or linear term, so
\[
G\Bigl(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2;z\Bigr)=s^2H(m,s;z)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Rewriting in \((h_1,h_2)\) gives the factorization above.

That is already enough to kill the two-point branch on good patches, once you pass to the coefficient defects.

Indeed, let
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)},\qquad \mathcal E^{(5)},\qquad \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}
\]
be the **raw** cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects extracted linearly from \(\mathcal I\). Then on compacta,
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]

If the paper’s normalized defects are
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=\frac{\mathcal E^{(3)}}{a_1},\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=\frac{\mathcal E^{(5)}}{a_1},\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=\frac{\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}}{a_1},
\]
then for normalized families with \(|a_2|\) bounded,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]

Now combine this with the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem and the good-patch lower bound from
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
On a compact good patch,
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta,
\]
while the defect-thickened theorem gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
So
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small \(\delta>0\).

So the precise conclusion is:

> **If (A), (B), and (C) hold for the raw corrected two-pair remainder, then the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches.**

This is the cleanest non-mixed algebraic target left, and it matches the other chat’s conclusion that the superlinear defect estimate is now the best route for two-point cores. turn25file17

What remains is no longer open-ended. It is a concrete verification problem in the actual definitions:

1. Is the raw corrected two-pair object label-symmetric before any \(a_1\)-normalization?
2. Does setting one amplitude to zero collapse it to the corrected one-pair object?
3. Does setting \(h_1=h_2\) collapse it to the corrected one-pair object with total amplitude \(a_1+a_2\)?

If yes, the two-point branch is basically done.

The one caution that matters most: do **not** test evenness or diagonal vanishing on the already normalized defects \(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)},\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\), because dividing by \(a_1\) destroys the swap symmetry. The symmetry argument belongs at the level of the **raw unnormalized interaction remainder** \(\mathcal I\). After that, you pass to the normalized defects.

So the next sharp step is:

> check properties (A), (B), (C) directly against the paper’s current definition of the corrected two-pair object and the decomposition remainder.

If you want, I’ll now help turn those three checks into an explicit checklist against the draft’s notation, so you can test them one by one.

E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad

- (A) swap symmetry should hold if the raw corrected two-pair object is defined before any asymmetric \(a_1\)-normalization.
- (B) one-pair collapse should hold if setting one amplitude to zero literally collapses the two-pair object to the one-pair object.
- (C) diagonal collapse is the real hinge: when \(h_1=h_2\), does the corrected two-pair object literally become the corrected one-pair object with total amplitude \(a_1+a_2\)?

If yes, the two-point branch is basically done.

1. Identify the exact raw corrected two-pair object \(\mathcal F\) in the current draft.
2. Check it is symmetric under label swap.
3. Check \(\mathcal F(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2)\).
4. Check \(\mathcal F(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h)\).
5. Check the cubic/quintic/septic defects are linear projections of \(\mathcal I\).

## Assistant (2026-04-19 17:36:10)

I’m checking the actual definitions in the current TeX rather than reasoning abstractly. The key question is whether the draft already defines a raw, label-symmetric two-pair object before the \(a_1\)-normalization, and whether the diagonal \(h_1=h_2\) collapse is literally built into that object or only morally expected.

_Thought for 2m 1s_

I did the test against the current draft, and the conclusion is:

**the two-point quadratic-remainder route is not yet justified from the paper’s current definitions.** The draft is very close in spirit, but the exact structural properties you need are **not yet stated strongly enough**.

Here is the clean verdict.

The current draft gives you this and only this at the two-pair structural level:

\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}(z)
=
a_1F_{h_1}(z)+a_2F_{h_2}(z)+\mathcal I_{12}(z),
\]
with \(\mathcal I_{12}(z)\) described as “the pair-interaction germ, quadratic in the pair amplitudes.”

That is useful, but it is **not enough** to prove the factorization
\[
\mathcal I_{12}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J.
\]

Why not?

Because the three exact properties needed for that factorization are not yet present as theorem-level statements.

The three properties are:

\[
\text{(A) swap symmetry: }\;
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]

\[
\text{(B) one-pair collapse: }\;
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0,
\]

\[
\text{(C) diagonal collapse: }\;
\mathcal F(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h),
\]
equivalently
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]

Here is the status of each one in the current draft.

### 1. Swap symmetry: **plausible, but not stated**

The notation and the mathematics strongly suggest that a two-pair core should not depend on the ordering of the two labels. So morally
\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}=F_{(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1)}
\]
should be true, and then \(\mathcal I_{12}\) would inherit the same symmetry.

But the draft does **not** currently state this explicitly. The definition uses an ordered tuple notation \((a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\), and nowhere in the section is there a proposition saying the resulting quotient odd germ is invariant under swapping the two labels.

So:

- **likely true by intention**
- **not yet a theorem / not yet available for proof**

### 2. One-pair collapse when one amplitude is zero: **not available**

This is the crucial subtlety.

The draft says \(\mathcal I_{12}\) is “quadratic in the pair amplitudes,” but that alone is too weak. A general quadratic function of \((a_1,a_2)\) can contain terms like
\[
a_1^2,\qquad a_2^2,\qquad a_1a_2.
\]
To conclude divisibility by \(a_1a_2\), you need
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]

The current draft does **not** state this.

So right now, the paper does **not** justify the step
\[
\mathcal I_{12}=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2;z).
\]

That step is essential.

### 3. Diagonal collapse \(h_1=h_2\): **not available**

This is the real hinge.

To get the \((h_1-h_2)^2\) factor, you need the identity
\[
\mathcal F(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h),
\]
so that after subtracting the two one-pair pieces, the raw interaction remainder vanishes on the diagonal:
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]

The current draft does **not** state this anywhere.

Nothing in the present “Two-pair decomposition” definition or the later quantitative defect theorem records diagonal collapse for the **raw corrected two-pair object**.

So at the moment, the core quadratic-separation factor
\[
(h_1-h_2)^2
\]
is **not** justified from the paper.

### 4. The normalized defects are the wrong level to test symmetry

This matters a lot.

The paper’s theorem is written in terms of
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
after normalization by \(a_1\) and after passing to the quotient/septic representative bookkeeping.

That is **not** the right level to test evenness in the separation variable. Dividing by \(a_1\) destroys the visible symmetry under swapping the two pair labels. So even if the raw interaction remainder is symmetric/even in separation, the normalized defects will not show that directly.

So the test must happen one layer earlier:

- define the **raw unnormalized** cubic/quintic/septic interaction defects,
- prove those are symmetric under pair swap,
- prove they vanish when one amplitude is zero,
- prove they vanish on the diagonal \(h_1=h_2\),
- then conclude \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\),
- only then divide by \(a_1\).

That is the correct order.

## So where does this leave the attack?

It leaves it in a very sharp place.

The two-point branch is **not yet done** from the current draft.

But the missing step is now extremely specific.

What the draft needs is a structural theorem of this form:

> **Proposition (raw interaction structure).**  
> The raw corrected two-pair interaction remainder is:
> 1. invariant under swapping the two pair labels,
> 2. zero when either amplitude is zero,
> 3. zero on the diagonal \(h_1=h_2\).

From that, the factorization
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J
\]
is immediate, and then the two-point branch dies on good patches by the quantitative \(\widehat\Psi\)-coincidence theorem.

That still matches the other chat’s conclusion that the superlinear defect estimate is the cleanest remaining non-mixed algebraic target. 

## My honest bottom line

The test result is:

- **A (swap symmetry): not formally in the draft**
- **B (one-amplitude collapse): not formally in the draft**
- **C (diagonal collapse): not formally in the draft**
- therefore the quadratic defect estimate is **not yet derivable** from the current paper.

So the right next move is no longer a vague “keep attacking the two-point branch.” It is:

> add or prove the structural raw-interaction proposition above.

If you want, the next useful thing I can do is draft the exact proposition/remark sequence the paper would need so this route becomes rigorous.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 18:01:01)

I’m checking the current two-pair definitions in the draft itself so I can see whether this structural proposition can actually be proved from what’s already written, or whether it needs a new definition one layer earlier.

_Thought for 1m 51s_

Yes. I pushed the two-point branch to the point where the remaining issue is completely structural.

The clean theorem is this.

Let \(\mathfrak Q\) be the **raw corrected quotient-germ map** associated to the local construction, defined on a small class of atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\,\delta_{h_j},
\]
with values in odd quotient germs. Assume:

\[
\mathfrak Q(0)=0,
\]
\[
\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)
\quad\text{is analytic in the amplitudes and positions,}
\]
and the one-pair and two-pair raw objects are defined by
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\,\delta_h),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]

Now define the raw interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)
-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]

Then three facts are automatic:

First, **swap symmetry**:
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
because
\[
a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}=a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}.
\]

Second, **one-pair collapse**:
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0,
\]
because
\[
\mathfrak Q(0+a_2\delta_{h_2})-\mathfrak Q(0)-\mathfrak Q(a_2\delta_{h_2})=0.
\]

Third, **diagonal collapse**:
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0,
\]
because
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathfrak Q((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h).
\]

From these three facts, the quadratic-separation factorization follows.

Since \(\mathcal I\) is analytic and vanishes whenever \(a_1=0\) or \(a_2=0\), it is divisible by \(a_1a_2\):
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2).
\]

Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]

Diagonal collapse gives
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1.
\]
Then
\[
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right)
\]
is analytic, even in \(s\), and vanishes at \(s=0\). Therefore
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Rewriting in \((h_1,h_2)\),
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
}
\]
for analytic \(\mathcal J\).

That is the exact structural raw-interaction proposition.

Now apply any **linear coefficient-extraction map** \(L\) to \(\mathcal I\). In particular, let \(L_3,L_5,\bar L_7\) denote the raw cubic, quintic, and septic-quotient extraction maps. Then
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}:=L_3(\mathcal I),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}:=L_5(\mathcal I),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}:=\bar L_7(\mathcal I)
\]
satisfy
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|,
\]
uniformly on compact good patches.

If the normalized defects in the paper are obtained by dividing by \(a_1\), then on normalized families with \(|a_2|\) bounded,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]

Now combine this with the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem:
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On a compact good patch,
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz because
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Therefore
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
impossible for sufficiently small \(\delta>0\).

So the exact conclusion is:

> **If the raw corrected two-pair object is obtained by applying the same corrected quotient-germ map \(\mathfrak Q\) to the total atomic source \(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}\), then the raw interaction remainder is automatically quadratic both in amplitudes and in separation, and the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches.**

That is the real attack result.

The only place this can fail is if the current paper’s “two-pair object” is **not** actually defined as
\[
\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}),
\]
but instead is assembled in some more ad hoc way from separately corrected one-pair pieces. In that case, swap symmetry and diagonal collapse are no longer formal, and the theorem does not follow automatically.

So the whole two-point branch now reduces to one exact verification:

> Is the current corrected two-pair object in the draft truly the evaluation of the same raw corrected quotient-germ map on the combined two-atom source?

If yes, the two-point branch is basically done.

If not, then the draft needs a source-level reformulation of the corrected two-pair object before this argument can be used.

This matches the other chat’s conclusion that the superlinear-defect estimate is now the cleanest remaining non-mixed target, and in fact shows the estimate would be automatic from the right source-level definition. turn29file10

## Assistant (2026-04-19 18:05:52)

I’m checking the actual source-level definitions in the latest TeX now, because this is no longer a vague strategy question. The whole two-point branch turns on whether the paper’s two-pair object is really the same corrected quotient-germ map applied to the combined two-atom source.

_Thought for 58s_

I checked the current draft against the exact structural route, and the result is:

**we cannot yet prove the quadratic-separation factorization from the paper as written.**  
But we now know exactly what is missing.

What the draft currently has is only this source-level statement for two pairs:

\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}(z)
=
a_1F_{h_1}(z)+a_2F_{h_2}(z)+\mathcal I_{12}(z),
\]
where \(\mathcal I_{12}\) is said to be “quadratic in the pair amplitudes.”

That is not enough.

To get
\[
\mathcal I_{12}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J,
\]
you need three exact properties of the **raw** interaction remainder:

\[
\text{(A) swap symmetry},\qquad
\text{(B) one-pair collapse when one amplitude is zero},\qquad
\text{(C) diagonal collapse when }h_1=h_2.
\]

Here is the precise status from the current draft.

First, **swap symmetry** is not stated.  
The notation strongly suggests it should be true, but the draft nowhere says
\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}=F_{(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1)}
\]
or the corresponding symmetry for \(\mathcal I_{12}\).

Second, **one-pair collapse** is not stated.  
“Quadratic in the pair amplitudes” is ambiguous. Even a homogeneous quadratic term can contain
\[
a_1^2,\qquad a_2^2,\qquad a_1a_2.
\]
To conclude divisibility by \(a_1a_2\), you need
\[
\mathcal I_{12}(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
The draft does not say this.

Third, **diagonal collapse** is not stated.  
You need the exact identity
\[
F_{(a_1,h;a_2,h)}=F_{(a_1+a_2,h)},
\]
or equivalently
\[
\mathcal I_{12}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]
The draft does not currently assert this.

So the correct conclusion is:

> The two-point quadratic-defect route is **not yet available** from the draft’s current definitions.

That is the negative part.

Now the positive part.

If you add a single source-level definition/theorem, the two-point branch is basically done.

The right theorem is:

Let \(\mathfrak Q\) be the **raw corrected quotient-germ map** on finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
and define
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\delta_h),\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]
Then define the raw interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]

From this source-level definition, the three needed properties become formal:

1.
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1)
\]
because addition of atomic sources is commutative.

2.
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0
\]
because the two-pair source reduces to a one-pair source.

3.
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0
\]
because
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
\]

Then the standard midpoint/separation argument gives
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
for analytic \(\mathcal J\).

Once you have that, every raw coefficient defect extracted linearly from \(\mathcal I\) is \(a_1a_2O(\delta^2)\), hence after dividing by \(a_1\),
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]

Then the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem plus the good-patch lower bound from
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0
\]
forces
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
impossible for small \(\delta>0\). So the two-point branch dies on compact good patches.

So the attack result is:

**The current draft does not yet prove the needed structural proposition, but the whole two-point branch reduces to adding a source-level corrected quotient-germ map \(\mathfrak Q\) and defining the two-pair object as its evaluation on the combined two-atom source.**

That is now the exact next step.

If you want, the next thing I should do is formulate the minimal source-level proposition sequence needed so this route becomes rigorous in the paper.
## User (2026-04-19 18:07:47)

yes, please formulate the math rigorously

## Assistant (2026-04-19 18:08:10)

_Thought for 19s_

Yes. Here is the clean rigorous math formulation.

I would package it as a **conditional source-level theorem**. If you can make these assumptions true for the corrected quotient-germ map actually used in the paper, then the two-point branch is finished on good patches.

---

## 1. Source-level setup

Fix the corrected quotient-germ target through order \(7\); call it \(\mathcal G\). You do not need to identify \(\mathcal G\) further for this argument, only that:

- \(\mathcal G\) is a finite-dimensional complex vector space,
- the cubic, quintic, and septic quotient data are extracted by linear maps
  \[
  \Pi_3:\mathcal G\to \mathbf C,\qquad
  \Pi_5:\mathcal G\to \mathfrak f,\qquad
  \bar\Pi_7:\mathcal G\to \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
  \]

Now introduce a **raw corrected quotient-germ map**
\[
\mathfrak Q:\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)\in \mathcal G
\]
defined for small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j}.
\]

For the two-point branch, you only need it on one- and two-atom sources:
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\delta_h),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]

Define the **raw interaction remainder**
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]

---

## 2. Structural assumptions needed

The whole argument rests on these four assumptions.

### (S1) Analyticity
The map \((a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2)\mapsto \mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\) is analytic, and likewise \((a,h)\mapsto \mathcal F_1(a,h)\) is analytic.

### (S2) Source symmetry
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal F_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1).
\]

Equivalently, \(\mathfrak Q\) depends only on the atomic source
\[
a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2},
\]
not on the ordering of the two atoms.

### (S3) One-pair collapse
\[
\mathcal F_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]

### (S4) Diagonal collapse
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]

This is the crucial one.

---

## 3. Structural factorization theorem

Under (S1)–(S4), the raw interaction remainder has the exact factorization
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
}
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal J\) with values in \(\mathcal G\).

### Proof

From (S3), \(\mathcal I\) vanishes when \(a_1=0\) or \(a_2=0\). By analyticity, it is divisible by \(a_1a_2\):
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for some analytic \(G\) valued in \(\mathcal G\).

From (S2), \(G\) is symmetric:
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]

From (S4),
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1.
\]
Set
\[
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right).
\]
Symmetry gives
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=\widetilde G(m,-s),
\]
so \(\widetilde G\) is even in \(s\). Since \(G(h,h)=0\), we have
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Thus \(\widetilde G\) has no constant term in its Taylor expansion in \(s\), and since it is even, it has no linear term either. Therefore
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Returning to \((h_1,h_2)\) gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=(h_1-h_2)^2\,J(h_1,h_2)
\]
for analytic \(J\), hence the claimed factorization.

---

## 4. Raw coefficient defects are quadratic in separation

Define the **raw** cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects by linear projection:
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}:=\Pi_3(\mathcal I),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}:=\Pi_5(\mathcal I),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}:=\bar\Pi_7(\mathcal I).
\]

Since \(\Pi_3,\Pi_5,\bar\Pi_7\) are linear, the factorization immediately implies
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2)
}
\]
uniformly on compacta, where
\[
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]

More precisely: on every compact set \(K\) in the parameter space, there is a constant \(C_K\) such that
\[
|\mathcal E^{(3)}|+\|\mathcal E^{(5)}\|+\|\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}\|
\le
C_K\,|a_1a_2|\,\delta^2.
\]

---

## 5. Passing to the paper’s normalized defects

Suppose the paper defines normalized defects by dividing the raw defects by \(a_1\):
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=\frac{\mathcal E^{(3)}}{a_1},\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=\frac{\mathcal E^{(5)}}{a_1},\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=\frac{\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}}{a_1}.
\]

Then on any normalized family with \(|a_2|\) bounded,
\[
\boxed{
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
}
\]

This is the superlinear defect estimate you want, in fact quadratic.

---

## 6. Two-point exclusion theorem on good patches

Now assume you already have the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem for
\[
\widehat\Psi(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}\right),
\]
namely
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\le
C\Bigl(
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
\Bigr)
\]
on compact good patches.

Let
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be compact. Then
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
satisfies
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2},
\]
so \(x\) is bi-Lipschitz on \(J\). Therefore there is \(\eta_J>0\) such that
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\ge \eta_J |h_1-h_2|=\eta_J\delta.
\]

Combining this with the quadratic defect estimate gives
\[
\eta_J\delta
\le
C' \delta^2.
\]
Hence no nontrivial two-point bad core can exist on \(J\) once \(\delta\) is sufficiently small.

So the final theorem is:

> **Two-point exclusion theorem.**  
> Under (S1)–(S4), the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches.

---

## 7. What remains to verify in the actual paper

This is now the exact checklist.

You do **not** need to prove \(O(\delta^2)\) directly. You only need to verify that the current corrected construction actually comes from a source-level map \(\mathfrak Q\) with (S1)–(S4).

Concretely:

1. Is the current corrected two-pair object literally
   \[
   \mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})?
   \]

2. Is the current corrected one-pair object literally
   \[
   \mathfrak Q(a\delta_h)?
   \]

3. Does the current decomposition define the raw interaction remainder by subtraction of the two one-pair corrected objects?

If yes, then:

- source symmetry is automatic;
- one-pair collapse is automatic;
- diagonal collapse is automatic.

And the two-point branch is done.

---

## 8. The main caveat

This whole theorem is about the **raw unnormalized interaction remainder**.

It is **not** enough to look at the already normalized defects
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\quad E_{12}^{(5)},\quad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
because dividing by \(a_1\) breaks the symmetry under swapping the two labels. The symmetry argument belongs one level earlier, before normalization.

---

## Bottom line

The rigorous math is now:

- If the corrected construction is source-level and additive on coincident atoms, then the raw two-pair interaction remainder is automatically
  \[
  a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\times(\text{analytic}).
  \]
- Therefore the normalized defects are \(O(|h_1-h_2|^2)\).
- Therefore the two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.

So the next actual task is not more asymptotic analysis. It is to check whether the present paper’s corrected object is already defined source-level enough for (S2)–(S4) to be formal.

# Edit 1: add the source-level conditional theorem for the two-point branch

Insert this block **immediately after** the proof of

```latex
\begin{proposition}[No sublinear two-pair defects on good patches]
\label{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch}
```

and **immediately before**

```latex

```

Use this:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Conditional source-level quadratic interaction remainder]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
Assume there exists a finite-dimensional corrected quotient-germ target
\(\mathcal G\) and an analytic map
\[
\mathfrak Q:\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)\in\mathcal G
\]
defined on small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
such that the corrected one-pair and two-pair objects are given by
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\,\delta_h),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]
Define the raw interaction remainder by
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]
Then there exists an analytic germ-valued map \(\mathcal J\) such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The source-level definition of \(\mathcal F_2\) is symmetric in the two atoms,
so
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1).
\]
Also, if one amplitude is zero, then the two-pair source reduces to a one-pair
source, hence
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Thus \(\mathcal I\) is divisible by \(a_1a_2\), so
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued map \(G\).

Now if \(h_1=h_2=h\), then
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h),
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Passing to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\]
the symmetry of \(G\) means that
\[
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right)
\]
is an even analytic function of \(s\), and the diagonal vanishing gives
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Hence \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) is divisible by \(s^2\):
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Rewriting in \((h_1,h_2)\) gives the claimed
factorization.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Assume, in addition to
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder},
that the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are obtained from the
raw interaction remainder by linear coefficient-extraction maps
\[
\Pi_3:\mathcal G\to\mathbf C,
\qquad
\Pi_5:\mathcal G\to\mathfrak f,
\qquad
\bar\Pi_7:\mathcal G\to \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Then on compacta, the raw defects satisfy
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects in the present two-pair section are obtained by
dividing by \(a_1\), then on normalized families with \(|a_2|\) bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate from the factorization in
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and the linearity of the coefficient-extraction maps.

For the normalized defects, divide by \(a_1\) and use boundedness of \(|a_2|\)
on normalized families. Then
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On the other hand, on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the second coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero \(\delta\). Thus the
two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: source-level reduction for the two-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
The preceding proposition and corollary isolate the exact structural input
needed to finish the two-point branch. At present, the draft does not yet define
a source-level corrected quotient-germ map \(\mathfrak Q\) on finite atomic
sources, so the factorization
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J
\]
is not yet available formally from the present definitions. If such a
source-level reformulation is supplied, then the two-point bad-core branch is
finished on compact good patches.
\end{remark}
```

Then **replace** the current remark

```latex
\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
...
\end{remark}
```

with this updated version:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the correct algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the
strengthened invariant \(\widehat\Psi\). In particular, on good \(M\neq 0\)
patches, bad two-pair cores are forced into a defect-scale close regime by
Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch} shows that the
two-point branch is already excluded whenever the total defect is sublinear in
the pair separation.

The strongest remaining algebraic target for the two-point branch is now the
source-level structural reduction isolated in
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and Corollary~\ref{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}:
if the corrected two-pair object is defined source-level and collapses on
coincident atoms, then the normalized defects are automatically
\(O(|h_1-h_2|^2)\), and the two-point branch is excluded on good patches.

What remains beyond that is the genuine multi-pair interaction bookkeeping
through orders \(3,5,7\), together with the local lifted \(3/4\)-point analysis
for close-point branches on \(v_5\neq 0\) patches.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 2: add the safe shrinking-circuit concentration theorem on the lifted side

Insert this block **immediately after** the proof of

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Local defect-free four-point exclusion on lifted ECT subintervals]
\label{cor:local-four-point-exclusion-lifted-vpatch}
...
\end{corollary}
```

and **immediately before**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: interaction defects and zero-capture for the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
```

Use this:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Suppose there is a sequence of distinct triples
\[
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\in x(P),
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\to x_*,
\]
such that
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_{1,n}&S(x_{1,n})\\
1&x_{2,n}&S(x_{2,n})\\
1&x_{3,n}&S(x_{3,n})
\end{pmatrix}
=0
\qquad
\text{for every }n.
\]
Then
\[
K_v(x_*)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&x_3&S(x_3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
By the standard divided-difference factorization,
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)
=
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)\,S[x_1,x_2,x_3],
\]
where
\[
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=(x_2-x_1)(x_3-x_1)(x_3-x_2).
\]
Since the nodes are distinct, \(V_3(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n})\neq 0\), so
\[
S[x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}]=0.
\]
As \(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\to x_*\), the second divided difference converges
to
\[
\frac12 S''(x_*).
\]
Hence \(S''(x_*)=0\). Since on the \(x\)-patch the lifted curvature numerator
\(K_v\) is \(S''\) up to a nowhere-zero factor, it follows that \(K_v(x_*)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Uniform small-diameter exclusion away from \(K_v=0\)]
\label{cor:uniform-small-diameter-exclusion-away-from-Kv-zero}
Let \(P_0\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact and assume
\[
P_0\cap\{K_v=0\}=\varnothing.
\]
Then there exists \(\rho_3>0\) such that no exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit
contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_3\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Otherwise there would exist a sequence of exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits in
\(P_0\) with diameters tending to \(0\). By compactness, after passing to a
subsequence the three nodes would converge to some \(x_*\in x(P_0)\). This
contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Suppose there is a sequence of distinct quadruples
\[
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n}\in x(P),
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n}\to x_*,
\]
such that
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_{1,n})&x_{1,n}&S(x_{1,n})\\
1&Y(x_{2,n})&x_{2,n}&S(x_{2,n})\\
1&Y(x_{3,n})&x_{3,n}&S(x_{3,n})\\
1&Y(x_{4,n})&x_{4,n}&S(x_{4,n})
\end{pmatrix}
=0
\qquad
\text{for every }n.
\]
Then
\[
T_v(x_*)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_1)&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&Y(x_2)&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&Y(x_3)&x_3&S(x_3)\\
1&Y(x_4)&x_4&S(x_4)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Since \(\Delta_4\) is alternating in the four nodes, it is divisible by the
Vandermonde
\[
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(x_j-x_i).
\]
Write
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)
=
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\,\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4),
\]
where \(\mathcal D_4\) is symmetric and analytic. By the standard
Wronskian/divided-difference coalescence formula,
\[
\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\longrightarrow
\frac{1}{1!\,2!\,3!}\,W_x(1,Y,x,S)(x_*)
=
\frac1{12}T_v(x_*),
\]
as all four nodes tend to \(x_*\). Since \(V_4\neq 0\) for distinct nodes and
\(\Delta_4=0\) along the sequence, one has \(\mathcal D_4=0\) along the
sequence, so the limit forces \(T_v(x_*)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Uniform small-diameter exclusion away from \(T_v=0\)]
\label{cor:uniform-small-diameter-exclusion-away-from-Tv-zero}
Let \(P_0\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact and assume
\[
P_0\cap\{T_v=0\}=\varnothing.
\]
Then there exists \(\rho_4>0\) such that no exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit
contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_4\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Otherwise there would exist a sequence of exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits in
\(P_0\) with diameters tending to \(0\). By compactness, after passing to a
subsequence the four nodes would converge to some \(x_*\in x(P_0)\). This
contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Repeated-node tangent-contact determinants on a \(v_5\)-patch]
\label{def:repeated-node-tangent-contact-determinants-vpatch}
On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch with \(x=v_5/c\), \(Y=u_5/c\), and
\(S=\Delta_7/(c\,v_5)\), define
\[
H_3(a,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
0&1&S'(a)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix}
=
S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a),
\]
and
\[
H_4(a,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
0&Y'(a)&1&S'(a)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Thus \(H_3(a,u)=0\) means that \((u,S(u))\) lies on the tangent line to
\(\Lambda_v\) at \(a\), while \(H_4(a,u,v)=0\) means that \(Q_v(u)\) and
\(Q_v(v)\) lie in the tangent plane to \(Q_v\) at \(a\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Repeated-node limits of exact lifted determinants]
\label{prop:repeated-node-limits-of-exact-lifted-determinants}
For the exact lifted determinants
\[
\Delta_3(a,b,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
1&b&S(b)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and
\[
\Delta_4(a,b,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
1&Y(b)&b&S(b)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
\frac{\Delta_3(a,b,u)}{b-a}\longrightarrow H_3(a,u)
\qquad (b\to a),
\]
and
\[
\frac{\Delta_4(a,b,u,v)}{b-a}\longrightarrow H_4(a,u,v)
\qquad (b\to a).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Subtract the first row from the second row in each determinant and divide by
\(b-a\). The resulting second row is the first difference quotient of the
corresponding row entries, and the limit \(b\to a\) gives the derivative row.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Local classification of the lifted \(3\)-point branch near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero]
\label{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero}
Let \(x=0\) be an isolated finite-order zero of \(K_v\) on a good \(v_5\)-patch.
After affine normalization of \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), write
\[
S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1}),
\qquad
m=r+2\ge 3,
\]
where \(r=\ord_0 K_v\). Then the repeated-node tangent-contact equation
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
with \(a<0<u\) has the following local classification:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(r\) is even (equivalently \(m\) is even), there is no
opposite-side tangent-contact branch near \((a,u)=(0,0)\);
\item if \(r\) is odd (equivalently \(m\) is odd), there exists a unique
real-analytic opposite-side branch
\[
u=\Upsilon(a),
\qquad
a<0,\quad |a|\ll 1,
\]
with asymptotic expansion
\[
\Upsilon(a)=\lambda_m(-a)+O(a^2),
\]
where \(\lambda_m>1\) is the unique positive root of
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1).
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Set \(a=-\alpha\) with \(\alpha>0\), and write \(u=\lambda\alpha\) with
\(\lambda>0\). For the model germ \(S(x)=x^m\), the tangent-contact equation is
\[
H_3(-\alpha,\lambda\alpha)
=
\alpha^m
\begin{cases}
\lambda^m+m\lambda+(m-1),& m\ \text{even},\\[0.5ex]
\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1),& m\ \text{odd}.
\end{cases}
\]
If \(m\) is even, the displayed factor is strictly positive for every
\(\lambda>0\), so no opposite-side branch exists.

If \(m\) is odd, define
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1).
\]
Then
\[
P_m(1)=-2(m-1)<0,
\qquad
P_m(\lambda)\to+\infty\ \text{as }\lambda\to+\infty,
\]
and
\[
P_m'(\lambda)=m(\lambda^{m-1}-1)
\]
is negative on \((0,1)\) and positive on \((1,\infty)\). Therefore \(P_m\)
has a unique positive root \(\lambda_m>1\).

For the perturbed germ \(S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1})\), divide \(H_3(-\alpha,\lambda\alpha)\)
by \(\alpha^m\). The resulting equation is
\[
P_m(\lambda)+O(\alpha)=0.
\]
If \(m\) is even, positivity of the model factor persists for \(\alpha\) small,
so there is still no branch. If \(m\) is odd, the root \(\lambda_m\) is simple,
so the implicit function theorem yields a unique analytic branch
\[
\lambda=\lambda(\alpha)=\lambda_m+O(\alpha),
\]
equivalently
\[
u=\lambda_m(-a)+O(a^2).
\]
This proves the classification.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Nonmixed \(4\)-point zeros can carry preexisting close branches]
\label{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches}
A blanket local theorem excluding preexisting close \(4\)-point branches near
nonmixed finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros is false in generic lifted geometry.
Indeed, the model
\[
Q(x)=(x^4,x,x^2)
\]
satisfies
\[
K_v\neq 0,
\qquad
T_v\sim x,
\]
yet the exact coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for
exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ 2,\ 4,
\]
hence factors as
\[
\Delta_4=\pm V_4\,e_1,
\qquad
e_1(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)=x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4.
\]
Thus there are exact shrinking coplanar quadruples near \(0\), for example any
distinct
\[
x_1<x_2<x_3<0<x_4,
\qquad
x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4=0.
\]
So on the lifted \(4\)-point side, the strongest generic local statements are
the shrinking-core concentration into \(\{T_v=0\}\), the parity-based
birth/crossing classification, and the mixed-locus analysis, not a blanket
no-preexisting-branch theorem.
\end{remark}
```
