with

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: interaction defects and global branch control for the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The results above isolate the correct local one-pair obstructions for the
finite-core endgame, but two ingredients are still open.

First, the actual multi-pair interaction germ
\[
\mathcal I_{\ge2}(z)
\]
has not yet been rewritten explicitly in the corrected finite-order model
through orders \(3,5,7\). Thus the genuine finite-core argument still needs
the defect terms
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)}.
\]

Second, the lifted local analysis now gives exact shrinking-core concentration
into the zero sets of \(K_v\) and \(T_v\), together with uniform
small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets. What is still missing is
not a blanket zero-capture theorem near nonmixed zeros: generic lifted
geometry already allows preexisting close branches near certain odd-order
nonmixed zeros. The real missing input is a branch-continuation /
non-recurrence theorem for the nonmixed lifted branches, together with the
analysis of the mixed codimension-two locus
\[
K_v=T_v=0.
\]

The same discussion has a parallel \(u_5\neq 0\) version obtained from the
local gauge \(u_7=0\), but the \(v_5\neq 0\) patch is the natural first
setting because \(x=v_5/c\) is already the distinguished ECT coordinate in
the one-pair planar geometry.
\end{remark}
```

### Replace

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
...
\end{remark}
```

with

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now splits into three regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
K_v=0,
\]
and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node
tangent-contact branch is completely classified: even order gives no
opposite-side branch, while odd order gives exactly one opposite-side branch.

Second, exact shrinking lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros control local
birth/crossing by parity, but generic models show that a preexisting close
branch can still exist near certain odd-order nonmixed zeros. Thus the
nonmixed \(4\)-point side is not governed by a blanket local-exclusion
theorem.

Third, the mixed case
\[
K_v=T_v=0
\]
is genuinely different. After affine normalization with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate, the lifted space curve is led to a monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\]
and the leading \(4\)-point coplanarity determinant becomes the generalized
Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
\]
For some exponent patterns this model does admit opposite-side quadruples, so
the mixed locus remains the genuinely new codimension-two local obstruction.

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are:
the continuation / non-recurrence of the unique odd-order \(3\)-point branch,
the continuation / non-recurrence of nonmixed \(4\)-point branches, possible
infinite-order flatness, and the mixed codimension-two locus.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
In parallel, the finite-core endgame now splits into a global bridge and a
local lifted problem. On the global side, the two-pair algebra forces
quantitative near-coincidence of the strengthened invariant $\widehat\Psi$,
and on good $M\neq 0$ patches this forces bad two-pair cores into a
defect-scale close regime. On the local side, what remains is to extract the

\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)},
```

```latex
In parallel, the finite-core endgame now splits into a global bridge, a
two-point algebraic branch, and a lifted \(3/4\)-point branch. On the global
side, the two-pair algebra forces quantitative near-coincidence of the
strengthened invariant \(\widehat\Psi\), and on good \(M\neq 0\) patches this
forces bad two-pair cores into a defect-scale close regime. For the two-point
branch, the sharp remaining algebraic target is the source-level structural
reduction of the raw corrected interaction remainder: if the corrected
two-pair object is defined source-level and collapses on coincident atoms,
then the normalized defects are \(O(|h_1-h_2|^2)\) and the two-point branch
is excluded on compact good patches.

On the lifted side, exact shrinking \(3\)- and \(4\)-point circuits now
concentrate into the zero sets of \(K_v\) and \(T_v\), respectively, with
uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets. Near finite-order
isolated \(K_v\)-zeros, the \(3\)-point branch is completely classified by
parity. On the \(4\)-point side, finite-order sterility controls local
birth/crossing, but generic nonmixed odd-order zeros can still carry a
preexisting close branch. Thus the remaining lifted local issues are the
global continuation / non-recurrence of the nonmixed branches, possible
infinite-order flatness, and the mixed codimension-two locus
\[
K_v=T_v=0.
\]
```

---

## What I would **not** add yet

I would **not** add a theorem claiming that small-defect bad finite cores on good \(v_5\)-patches can survive only near \(K_v=T_v=0\). The current math is not strong enough for that, because generic nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can carry preexisting close branches.

I would also **not** add a theorem claiming the two-point branch is already finished unconditionally. That still needs the source-level corrected quotient-germ map \(\mathfrak Q\), or an equivalent direct proof of the raw structural properties.

These four edits capture the math you really have now, including the useful negative result, without overclaiming.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Nonmixed $4$-point zeros can carry preexisting close branches]
\label{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches}
At a nonmixed lifted point
\[
K_v(0)\neq 0,
\qquad
T_v(0)=0,
\]
the local model may be affine-normalized to
\[
Q_v(x)=(x^n,x,x^2),
\qquad
n\ge 3,
\]
so that
\[
\ord_0 T_v=n-3.
\]

The exact four-point coplanarity determinant of this model is the generalized
Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ 2,\ n,
\]
hence factors as
\[
\Delta_4^{\mathrm{model}}
=
\pm V_4\,h_{n-3},
\]
where \(V_4\) is the ordinary Vandermonde and \(h_{n-3}\) is the complete
homogeneous symmetric polynomial of degree \(n-3\).

In particular, the case \(n=4\) gives
\[
\Delta_4^{\mathrm{model}}
=
\pm V_4\,e_1,
\qquad
e_1(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)=x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4.
\]
Thus there are exact shrinking coplanar quadruples near \(0\), for example any
distinct
\[
x_1<x_2<x_3<0<x_4,
\qquad
x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4=0.
\]

So on the lifted \(4\)-point side, the strongest generic local statements are:
shrinking-core concentration into \(\{T_v=0\}\), parity-based
birth/crossing control, and the mixed-locus analysis. A blanket
no-preexisting-branch theorem near nonmixed finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros is
false in generic lifted geometry.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 2: insert the mixed-order bookkeeping / no-generic-parity-obstruction remark

### Insert **immediately after** the remark above and **before**
```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: interaction defects and global branch control for the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
```

### Insert this

```latex
\begin{remark}[Mixed order bookkeeping and lack of generic parity obstruction]
\label{rem:mixed-order-bookkeeping-no-generic-parity-obstruction}
At a mixed lifted point
\[
K_v(0)=0,
\qquad
T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current affine-normalized model is
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,
\qquad
n>m.
\]
If
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,
\qquad
s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then the model exponents satisfy
\[
r=m-2,
\qquad
s=m+n-5,
\]
hence
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]

The immediately dangerous parity sector in the mixed model is
\[
n\ \text{even}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
s-r\ \text{odd}.
\]

However, generic smooth lifted geometry imposes no further parity restriction.
Indeed, the smooth local model
\[
c(x)\equiv 1,
\qquad
v_5(x)=1+x,
\qquad
S(x)=x^m,
\qquad
Y(x)=x^n
\]
lies on a good \(v_5\)-patch and realizes arbitrary integers
\[
m\ge 3,
\qquad
n>m,
\]
hence arbitrary order pairs
\[
r\ge 1,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]

Thus any exclusion of dangerous mixed patterns must come from RH-specific jet
identities or from additional algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad
four-point cores, not from generic lifted differential geometry alone.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Next algebraic target on the four-point branch]

The lifted four-point geometry shows that generic coplanarity alone is too

local lifted coplanarity branch, beyond the vanishing of the lifted four-point
determinant?
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry now splits more sharply than a blanket
zero-capture problem.

First, Propositions~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}
and~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero} show
that shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v=0,
\]
respectively, and give uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero
sets.

Second, Proposition~\ref{prop:repeated-node-limits-of-exact-lifted-determinants}
identifies the one-pair collapse limits as tangent-line and tangent-plane
contact determinants for the lifted curves \(\Lambda_v\) and \(Q_v\).

Third, the nonmixed and mixed four-point local pictures are genuinely
different. On the nonmixed side, generic odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can carry a

bookkeeping is
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r,
\]
and there is no generic parity obstruction beyond this order inequality.

Thus the missing global ingredient is no longer a single blanket first-contact
lemma. It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of the multi-pair interaction defects
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)};
\]
\item extra algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad four-point cores,
beyond generic coplanarity of the lifted points;
\item and, on the mixed side, RH-specific jet restrictions excluding the
dangerous exponent patterns.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
```

```latex
The lifted local obstruction now splits into three regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[

and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node tangent-contact

\[

\]

\qquad
```

---

Yes — it helps a lot, but mostly by clarifying **what kind of extra algebraic condition to look for** on the (4)-point branch.

For the (2)-point branch, I agree with the other chat almost completely: if you can promote the corrected construction to a **source-level quotient-germ map** and prove raw interaction symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse, then the quadratic separation factorization
[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J
]
is basically formal, and the two-point branch dies on good patches by the quantitative (\widehat\Psi)-coincidence theorem plus the (x=v_5/c) bi-Lipschitz lower bound. That is the cleanest non-mixed algebraic target left for two points. 

What is more interesting for the **(4)-point** attack is the pattern behind it.

The note suggests a general principle:

> do not look for the missing condition at the level of already-normalized defects; look for it at the level of the **raw source-level corrected object**.

That is exactly the right lesson for (4)-point cores too. A true bad (4)-point core should not be modeled merely as an arbitrary coplanar quadruple on the lifted curve (Q_v). It should come from a raw corrected (4)-atom source, and that should impose extra algebraic structure beyond coplanarity — just as the (2)-point branch should impose more than mere coincidence of (\widehat\Psi). 

So I think the right (4)-point analogue is this.

Let (\mathfrak Q) be the raw corrected quotient-germ map on finite atomic sources, and define the raw (4)-point corrected object
[
\mathcal F_4(a_1,h_1;\dots;a_4,h_4):=\mathfrak Q!\left(\sum_{j=1}^4 a_j\delta_{h_j}\right).
]
Then define the **pure (4)-body interaction remainder** by inclusion–exclusion, subtracting all (1)-, (2)-, and (3)-atom contributions. If that source-level object exists, then three kinds of conditions should become formal:

First, full **label symmetry** under permuting the four atoms.

Second, **collapse on partial diagonals**: whenever two atoms coincide, the (4)-atom source reduces to a (3)-atom source, so the pure (4)-body remainder should vanish.

Third, **vanishing when any amplitude is zero**.

Those are the exact (4)-point analogues of the (2)-point structural conditions in the note. And if they hold, then the pure (4)-body remainder should inherit very strong divisibility:

* by (\prod_j a_j) from amplitude collapse,
* and by every pair difference (h_i-h_j) from partial-diagonal collapse.

Because the object is symmetric, vanishing on each partial diagonal should force divisibility by the **discriminant**
[
\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2
]
rather than just a single linear factor. That is the (4)-point analogue of the midpoint/separation evenness argument in the (2)-point note. I would not claim this as proved yet, but structurally it is exactly the kind of theorem to attack.

And this would be a big deal, because it would give the extra algebraic condition you asked for:

> a true bad (4)-point core is not merely coplanar on (Q_v); it lies on a coplanarity branch along which a much more singular source-level (4)-body remainder vanishes.

That is exactly the kind of restriction that a generic local branch sheet like the nonmixed odd-order model
[
Q(x)=(x^4,x,x^2)
]
will probably **not** satisfy automatically.

So my answer is:

* **Yes**, this helps the (4)-point attack conceptually.
* It does **not** solve the (4)-point branch directly.
* But it points to the right missing theorem: a **source-level (4)-body interaction remainder theorem**.

That is now the cleanest way I see to derive an extra algebraic condition beyond coplanarity.

The exact next attack I would make is:

1. define the raw pure (4)-body interaction remainder by inclusion–exclusion from the source-level corrected map;
2. prove it is symmetric, vanishes when any amplitude is zero, and vanishes on every partial diagonal (h_i=h_j);
3. deduce discriminant-type divisibility;
4. then test whether the unique nonmixed odd-order branch sheet and the mixed normal form can satisfy the resulting higher-order vanishing.

That is the strongest way this note helps the (4)-pair side.

I’m keeping the attack entirely on the 4-point side now. The question is no longer “is there a coplanar branch?” — we already know there can be — but “what extra algebraic condition does a true bad 4-point core impose beyond coplanarity, and can the local branch satisfy it?”

Yes. I pushed on exactly that question, and the clean conclusion is:

**at the current defect-free lifted level, there is no extra algebraic condition beyond coplanarity.**

That is the real (4)-point attack result.

On a good (v_5)-patch, the lifted coordinates are
[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5},
\qquad
Q_v=(y,x,\sigma_v).
]
The current defect-free order-(\le 7) theorem says that a bad (4)-point core becomes an affine dependence of the four lifted points (Q_v(h_j)), i.e. coplanarity in (\mathbf C^3). In the current formulation, there is no second independent scalar equation left over after passing to (Q_v); the bad-core condition has already been compressed into that affine circuit statement.

More concretely, if
[
\sum_{j=1}^4 b_j=0,\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^4 b_j,y_j=0,\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^4 b_j,x_j=0,\qquad
\sum_{j=1}^4 b_j,\sigma_{v,j}=0,
]
with
[
(y_j,x_j,\sigma_{v,j})=Q_v(h_j),
]
then on a good patch (c(h_j)\neq 0), so setting
[
a_j:=\frac{b_j}{c(h_j)}
]
recovers the corresponding defect-free finite-core coefficients at the lifted order-(7) level. Thus, as far as the current defect-free lifted formulation goes, **coplanarity already is the whole condition**. There is no additional compatibility equation hiding inside the same package.

That means the nonmixed odd-order local exact branch sheet is not something you can hope to kill by saying “coplanarity is not enough for a true bad (4)-point core.” At the present lifted order-(7) level, coplanarity is exactly what the bad (4)-point core becomes. So on that route, the unique nonmixed odd-order branch sheet is a **real candidate**, not a fake one. The same is true a fortiori for the mixed normal form: once the generalized-Vandermonde branch exists, the defect-free lifted theory does not add another scalar obstruction on top of it. 

So the attack changes direction:

the missing “extra algebraic condition beyond coplanarity” will **not** come from further squeezing the same defect-free lifted (Q_v)-equations. It can only come from going one layer higher, exactly as the other chat found for the (2)-point branch: a **source-level multi-body interaction remainder**. 

For (4) points, the right object would be a raw corrected source-level map
[
\mathfrak Q!\left(\sum_{j=1}^4 a_j\delta_{h_j}\right)
]
and then the pure (4)-body remainder obtained by inclusion–exclusion:
[
\mathcal I_4
============

\mathcal F_4
-\sum \mathcal F_3
+\sum \mathcal F_2
-\sum \mathcal F_1.
]
If that source-level object exists and is symmetric, vanishes when any amplitude is zero, and collapses on every partial diagonal (h_i=h_j), then that would impose a genuinely new algebraic divisibility condition — something like a factor of
[
\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j
\quad\text{and}\quad
\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)^2
]
on the pure (4)-body remainder. **That** would be an extra algebraic condition beyond coplanarity. But the current paper does not yet have that source-level (4)-body object. 

So the honest state of the (4)-point attack is:

* the defect-free lifted order-(7) geometry reduces true bad (4)-point cores to coplanarity of (Q_v);
* therefore there is no extra algebraic condition available at that same level;
* the nonmixed odd-order local exact branch sheet remains genuinely viable there;
* and any stronger obstruction must come from a new source-level pure (4)-body interaction theorem, not from more manipulation of the current coplanarity condition.

So the clean next attack on (4)-pair is now:

[
\boxed{
\text{define and study the pure source-level }4\text{-body interaction remainder } \mathcal I_4.
}
]

That is the first place an “extra condition beyond coplanarity” can actually appear.

## User (2026-04-19 18:40:13)

here is another update:

----

Yes. There is a real (4)-point attack now, and it gives a useful answer.

The clean source-level analogue of the (2)-point strategy is this:

Assume there is a raw corrected quotient-germ map on finite atomic sources, and define the **pure (4)-body remainder** by inclusion–exclusion:
[
\mathcal I_4
:=
\mathcal F_4
-\sum \mathcal F_3
+\sum \mathcal F_2
-\sum \mathcal F_1.
]
If this source-level object is symmetric in the four labeled atoms, vanishes when any amplitude is zero, and collapses on every partial diagonal (h_i=h_j), then the same midpoint/separation logic as in the (2)-point branch forces a strong factorization:
[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_4
============

\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)
\Bigl(\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)^2\Bigr),
\mathcal J_4
}
]
for some analytic (\mathcal J_4). This is the natural (4)-point analogue of the quadratic-remainder theorem the other chat isolated for the (2)-point branch. 

That gives the extra algebraic condition you asked for: a true bad (4)-point core would not merely lie on a coplanarity branch of the lifted curve (Q_v); it would have to lie on such a branch while also making a source-level (4)-body remainder vanish to **discriminant-squared order**.

So the right test is:

> does this extra (4)-body condition actually kill the local dangerous (4)-point branches?

I attacked that on both local model types.

---

## 1. Test on the nonmixed odd-order branch sheet

Near a nonmixed odd-order (T_v)-zero, we already reduced the local exact branch sheet to the normalized model
[
Q_v(x)=(x^n,x,x^2),
\qquad n \ \text{even},
]
with the exact opposite-side branch parameterized on the scale
[
a=-t,\qquad b=-(1-\rho)t,\qquad u=pt,\qquad v=q(t,\rho,p)t,
]
for small (t>0). The full exact lifted (4)-point coplanarity determinant scales as
[
\Delta_4 \sim t^{,n+3}.
]
This is the model order we already identified when classifying the nonmixed odd-order sheet. 

Now on that same cone, every pair difference is (O(t)), so the discriminant-squared factor in the hypothetical source-level remainder scales like
[
\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2 \sim t^{12}.
]
Therefore the pure (4)-body correction scales like
[
\mathcal I_4 = O(t^{12})
]
up to the amplitude factor.

So the comparison is:

* geometric coplanarity branch term: (t^{,n+3}),
* source-level pure (4)-body correction: (t^{12}).

Hence:

### If (n+3<12), i.e. (n\le 8),

the pure (4)-body correction is **higher order** than the branch equation.

That means it cannot kill the local branch; it only perturbs it. Since the odd-order nonmixed branch sheet already has a nondegenerate implicit-function parameterization, the sheet persists under such a higher-order perturbation.

So the low-order dangerous nonmixed cases
[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\ord T_v = 1,\ 3,\ 5
]
are **robust** against any extra (4)-body obstruction of discriminant-squared type.

Only when
[
n\ge 10
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\ord T_v\ge 7
]
could the extra (4)-body term enter at equal or lower order and potentially matter.

This is already a strong conclusion: the source-level (4)-body correction, even if it exists exactly as hoped, cannot eliminate the low-order nonmixed odd branch sheets.

---

## 2. Test on the mixed normal form

At a mixed point (K_v=T_v=0), the normalized model is
[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\quad n>m,
]
and the leading (4)-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
]
Its total scaling order on a shrinking opposite-side quadruple is
[
t^{,m+n+1},
]
because the Vandermonde contributes (t^6) and the Schur factor contributes degree (m+n-5). This is exactly the mixed order count already implicit in the other chat’s monomial analysis. 

Again, the source-level pure (4)-body correction contributes order
[
t^{12}.
]

So:

### If (m+n+1<12), i.e. (m+n\le 10),

the discriminant-squared (4)-body correction is again **higher order** than the mixed coplanarity equation.

Therefore it cannot remove those mixed dangerous local branches either; it only deforms them.

So all low-order mixed dangerous patterns with
[
m+n\le 10
]
are also robust against this kind of extra algebraic condition.

Only in the high-order mixed regime
[
m+n\ge 11
]
could the source-level (4)-body remainder enter at competitive order.

---

## 3. What this means

This is the real attack result:

[
\boxed{
\text{Even if a pure source-level (4)-body remainder exists with discriminant-squared factorization, it cannot kill the low-order dangerous (4)-point branches.}
}
]

So the extra algebraic condition you wanted **does exist in principle**, but after testing it on the actual local models, it turns out to be too high-order to eliminate the low-order dangerous branches.

That means:

* it is still worth formulating the pure (4)-body remainder theorem, because it is the correct source-level structure;
* but it will only matter in sufficiently high-order local regimes;
* the genuinely dangerous low-order nonmixed odd sheets and low-order mixed sheets must be ruled out, if at all, by **RH-specific jet restrictions**, not by generic discriminant-squared (4)-body algebra.

---

## 4. The sharpened roadmap for (4)-pair

So the (4)-point attack now splits very cleanly.

First, it is still worth trying to formalize the source-level (4)-body remainder theorem, because it is the right structural statement.

But second, the test above shows that the decisive local question is now:

[
\boxed{
\text{Can the actual zeta geometry realize the low-order dangerous nonmixed odd patterns }n=4,6,8,
\text{ or low-order dangerous mixed patterns with }m+n\le 10?
}
]

That is the real next frontier.

So my honest conclusion is:

* the extra (4)-body compatibility condition is conceptually real;
* but on the low-order dangerous local branches, it is too weak to kill them;
* therefore the (4)-point branch will now stand or fall on **RH-specific local jet restrictions**, not on generic higher-body divisibility alone.

_Thought for 2m 49s_

Yes — this update helps a lot, and it changes the 4-point attack in a useful way.

The main takeaway is:

**a pure source-level 4-body remainder is the right structural object, but by itself it is too weak to kill the low-order dangerous 4-point branches.**

So the 4-point attack now splits cleanly into two layers.

First, the structural layer:

If you can define a source-level corrected quotient-germ map on finite atomic sources and then define the pure 4-body remainder by inclusion–exclusion,
\[
\mathcal I_4
=
\mathcal F_4
-\sum \mathcal F_3
+\sum \mathcal F_2
-\sum \mathcal F_1,
\]
then the exact analogue of the 2-point argument is plausible:

- symmetry under permuting the 4 atoms,
- vanishing when any amplitude is zero,
- collapse on every partial diagonal \(h_i=h_j\),

should force a discriminant-squared factorization of the form
\[
\mathcal I_4
=
\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)
\Bigl(\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)^2\Bigr)\,
\mathcal J_4.
\]

That is the right source-level theorem to aim for.

But second, the scaling test in the update shows something important:

for the **low-order dangerous local models**, this extra 4-body factor still comes in too high.

On a shrinking 4-point configuration with scale \(t\), the discriminant-squared factor contributes order \(t^{12}\).

By contrast:

- on the nonmixed odd-order branch \(Q(x)=(x^n,x,x^2)\), the coplanarity branch equation is order
  \[
  t^{n+3}.
  \]
  So for
  \[
  n=4,6,8
  \quad\text{equivalently}\quad
  \ord T_v=1,3,5,
  \]
  the geometric branch occurs at orders \(7,9,11\), all lower than \(12\). So a \(t^{12}\) correction cannot kill those sheets; at most it perturbs them.

- on the mixed model \(Q(x)\sim(x^n,x,x^m)\), the leading coplanarity equation is order
  \[
  t^{m+n+1}.
  \]
  So when
  \[
  m+n\le 10,
  \]
  again the geometric branch appears at order \(<12\), and the discriminant-squared 4-body correction is too high-order to remove it.

That means the low-order dangerous branches are **robust** against this type of source-level 4-body correction.

So the 4-point roadmap is now much sharper:

### What still makes sense to prove

1. **Conditional pure 4-body remainder theorem**  
   Formalize the source-level inclusion–exclusion remainder \(\mathcal I_4\) and prove the discriminant-squared factorization, conditional on the source-level corrected map.

2. **Low-order robustness proposition**  
   State explicitly that such a discriminant-squared correction cannot eliminate:
   - the nonmixed odd-order sheets with \(n=4,6,8\),
   - the dangerous mixed low-order sector with \(m+n\le 10\).

That is mathematically useful because it tells you what this structural theorem can and cannot do.

### What the decisive next attack has to be

The real frontier is no longer “find another generic algebraic obstruction.” It is:

> derive **RH-specific local jet restrictions** that rule out the low-order dangerous 4-point patterns.

Concretely, I would now attack exactly these finite lists.

For the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), the dangerous low-order odd sheets are:
\[
n=4,6,8
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\ord T_v=1,3,5.
\]

So the right theorem target is:

> show that at a true RH nonmixed point, after normalizing
> \[
> Q_v(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x)),\qquad S(x)=x^2,
> \]
> the jet of \(Y\) modulo \(\mathrm{span}\{1,x,x^2\}\) cannot begin in degrees \(4,6,8\).

For the mixed side, the dangerous low-order sector is:
\[
m+n\le 10
\quad\text{with }n\text{ even and }n>m\ge 3.
\]
So the actual low-order dangerous pairs are
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]
In terms of
\[
r=\ord K_v,\qquad s=\ord T_v,
\]
these are
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5).
\]

So the mixed theorem target is:

> prove that the actual RH jet identities forbid the mixed order pairs
> \[
> (r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5).
> \]

That is now a finite, concrete obstruction list.

So the cleanest way I can help next is one of these two:

I can formalize the **conditional pure 4-body remainder theorem** and the **low-order robustness corollary** in exact math form, or I can start attacking the **RH-specific jet exclusions** for the nonmixed low-order patterns \(n=4,6,8\) and the mixed order pairs \((1,2),(1,4),(2,5)\).

If the goal is to make real progress on the 4-point branch, I would now prioritize the second.
## User (2026-04-19 18:43:17)

formalize this first in math form: I can formalize the conditional pure 4-body remainder theorem and the low-order robustness corollary in exact math form

## Assistant (2026-04-19 18:45:39)

_Thought for 2m 17s_

Yes. Here is a clean math formalization of the **conditional pure 4-body remainder theorem** and the **low-order robustness corollary**.

I will keep it entirely at the level of rigorous statements and proofs, with the minimum assumptions needed.

---

## 1. Source-level setup for the pure 4-body remainder

Let \(\mathcal G\) be a finite-dimensional complex vector space, and let
\[
\mathfrak Q:\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)\in\mathcal G
\]
be an analytic map defined on small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_{j=1}^N a_j\delta_{h_j}.
\]

For every nonempty subset \(I\subset\{1,2,3,4\}\), write
\[
\mu_I:=\sum_{i\in I} a_i\delta_{h_i},
\qquad
\mathcal F_I:=\mathfrak Q(\mu_I).
\]

Define the **pure 4-body remainder** by Möbius inversion on the subset lattice:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_4(a_1,h_1;\dots;a_4,h_4)
:=
\sum_{\varnothing\neq I\subset\{1,2,3,4\}}
(-1)^{\,4-|I|}\,\mathcal F_I.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal I_4
=
\mathcal F_{1234}
-\sum_{|I|=3}\mathcal F_I
+\sum_{|I|=2}\mathcal F_I
-\sum_{|I|=1}\mathcal F_I.
\]

---

## 2. Conditional pure 4-body factorization theorem

The right structural theorem is this.

### Theorem
Assume:

1. \(\mathfrak Q\) is analytic in the amplitudes and support positions.

2. \(\mathfrak Q\) is source-symmetric, so \(\mathfrak Q(\mu)\) depends only on the atomic source and not on the ordering of the labeled atoms.

3. The pure 4-body remainder vanishes on every partial diagonal:
   for every \(1\le i<j\le 4\),
   \[
   \mathcal I_4(a_1,h_1;\dots;a_i,h;\dots;a_j,h;\dots;a_4,h_4)=0.
   \]

Then there exists an analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued germ \(\mathcal J_4\) such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_4
=
\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)
\Bigl(\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)^2\Bigr)\,
\mathcal J_4.
}
\]

So the pure 4-body remainder carries both a full amplitude factor and a discriminant-squared factor.

---

### Proof

We break it into three steps.

#### Step 1: divisibility by \(\prod_j a_j\)

Fix \(k\in\{1,2,3,4\}\). If \(a_k=0\), then for every subset \(J\subset\{1,2,3,4\}\setminus\{k\}\),
\[
\mathcal F_{J\cup\{k\}}=\mathcal F_J,
\]
because the \(k\)-th atom contributes nothing to the source.

Therefore in the inclusion–exclusion sum for \(\mathcal I_4\), the terms indexed by \(J\) and \(J\cup\{k\}\) cancel pairwise:
\[
(-1)^{4-|J|}\mathcal F_J
+
(-1)^{4-(|J|+1)}\mathcal F_{J\cup\{k\}}
=
0.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal I_4=0
\qquad\text{whenever }a_k=0.
\]

Since this holds for each \(k\), analyticity implies divisibility by all four amplitudes:
\[
\mathcal I_4
=
\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)\,G(h_1,h_2,h_3,h_4)
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued germ \(G\).

#### Step 2: symmetric vanishing on every diagonal implies a Vandermonde factor

Because \(\mathfrak Q\) is source-symmetric and the inclusion–exclusion definition is symmetric in the four labels, the function \(G\) is symmetric in
\[
(h_1,h_2,h_3,h_4).
\]

By hypothesis, \(\mathcal I_4\) vanishes whenever \(h_i=h_j\). Since the amplitude prefactor does not vanish generically, the same is true of \(G\):
\[
G|_{h_i=h_j}=0
\qquad
(1\le i<j\le 4).
\]

Fix \(i<j\). The diagonal \(h_i=h_j\) is the zero set of the irreducible analytic factor \((h_i-h_j)\). Since \(G\) vanishes identically on that hypersurface, the analytic divisibility theorem gives
\[
(h_i-h_j)\mid G.
\]
Doing this for every \(i<j\), we get
\[
\Delta(h):=\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)
\quad\text{divides }G.
\]
So
\[
G=\Delta\,H
\]
for some analytic \(H\).

#### Step 3: symmetry upgrades \(\Delta\) to \(\Delta^2\)

The Vandermonde \(\Delta\) is alternating, while \(G\) is symmetric. Therefore
\[
H=\frac{G}{\Delta}
\]
is alternating:
\[
H(h_{\sigma(1)},\dots,h_{\sigma(4)})
=
\operatorname{sgn}(\sigma)\,H(h_1,\dots,h_4).
\]

A standard alternant factorization lemma now applies: every analytic alternating germ is divisible by the Vandermonde. Hence
\[
H=\Delta\,K
\]
for some analytic symmetric germ \(K\).

Therefore
\[
G=\Delta^2 K,
\]
and so
\[
\mathcal I_4
=
\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)\,\Delta(h)^2\,K.
\]

Writing \(\mathcal J_4:=K\) proves the theorem.

---

## 3. Coefficient-level consequence

Let
\[
L:\mathcal G\to V
\]
be any fixed linear projection into some coefficient space \(V\) — for example a cubic scalar space, a quintic fixed-sector space, or a septic quotient space.

Then the projected pure 4-body defect
\[
\mathcal E_4^L:=L(\mathcal I_4)
\]
satisfies the same factorization:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_4^L
=
\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)
\Bigl(\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)^2\Bigr)\,
\mathcal J_4^L
}
\]
for analytic \(\mathcal J_4^L\).

In particular, on a shrinking 4-point configuration at scale \(t\), the pure 4-body correction is always
\[
O(t^{12})
\]
times the amplitude product.

That is the key scaling fact.

---

## 4. Low-order robustness on the nonmixed branch

Now test this against the dangerous local nonmixed model
\[
Q_n(x)=(x^n,x,x^2),
\qquad n\ge 4,\ n\ \text{even}.
\]

Its exact 4-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,1,2,n,
\]
so on a shrinking configuration
\[
x_j=t\xi_j
\]
it scales as
\[
\Delta_4^{\mathrm{model}}(t\xi_1,\dots,t\xi_4)
=
t^{n+3}\,\Gamma_n(\xi_1,\dots,\xi_4),
\]
where \(\Gamma_n\) is the corresponding homogeneous generalized-Vandermonde factor.

The pure 4-body correction from the theorem above scales like
\[
O(t^{12}).
\]

So if
\[
n+3<12
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
n\le 8,
\]
then the pure 4-body correction is strictly higher order than the geometric coplanarity equation.

This gives the precise robustness statement.

### Corollary (nonmixed low-order robustness)
Assume the conditional pure 4-body factorization theorem above. Let
\[
Q_n(x)=(x^n,x,x^2),
\qquad n=4,6,8.
\]
Let \(p\) be a smooth point of the model branch
\[
\Gamma_n(\xi)=0
\]
with
\[
\nabla \Gamma_n(p)\neq 0.
\]
Then for every sufficiently small \(t>0\), any perturbation of the form
\[
t^{n+3}\Gamma_n(\xi)+t^{12}R_t(\xi)=0
\]
with \(R_t\) analytic and uniformly bounded has a nearby smooth solution branch through \(p\).

So the low-order nonmixed dangerous sheets
\[
n=4,6,8
\]
are robust against any discriminant-squared 4-body correction.

### Proof
Divide the equation by \(t^{n+3}\):
\[
\Gamma_n(\xi)+t^{12-(n+3)}R_t(\xi)=0.
\]
Since \(12-(n+3)>0\) for \(n=4,6,8\), the perturbation tends to zero uniformly. At a smooth point \(p\) of \(\Gamma_n=0\), the implicit function theorem gives a nearby smooth solution branch for small \(t\).

---

## 5. Low-order robustness on the mixed branch

Now test the mixed model
\[
Q_{m,n}(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,\quad n>m.
\]

Its leading 4-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,1,m,n,
\]
so on a shrinking configuration \(x_j=t\xi_j\),
\[
\Delta_{m,n}^{\mathrm{model}}(t\xi_1,\dots,t\xi_4)
=
t^{m+n+1}\,\Gamma_{m,n}(\xi_1,\dots,\xi_4),
\]
because the Vandermonde contributes degree \(6\) and the Schur factor contributes degree \(m+n-5\).

Again the pure 4-body correction is \(O(t^{12})\). Therefore:

if
\[
m+n+1<12
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
m+n\le 10,
\]
then the pure 4-body correction is strictly higher order than the mixed coplanarity equation.

So we get the mixed analogue.

### Corollary (mixed low-order robustness)
Assume the conditional pure 4-body factorization theorem above. Let
\[
Q_{m,n}(x)\sim(x^n,x,x^m)
\]
with
\[
m+n\le 10.
\]
Let \(p\) be a smooth point of the mixed model branch
\[
\Gamma_{m,n}(\xi)=0
\]
with \(\nabla\Gamma_{m,n}(p)\neq 0\). Then every perturbation of the form
\[
t^{m+n+1}\Gamma_{m,n}(\xi)+t^{12}R_t(\xi)=0
\]
with \(R_t\) analytic and uniformly bounded has a nearby smooth solution branch through \(p\) for sufficiently small \(t\).

So the low-order mixed dangerous branches with
\[
m+n\le 10
\]
are robust against any discriminant-squared 4-body correction.

---

## 6. What this proves and what it does not prove

This gives a real and useful theorem package:

1. If a source-level pure 4-body remainder exists and vanishes on every partial diagonal, then it carries the strong factor
   \[
   \Bigl(\prod_j a_j\Bigr)\Bigl(\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2\Bigr).
   \]

2. That factor is **too high-order** to eliminate the low-order dangerous local 4-point branches.

Concretely:

- on the nonmixed side, the dangerous low-order sheets
  \[
  n=4,6,8
  \quad\text{equivalently}\quad
  \ord T_v=1,3,5
  \]
  survive;

- on the mixed side, the dangerous low-order sector
  \[
  m+n\le 10
  \]
  survives.

So the pure 4-body structural theorem is real, but it cannot by itself kill the low-order dangerous 4-point branches.

That means the 4-point branch will ultimately stand or fall on **RH-specific jet restrictions**, not on discriminant-squared many-body divisibility alone.

---

## 7. The sharpened next target

The real next theorem target is now finite and concrete.

On the nonmixed side, the low-order dangerous cases are
\[
n=4,6,8.
\]

On the mixed side, the low-order dangerous cases are
\[
m+n\le 10.
\]
Since the mixed immediately dangerous sector is \(n\) even with \(n>m\ge 3\), this finite list is
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]

So the next serious attack is:

> prove that the actual RH jet identities forbid these low-order nonmixed and mixed patterns.

That is now the sharpest local frontier on the 4-point branch.

For the **nonmixed (4)-point branch**, the local problem reduces exactly to a jet theorem for one scalar function. Near a point with
[
T_v(0)=0,\qquad K_v(0)\neq 0,
]
the lifted curve
[
Q_v=(Y,x,S),\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\quad S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5},
]
can be affinely normalized so that
[
Q_v(x)=(\widetilde Y(x),,x,,x^2),
]
because when (K_v\neq 0), the lower triple ((1,x,S)) is already disconjugate and (S) is a genuine quadratic coordinate to first order. In this normalization, the lifted (4)-point Wronskian becomes
[
T_v=W_x(1,\widetilde Y,x,x^2)=2,\widetilde Y'''.
]
So the dangerous nonmixed odd-order branch is nothing more and nothing less than an **odd-order zero of (\widetilde Y''')**.

That makes the low-order dangerous cases completely explicit:

* (n=4) means
  [
  \widetilde Y'''(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0;
  ]
* (n=6) means
  [
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0;
  ]
* (n=8) means
  [
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=\widetilde Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
  ]

So the nonmixed (4)-pair problem has now been reduced to this very sharp statement:

[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized germ }\widetilde Y=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{mod}\ \operatorname{span}{1,x,x^2}
\text{ cannot have odd-order zeros of }\widetilde Y''' \text{ of orders }1,3,5.
}
]

That is much sharper than “rule out odd-order nonmixed (T_v)-zeros” in the abstract. It is a concrete jet condition.

For the **mixed (4)-point branch**, the notes already give the monomial normal form
[

\qquad m\ge 3,\ n>m,
]

The dangerous parity sector is (n) even, and the low-order dangerous cases are exactly those with
[

]
That leaves only the three model pairs
[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
]
So the mixed (4)-pair problem is now equally sharp:

[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized lifted jets cannot realize }(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6).
}
]

Nothing broader is needed on the mixed side anymore.

The important negative conclusion is that the current draft does **not** yet contain any identity linking
[

\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}
]
tightly enough to rule out those low-order patterns. At the present defect-free lifted level, a bad (4)-point core becomes coplanarity of the lifted points (Q_v(h_j)), and there is no extra scalar compatibility condition beyond that. So generic branch geometry will not save the (4)-pair branch. Any further progress must come from **RH-specific jet identities** for (u_5) and (\Delta_7), not from another generic first-contact argument.

So the attack result is:

[
\boxed{
\text{The (4)-pair endgame has now been reduced to a finite list of explicit low-order jet obstructions.}
}
]

More concretely, the next exact theorem to try to prove is one of these two:

1. a **nonmixed jet theorem**
   [

I attacked it as hard as I can from the current draft, and the honest result is:

**I cannot prove that the actual RH jet identities forbid the low-order dangerous 4-point patterns from the identities currently in the paper.**

What I *can* prove rigorously is that the 4-point problem has now been reduced to a **finite list of explicit jet obstructions**, and that the current draft does **not yet contain** an identity strong enough to eliminate them.

Here is the clean reduction.

---

## 1. Nonmixed 4-point branch reduces to one scalar jet

Work on a good \(v_5\)-patch and write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\qquad
Q_v=(Y,x,S).
\]

Let \(x=0\) be a nonmixed 4-point point:
\[
K_v(0)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(0)=0.
\]

Because \(K_v(0)\neq 0\), the function \(S\) has nonzero second derivative at \(0\) in the \(x\)-coordinate. After subtracting an affine function of \(x\) from \(S\), the germ \(S\) has a nondegenerate critical point at \(0\). By the one-variable analytic Morse lemma, after an analytic reparametrization \(x\mapsto \xi\) and an affine target change preserving coplanarity, we may normalize to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2).
\]

Now replace \(\widetilde Y\) by its class modulo \(\operatorname{span}\{1,\xi,\xi^2\}\), so that
\[
\widetilde Y(0)=\widetilde Y'(0)=\widetilde Y''(0)=0.
\]

Then the lifted 4-point Wronskian becomes
\[
W_\xi(1,\widetilde Y,\xi,\xi^2)
=
-2\,\widetilde Y'''.
\]
Since Wronskians under analytic reparametrization change only by a nowhere-zero factor, this means:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At a nonmixed point, }T_v=0
\iff
\widetilde Y'''=0
\text{ after normalization.}
}
\]

More precisely, if
\[
\widetilde Y(\xi)=c_n \xi^n+O(\xi^{n+1}),
\qquad c_n\neq 0,
\qquad n\ge 3,
\]
then
\[
\ord_0 T_v=n-3.
\]

So the dangerous low-order nonmixed cases are exactly:

- \(n=4\), i.e.
  \[
  \widetilde Y'''(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0;
  \]
- \(n=6\), i.e.
  \[
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(5)}(0)=0,
  \qquad
  \widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0;
  \]
- \(n=8\), i.e.
  \[
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=\widetilde Y^{(7)}(0)=0,
  \qquad
  \widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
  \]

So the nonmixed 4-point problem is now exactly this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized germ }\widetilde Y
\text{ cannot have odd-order zeros of }\widetilde Y'''
\text{ of orders }1,3,5.
}
\]

---

## 2. Mixed 4-point branch reduces to a finite list of monomial pairs

At a mixed point
\[
K_v(0)=0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current draft already reduces the local model to
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,\quad n>m.
\]

Write
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v.
\]
Then the monomial bookkeeping gives
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,\qquad s\ge 2r.
\]

The dangerous mixed sector is \(n\) even. The low-order dangerous cases are those with
\[
m+n\le 10.
\]
Since \(n>m\ge 3\) and \(n\) must be even, this leaves exactly:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\qquad (3,6),\qquad (4,6).
\]

Equivalently, in \((r,s)\)-coordinates these are
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\qquad (1,4),\qquad (2,5).
\]

So the mixed 4-point problem is now equally sharp:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized lifted jets cannot realize }
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6).
}
\]

---

## 3. What the current draft does **not** yet contain

This is the crucial point.

The current draft gives:

- linear independence of
  \[
  1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c},
  \]
- non-affinity of
  \[
  \sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
  \]
  in
  \[
  x=\frac{v_5}{c},
  \]
- \(K_v\not\equiv 0\),
- \(T_v\not\equiv 0\),
- shrinking exact 4-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\),
- model-level parity and branch information.

But it does **not** contain any RH-specific identity coupling
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
strongly enough to force:

- \(\widetilde Y''' \) to avoid odd-order zeros of orders \(1,3,5\), or
- the mixed order pairs \((1,2),(1,4),(2,5)\) to be impossible.

At the current defect-free lifted level, a bad 4-point core is exactly compressed into **coplanarity of the lifted points**. There is no second scalar compatibility condition left over at that same level.

So the current draft is **not yet strong enough** to prove the desired exclusion.

---

## 4. Why this is a real reduction, not just a failure

This is still useful, because the 4-point endgame is no longer vague.

It has been reduced to a **finite list of explicit low-order jet obstructions**:

### Nonmixed
Exclude
\[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8.
\]

### Mixed
Exclude
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5).
\]

That is a sharp finite target.

---

## 5. The actual next theorem to attack

So the next honest theorem target is one of these two.

### Nonmixed jet theorem
Prove that for the actual RH normalized germ
\[
Q_v(\xi)=(\widetilde Y(\xi),\xi,\xi^2),
\]
the function \(\widetilde Y'''\) cannot have odd-order zeros of orders \(1,3,5\).

### Mixed jet theorem
Prove that the actual RH lifted jets cannot realize
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]

Those are now the sharpest local frontiers on the 4-point branch.

---

## 6. Bottom line

So my attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The 4-point endgame has been reduced to a finite list of explicit low-order jet obstructions,}
}
\]
but

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current draft does not yet contain the RH-specific identities needed to rule them out.}
}

The right next move is not another generic branch or coplanarity argument. It is to find a **new RH-specific jet identity** linking \(u_5\) and \(\Delta_7\) strongly enough to exclude those explicit low-order patterns.

What I *can* do is formalize exactly what identity would be sufficient, and reduce both the nonmixed and mixed 4-point problems to that one target.

Here is the clean math.

---

## 1. Exact nonmixed reduction

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\qquad
Q_v=(Y,x,S).
\]

At a nonmixed point
\[
K_v(0)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
the analytic Morse lemma lets you normalize the third coordinate to a true quadratic coordinate. After an analytic reparametrization \(\xi=\xi(x)\) and an affine target change preserving coplanarity, you can write
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\widetilde Y(0)=\widetilde Y'(0)=\widetilde Y''(0)=0.
\]

In this normalization,
\[
W_\xi(1,\widetilde Y,\xi,\xi^2)=-2\,\widetilde Y'''.
\]
Since \(T_v\) transforms by a nowhere-zero factor under analytic reparametrization,
\[
\boxed{
T_v=0
\iff
\widetilde Y'''=0
\text{ in the normalized nonmixed chart.}
}
\]

So the dangerous low-order nonmixed cases are exactly:
\[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8
\]
for the leading order of \(\widetilde Y\), equivalently odd-order zeros of \(\widetilde Y'''\) of orders
\[
1,\ 3,\ 5.
\]

So the nonmixed 4-point problem has been reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the normalized germ }\widetilde Y
\text{ cannot have first nonzero term in degrees }4,6,8.
}
\]

---

## 2. Exact mixed reduction

At a mixed point
\[
K_v(0)=0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current draft already gives the monomial normal form
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,\quad n>m.
\]

Write
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v.
\]
Then
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,\qquad s\ge 2r.
\]

The dangerous mixed sector is \(n\) even. The low-order dangerous cases are exactly
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5).
\]

So the mixed 4-point problem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized lifted jets cannot realize }
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6).
}
\]

---

## 3. A single sufficient identity that kills **both** problems

There is one very natural RH-specific jet identity that would simultaneously kill all the explicit low-order dangerous patterns.

### Candidate parity-normalized jet identity
After the nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
suppose one could prove
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y(-\xi)=-\widetilde Y(\xi).
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\widetilde Y(\xi)\in \xi\,\mathbf C\{\xi^2\}.
\]

Then only odd powers of \(\xi\) occur in \(\widetilde Y\). In particular:

- the nonmixed dangerous degrees \(4,6,8\) are impossible;
- \(\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\) is an even function, so any zero at \(0\) has **even** order;
- therefore odd-order nonmixed \(T_v\)-zeros of orders \(1,3,5\) are impossible.

This already kills the low-order nonmixed dangerous cases.

And it also kills the dangerous mixed cases, because the mixed dangerous sector is exactly \(n\) even. If the first component of the normalized lifted germ is always odd in the normalized local coordinate, then \(n\) is always odd, so
\[
(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
are all excluded.

So this single parity identity would resolve the full low-order explicit list.

---

## 4. A weaker finite-jet version that would still suffice

If full oddness is too strong, the exact low-order theorem you need is only:

### Nonmixed finite-jet exclusion
In the normalized nonmixed chart,
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)=0.
}
\]
That is enough to exclude \(n=4,6,8\).

### Mixed finite-jet exclusion
At mixed points, the first nonzero term of the normalized first component should not occur in degrees
\[
4,\ 6
\]
when the second nonzero third-coordinate order is \(m=3,4\) in the low-order list. Equivalently, exclude
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]

So the whole 4-point low-order obstruction is now a finite jet condition.

---

## 5. What the current draft does **not** yet give

I do **not** see any identity currently in the draft that implies:

- \(\widetilde Y\) is odd in the normalized nonmixed coordinate, or
- \(\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)=0\), or
- the mixed low-order pairs \((3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\) are impossible.

At the present defect-free lifted level, a bad 4-point core is exactly compressed into coplanarity of the lifted points. There is no extra scalar compatibility condition in the current paper beyond that.

So there is **no new RH-specific jet identity yet available from the present text**.

---

## 6. The clean theorem target to add to your attack list

The mathematically sharp next theorem is:

### Nonmixed jet theorem
At every nonmixed point, after normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\xi,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the normalized first component satisfies
\[
\widetilde Y(\xi)\in \xi\,\mathbf C\{\xi^2\},
\]
or at least
\[
\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)=0.
\]

### Mixed jet theorem
At every mixed point, the normalized lifted germ cannot realize
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]

Those are now the precise finite targets.

---

## 7. My best attack suggestion from here

The only realistic places such an identity could come from are:

1. a **source-level corrected quotient-germ map** plus a 4-body structural theorem that imposes more than coplanarity on true 4-point cores; or

2. an **RH-specific symmetry** of the normalized lifted germ, which in practice would show up as oddness of the first normalized coordinate \(\widetilde Y\).

So the clean next move is not more generic geometry. It is to search for a **normal-form involution symmetry**:
\[
\xi\mapsto -\xi
\]
under which the normalized first component is odd.

That is the one new RH-specific identity that would actually kill the explicit low-order list in one shot.

If you want, I’ll now formalize this as exact proposition/theorem statements in paper-ready math language, or help test whether any current formulas for \(u_5\) and \(\Delta_7\) are compatible with that oddness target.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 19:00:10)

The key question is whether the draft already forces any parity, order-gap, or derivative relation strong enough to kill the low-order dangerous cases.

_Thought for 2m 55s_

I pushed the hunt as far as the current draft allows, and I found something important that is **not** in the paper:

## Main result: there is no new jet identity available at the current lifted level

The current defect-free lifted formalism is too flexible to forbid the low-order dangerous 4-point patterns. In fact, one can realize **arbitrary** analytic lifted germs \(Y,S\) on a good \(v_5\)-patch using only the current variables \((c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)\).

That means:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No identity involving only }c,\ v_5,\ u_5,\ \Delta_7
\text{ and their derivatives can exclude the low-order dangerous 4-point patterns.}
}
\]

So if an RH-specific jet obstruction exists, it must come from **deeper source-level structure** that is not yet encoded in the current lifted variables alone.

---

# 1. Exact realization lemma

Let \(\widetilde Y(\xi)\) and \(\widetilde S(\xi)\) be arbitrary analytic germs at \(\xi=0\).

Define
\[
c(\xi)\equiv 1,
\qquad
v_5(\xi):=1+\xi,
\qquad
u_5(\xi):=\widetilde Y(\xi),
\qquad
\Delta_7(\xi):=(1+\xi)\widetilde S(\xi).
\]

Then on a sufficiently small neighborhood of \(0\),

- \(c\neq 0\),
- \(v_5\neq 0\),
- and
  \[
  M=c\,v_5'-c'v_5=1\neq 0.
  \]

So this is a good \(v_5\)-patch.

Now the normalized lifted coordinates are
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=1+\xi,
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=\widetilde Y(\xi),
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\widetilde S(\xi).
\]

After the harmless affine shift \(x\mapsto x-1\), the lifted curve becomes
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\widetilde S(\xi)\bigr).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every analytic pair of germs }(\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)
\text{ occurs as a lifted germ }(Y,S)
\text{ on some good }v_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is the key realization lemma.

---

# 2. Consequence: no hidden lifted jet obstruction at the current level

Because arbitrary analytic \((\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)\) are realizable, the current lifted formalism by itself cannot force:

- parity of \(\widetilde Y\),
- vanishing of specific derivatives of \(\widetilde Y\),
- parity restrictions on mixed exponents \((m,n)\),
- or any low-order exclusion beyond what is already encoded by the explicit \(K_v\)- and \(T_v\)-based bookkeeping.

In other words:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any new RH-specific jet identity must use information not contained in the current variables }
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)\text{ alone.}
}
\]

It must come from one of:

1. the **underlying source-level corrected quotient-germ map** on atomic sources;
2. the deeper matrix-level construction behind \(u_5\) and \(\Delta_7\) (the \(X_1,X_3,\ldots\) data);
3. or an RH-specific symmetry/involution not yet encoded in the current lifted formulation.

This is a real negative theorem, and it is useful: it tells you where **not** to keep hunting.

---

# 3. Explicit realization of all low-order dangerous patterns

This realization lemma immediately shows that all the currently dangerous low-order local models are realizable at the present lifted level.

## Nonmixed dangerous patterns

Take
\[
\widetilde S(\xi)=\xi^2,
\qquad
\widetilde Y(\xi)=\xi^n,
\]
with
\[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8.
\]

Then
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\xi^n,\ \xi,\ \xi^2\bigr),
\]
which is exactly the dangerous nonmixed model.

In this case
\[
K_v\neq 0,
\qquad
T_v\sim \xi^{n-3},
\]
so the odd-order nonmixed dangerous cases
\[
\ord T_v=1,3,5
\]
are all realizable.

## Mixed dangerous patterns

Take
\[
\widetilde S(\xi)=\xi^m,
\qquad
\widetilde Y(\xi)=\xi^n,
\]
with
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]

Then
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\xi^n,\ \xi,\ \xi^m\bigr),
\]
which is exactly the dangerous mixed model.

So the entire low-order dangerous list is realizable in the current lifted variables.

That means:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the current lifted identities are too weak to exclude the explicit low-order dangerous 4-point patterns.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Exact nonmixed reduction, formalized

This part **is** still useful and should be kept as a named target.

At a nonmixed point
\[
K_v(0)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
after analytic reparametrization and affine target normalization preserving coplanarity, the lifted germ can be written as
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\widetilde Y(0)=\widetilde Y'(0)=\widetilde Y''(0)=0.
\]

Then
\[
W_\xi(1,\widetilde Y,\xi,\xi^2)=-2\,\widetilde Y'''.
\]
So the nonmixed 4-point problem is exactly the jet problem
\[
\boxed{
\text{exclude odd-order zeros of }\widetilde Y'''
\text{ of orders }1,3,5.
}
\]

Equivalently, exclude leading terms of \(\widetilde Y\) in degrees
\[
4,\ 6,\ 8.
\]

This is the sharpest nonmixed formulation.

---

# 5. Exact mixed reduction, formalized

At a mixed point
\[
K_v(0)=0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current bookkeeping gives the monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,\quad n>m,
\]
with
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
and
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,\qquad s\ge 2r.
\]

The dangerous low-order mixed cases are exactly
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5).
\]

So the mixed 4-point problem is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exclude the three explicit mixed low-order jet pairs }
(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
}
\]

This is now finite and concrete.

---

# 6. The identity that would actually be strong enough

There *is* a single clean RH-specific identity that would kill the whole low-order list in one shot.

After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
if one could prove the parity identity
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y(-\xi)=-\widetilde Y(\xi),
}
\]
then:

- only odd powers of \(\xi\) appear in \(\widetilde Y\);
- so degrees \(4,6,8\) are impossible;
- and all dangerous mixed cases with \(n\) even are impossible too.

So the real dream identity is:

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y\in \xi\,\mathbf C\{\xi^2\}.
}
\]

But I do **not** see any route to derive this from the current paper.

---

# 7. What this means for the next attack

This is the real conclusion of the hunt:

## What I found
- a rigorous **realization lemma** showing arbitrary analytic \((Y,S)\) occur on good \(v_5\)-patches;
- therefore no new jet obstruction can come from the current lifted variables alone;
- and the 4-point endgame is reduced to a finite explicit jet list.

## What I did **not** find
- any new RH-specific jet identity already latent in the current draft that forbids
  \[
  n=4,6,8
  \quad\text{or}\quad
  (m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6).
  \]

## What must happen next
Any real progress now has to use **deeper RH-specific structure**:
- source-level corrected quotient-germ maps and 4-body remainders,
- or matrix-level identities behind \(u_5\) and \(\Delta_7\),
- or a hidden local involution symmetry that forces \(\widetilde Y\) odd.

---

# 8. The strongest new statement I’d add to the attack notes

Here is the best concise theorem-level summary:

> **Realization lemma for lifted germs.**  
> Every analytic pair of local germs \((\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)\) occurs, after affine normalization, as the lifted pair
> \[
> \left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}\right)
> \]
> on some good \(v_5\)-patch with \(c\neq 0\), \(v_5\neq 0\), \(M\neq 0\).

> **Corollary.**  
> No obstruction to the low-order dangerous 4-point patterns can be derived from identities involving only \(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7\) and their derivatives. Any such obstruction must come from deeper RH-specific source-level or matrix-level structure.

That is, in my view, the most useful thing I found.

If you want, the next thing I can do is formalize this as exact LaTeX propositions/remarks for the paper, or help design the next search at the matrix/source level where a real RH-specific identity could still live.
## User (2026-04-19 19:04:51)

from the other chat:

---

Yes. Going only from what is already in the current file, the strongest exact lifted (4)-point identities you can derive are these. The file gives the lifted patch variables
[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c,v_5},
]
together with
[
K_v=x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v'x'',
\qquad
T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S). ; ;
]

Now treat (x) as the local coordinate on a good (v_5)-patch, so (x'(h)\neq 0). Writing (S=S(x)), chain rule gives
[
\sigma_v'(h)=S_x,x',
\qquad
\sigma_v''(h)=S_{xx}(x')^2+S_x x'',
]
hence
[
K_v
===

# x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v' x''

(x')^3 S_{xx}.
]
So the exact coordinate relation is
[
\boxed{K_v=(x')^3,S''(x).}
]
In particular, (K_v) and (S'') have the same zero set and the same vanishing order on a good patch. This is the precise version of the “(K_v) is (S'') up to a nowhere-zero factor” statement already used in the file.

For (T_v), use the reparametrization formula for Wronskians of four functions:
[
W_h(1,Y,x,S)=(x')^6,W_x(1,Y,x,S).
]
A direct determinant expansion gives
[
W_x(1,Y,x,S)
============

\det!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y&x&S\
0&Y'&1&S'\
0&Y''&0&S''\
0&Y'''&0&S'''
\end{pmatrix}
=============

S''Y'''-S'''Y''.
]
Therefore
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr).}
]
Equivalently,
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6,S''^{,2},\frac{d}{dx}!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).}
]
Since (K_v=(x')^3S''), this can also be written as
[
\boxed{T_v=K_v^{,2},\frac{d}{dx}!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).}
]
That is the cleanest identity in the file for the lifted (4)-point branch. It is stronger than the bare statement “(T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S)).”

This immediately gives the exact nonmixed reduction. If (K_v(0)\neq 0), then after affine normalization of the lower triple ((1,x,S)) you may take
[
S=x^2,
\qquad
S''=2,
\qquad
S'''=0,
]
so the identity becomes
[
\boxed{T_v=2(x')^6,Y'''.}
]
Thus at a nonmixed point, the dangerous low-order branch cases are exactly the odd-order zeros of (Y'''). In particular:
[
\ord_0 T_v=1 \iff Y'''(0)=0,\ Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0,
]
[
\ord_0 T_v=3 \iff Y^{(3)}(0)=Y^{(4)}(0)=Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\ Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0,
]
[
\ord_0 T_v=5 \iff Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\ Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
]
So the nonmixed (4)-point obstruction has been reduced to a jet theorem for one scalar germ (Y=u_5/c) after normalizing (S) to (x^2).

For the mixed case, let
[
r:=\ord_0 K_v.
]
Since (K_v=(x')^3S''), one has
[
S''(x)=\kappa x^r+O(x^{r+1}),
\qquad \kappa\neq 0.
]
After removing affine terms and integrating twice,
[
\boxed{S(x)=\frac{\kappa}{(r+1)(r+2)}x^{r+2}+O(x^{r+3}).}
]
So the mixed exponent (m) is exactly
[
\boxed{m=r+2.}
]

Now write the first term of (Y) not absorbed by (\operatorname{span}{1,x,S}) as
[
Y(x)=\alpha x^n+O(x^{n+1}),
\qquad \alpha\neq 0,\qquad n>r+2.
]
Substituting into
[
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr)
]
gives
[
S''Y'''-S'''Y''
===============

\kappa\alpha,n(n-1)\bigl(n-r-2\bigr)x^{n+r-3}+O(x^{n+r-2}),
]
so
[
\boxed{\ord_0 T_v=n+r-3.}
]
If (s:=\ord_0 T_v), this becomes
[
\boxed{n=s-r+3,}
]
which is exactly the mixed bookkeeping relation already recorded in the recent notes. ; ;

The same identity also yields a cleaner invariant quantity:
[
\boxed{
\ord_0!\left(\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\right)=s-2r.
}
]
So the low-order dangerous mixed cases are not abstract anymore. They are exactly
[
(r,s)\in{(1,2),(1,4),(2,5)},
]
equivalently
[
(m,n)\in{(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)},
]
equivalently
[
\ord_0!\left(\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\right)\in{0,2,1}.
]
That is the finite list of low-order mixed jet obstructions currently visible from the file. ; ;

So the exact identities you can really extract from the current draft are:

[
\boxed{K_v=(x')^3S''}
]
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6(S''Y'''-S'''Y'')}
]
[
\boxed{T_v=K_v^2\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)}
]
and therefore the two sharp reductions:

* nonmixed: dangerous (4)-point branches are exactly low odd-order zeros of (Y''') after normalizing (S=x^2);
* mixed: dangerous (4)-point branches are exactly the three low-order order pairs ((r,s)=(1,2),(1,4),(2,5)).

What the current file still does **not** provide is an RH-specific relation forcing those low-order patterns to be impossible. But it does now reduce the (4)-pair endgame to a finite list of explicit low-order jet identities to kill.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 19:06:34)

_Thought for 1m 40s_

Yes — this is exactly the right direction, and I think there is one genuinely useful identity here that is **not** yet emphasized in the draft.

The formulas from the other chat are right. On a good \(v_5\)-patch, with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
you get
\[
K_v=(x')^3\,S''(x),
\]
and
\[
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
T_v=(x')^6\,S''^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)
}
\]
on every nonmixed patch where \(K_v\neq 0\). That is the cleanest exact lifted \(4\)-point identity currently available. 

I would package the new invariant as
\[
\mathcal R(x):=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).
\]

This is useful because \(\mathcal R\) is the **canonical scalar invariant** of the lifted \(4\)-point branch on a nonmixed patch.

Why canonical?

If you change \(Y\) by the affine gauge that leaves coplanarity unchanged,
\[
Y\longmapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S,
\]
then
\[
Y''\longmapsto Y''+\gamma S'',
\qquad
\frac{Y''}{S''}\longmapsto \frac{Y''}{S''}+\gamma,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)
\]
is unchanged. So \(\mathcal R\) is exactly the gauge-invariant scalar you want to study, not \(Y\) by itself.

That gives a sharper reformulation of the nonmixed branch.

At a nonmixed point \(K_v(0)\neq 0\), you may normalize to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr).
\]
Then
\[
S''=2,\qquad S'''=0,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi).
\]
Therefore the dangerous nonmixed cases are exactly
\[
\ord_0 \mathcal R=1,\ 3,\ 5,
\]
equivalently
\[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8.
\]

This is cleaner than saying “odd-order zeros of \(T_v\)” because it isolates the invariant scalar that survives normalization.

The mixed case also gets cleaner in terms of \(\mathcal R\).

If
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then from
\[
K_v=(x')^3S'',
\qquad
\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}=\mathcal R
\]
you get
\[
\ord_0 \mathcal R = s-2r.
\]
And since the mixed normal form has
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,
\]
you can rewrite it as
\[
\boxed{
m=r+2,\qquad n=r+\ord_0\mathcal R+3.
}
\]

So the dangerous mixed low-order list
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
is equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

That is a very useful compression. It means the entire low-order \(4\)-point obstruction can be stated in terms of the pair
\[
\bigl(\ord_0 K_v,\ \ord_0 \mathcal R\bigr).
\]

So I think the strongest “new identity not yet in the paper” is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R:=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)
}
\]
on nonmixed patches, together with the order bookkeeping
\[
\boxed{
\ord_0 \mathcal R=s-2r.
}
\]

This unifies both branches:

For nonmixed points \(r=0\), dangerous cases are
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R=1,3,5.
\]

For mixed points \(r\ge 1\), dangerous low-order cases are exactly
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

That is the sharpest finite target I can derive from the current file.

Now for the bad news.

I do **not** see any current RH-specific identity in the draft forcing:

- \(\mathcal R\) to be even,
- or \(\ord_0\mathcal R\notin\{1,3,5\}\) in the nonmixed case,
- or \((r,\ord_0\mathcal R)\notin\{(1,0),(1,2),(2,1)\}\) in the mixed case.

And the realization lemma shows why: at the present lifted level, arbitrary analytic \((Y,S)\) can be realized on a good patch, so no identity involving only \(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7\) and their derivatives can exclude those patterns. Any such exclusion must come from deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, not from the lifted variables alone.

So the strongest rigorous conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current draft reduces the \(4\)-point branch to a finite low-order jet obstruction for the invariant }
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\text{ but does not yet provide an RH-specific identity forbidding it.}
}
\]

That suggests the next exact theorem target should be phrased in terms of \(\mathcal R\), not directly in terms of \(Y\) and \(S\).

The clean targets are:

For nonmixed points:
\[
\boxed{
\ord_0\mathcal R\notin\{1,3,5\}.
}
\]

For mixed points:
\[
\boxed{
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)\notin\{(1,0),(1,2),(2,1)\}.
}
\]

That is the sharpest way I know to formulate the 4-point endgame from the current file. 

The most promising next hunt is no longer among lifted identities. It is in the deeper matrix/source-level construction behind \(u_5\) and \(\Delta_7\), looking for a symmetry or structural relation that forces \(\mathcal R\) to have better parity or higher vanishing than generic smooth geometry allows.
## User (2026-04-19 19:09:05)

## Assistant (2026-04-19 19:11:33)

_Thought for 2m 20s_

I pushed the hunt hard, and here is the strongest clean reduction I can actually justify.

## 1. The right invariant to study is not \(Y\) itself

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Then the exact lifted identities are
\[
K_v=(x')^3 S''(x),
\qquad
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr),
\]
hence on every nonmixed patch \(K_v\neq 0\),
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\qquad
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.
}
\]
So \(\mathcal R\) is the canonical scalar invariant of the lifted \(4\)-point branch. It is gauge-invariant under
\[
Y\mapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S,
\]
because \(\mathcal Z\mapsto \mathcal Z+\gamma\), so \(\mathcal R\) stays fixed. This is the cleanest exact identity currently visible from the file. 

## 2. Nonmixed and mixed low-order obstructions in terms of \(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R\)

At a nonmixed point, after normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
you have
\[
\mathcal Z(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y''(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi).
\]
So the dangerous nonmixed cases
\[
n=4,6,8
\]
become exactly
\[
\ord_0 \mathcal Z=2,4,6
\qquad\text{or equivalently}\qquad
\ord_0 \mathcal R=1,3,5.
\]

At a mixed point, if
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then the monomial bookkeeping gives
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,
\]
and
\[
\ord_0 \mathcal Z = n-r-2 = s-2r+1,
\qquad
\ord_0 \mathcal R = s-2r.
\]
So the dangerous mixed low-order list
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
is exactly
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

That means the whole \(4\)-point endgame has now been reduced to a finite jet obstruction for \(\mathcal Z\) or \(\mathcal R\). 

## 3. The dream identity, properly formulated

The “dream identity” should not be stated as “\(Y\) is odd” in an arbitrary chart. The invariant form is:

### Nonmixed dream identity
After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the normalized first component satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y(-\xi)=-\widetilde Y(\xi).
}
\]

This is equivalent to either of the following:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y''(\xi)\ \text{is odd},
}
\qquad
\boxed{
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\ \text{is even}.
}
\]

So the dream identity is really:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At every nonmixed point, }\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
\text{ is even in the normalized local coordinate.}
}
\]

If that were true, it would immediately kill the dangerous nonmixed cases
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R=1,3,5.
\]

Geometrically, it says the normalized lifted curve is invariant under the involution
\[
(\eta,\xi,\zeta)\mapsto(-\eta,-\xi,\zeta),
\]
which is exactly the reflection symmetry one would hope for in the nonmixed normal form.

## 4. A mixed analogue that would also suffice

For the mixed branch, a sufficient identity is weaker and more combinatorial:

\[
\boxed{
\ord_0 \mathcal Z \ge 4
\quad\text{at every mixed point.}
}
\]

Because the dangerous mixed low-order list has
\[
\ord_0\mathcal Z=1,3,2,
\]
this single bound would kill
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
in one shot.

So the two clean theorem targets are now:

### Nonmixed parity theorem
\[
\mathcal R \text{ is even in the normalized coordinate.}
\]

### Mixed order-gap theorem
\[
\ord_0 \mathcal Z \ge 4.
\]

These are the sharpest finite targets I can derive.

## 5. What I found — and what I did not

I did **not** find a proof of either theorem from the current draft.

In fact, the realization lemma shows why: at the present lifted level, arbitrary analytic pairs \((Y,S)\) can be realized on a good \(v_5\)-patch, so no identity involving only
\[
c,\ v_5,\ u_5,\ \Delta_7
\]
and their derivatives can force the parity of \(\mathcal R\) or the lower bound \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\ge 4\). Any such identity has to come from deeper RH-specific structure — source-level or matrix-level — not from the lifted variables alone.

So the hunt result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current file reduces the \(4\)-point branch to the invariant pair }(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R),
\text{ but does not yet contain the RH-specific identity needed to control them.}
}
\]

## 6. Where to hunt next

There are only two plausible places left for the missing identity to live.

### A. Source-level reflection symmetry
If the raw corrected quotient-germ map had a local involution symmetry near a one-pair source that, after normalization, became
\[
\xi\mapsto -\xi,
\]
then the dream identity \(\widetilde Y\) odd would follow. This is the most conceptual route.

### B. Matrix-level fixed-sector identity
Since \(u_5\) and \(\Delta_7\) come from deeper matrix-level objects, one could hope for an identity forcing
\[
\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)
\]
to be even, or at least forcing
\[
\ord_0\mathcal Z\ge 4
\]
at mixed points. But nothing like that is yet visible in the current draft.

## 7. The strongest exact next statements to add to the attack list

I would now treat these as the named theorem targets:

### Nonmixed jet theorem
At every nonmixed point,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
\text{ is even in the normalized local coordinate.}
}
\]

### Mixed jet theorem
At every mixed point,
\[
\boxed{
\ord_0\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\ge 4.
}
\]

If either one can be proved from RH-specific source/matrix-level structure, the low-order dangerous \(4\)-point list collapses immediately.

So the “dream identity” is not dead — it just needs to be reformulated correctly. The right dream identity is **evenness of \(\mathcal R=T_v/K_v^2\)** in the normalized nonmixed coordinate, with mixed counterpart **\(\ord \mathcal Z\ge 4\)**. Those are the two exact places I would keep attacking.
