_Thought for 51s_

Yes. The next attack should be a **finite linear system** for the parity-bad coefficients.

The point is to stop talking abstractly about “equivariant normalization” and isolate the exact unknowns that must vanish to kill the explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list. The background facts we are now taking as fixed are: the nonmixed \(3\)-point branch is locally classified, the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch can carry preexisting odd-order sheets, and the mixed locus is the real codimension-two danger. turn33file14

Here is the concrete setup.

Let \(\xi\) be a centered local coordinate, and truncate all jets at order \(8\). Write
\[
c(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 c_j \xi^j,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 B_j \xi^j,
\qquad
\Delta_7(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 d_j \xi^j,
\]
where each \(B_j\in \mathfrak f\) and may be unpacked as
\[
B_j=u_j I+v_j S.
\]

The coefficients you need to force to zero are exactly the **parity-bad** ones:
\[
\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}
=
(c_1,c_3,c_5,c_7;\ B_0,B_2,B_4,B_6,B_8;\ d_0,d_2,d_4,d_6,d_8).
\]
If you can prove
\[
\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0,
\]
then through the needed orders you get
\[
c \text{ even},\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f} \text{ odd},\qquad \Delta_7 \text{ odd}.
\]
That already implies
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}\ \text{even},
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{odd},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}\ \text{even},
\]
which kills the explicit nonmixed bad cases \(n=4,6,8\) and the mixed bad list \((m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\).

So the whole dream-identity route is now a linear algebra problem:

write the normalization equations that define \((c,A_5^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7)\) from the raw centered jet \(R\) as
\[
\Phi(c,A_5^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7;R)=0.
\]

Linearize at the centered base jet:
\[
D\Phi=
\begin{pmatrix}
L_{\mathrm{bad}} & L_{\mathrm{good}} & L_R
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where \(L_{\mathrm{bad}}\) is the block multiplying \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}\), \(L_{\mathrm{good}}\) multiplies the parity-good coefficients, and \(L_R\) multiplies the raw-jet perturbation.

Under centered reflection \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\), the parity-good variables live in
\[
\mathbf p_{\mathrm{good}}
=
(c_0,c_2,c_4,c_6,c_8;\ B_1,B_3,B_5,B_7;\ d_1,d_3,d_5,d_7),
\]
while \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}\) changes sign relative to the desired package.

The strongest usable criterion is this:

> if the reflected normalization equations split into even and odd channels, and the subsystem for \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}\) is homogeneous and invertible, then \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0\).

Concretely, after parity-splitting the equations, you want the “wrong-parity” block to look like
\[
M_{\mathrm{bad}}\,\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0
\]
with
\[
\det M_{\mathrm{bad}}\neq 0.
\]
Then the parity-bad coefficients vanish automatically.

So the exact next computational attack is:

1. Write the raw-to-canonical normalization equations through order \(8\).
2. Expand them in \(\xi\).
3. Separate even and odd parts.
4. Extract the subsystem involving only
   \[
   c_1,c_3,c_5,c_7,\ B_0,B_2,B_4,B_6,B_8,\ d_0,d_2,d_4,d_6,d_8.
   \]
5. Check whether that subsystem is homogeneous and invertible.

That is the finite-jet slice test.

There is also a slightly weaker but easier route that would still be enough: you do not need to kill all parity-bad coefficients. It would already suffice to prove
\[
B_0=B_2=B_4=B_6=B_8=0
\]
through the relevant orders and
\[
d_0=d_2=d_4=d_6=d_8=0,
\]
because that forces \(Y\) odd and \(S\) even through the low orders that generate the dangerous \(4\)-point patterns. If the scalar \(c\) is not fully even but starts with a nonzero constant and no odd terms up to order \(3\), that is already enough for the currently explicit low-order list.

So there are really two targets:

The strong one:
\[
\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0.
\]

The minimal one:
\[
B_0=B_2=B_4=B_6=B_8=0,\qquad d_0=d_2=d_4=d_6=d_8=0,
\]
plus enough low-order vanishing on odd coefficients of \(c\) to keep \(x=v_5/c\) odd through the needed orders.

That is as far as I can take the attack without the actual normalization equations written out explicitly. The next move is to take the normalization conditions from the paper and plug them into this block form.

Here is the next real attack.

Since the current draft still does not expose the raw normalization equations, the best move is to **force the problem into an explicit abstract package** that can later be instantiated. That way, the parity attack becomes a theorem with a finite checklist instead of an amorphous hope.

## 1. Minimal abstract framework you need

Introduce a centered raw one-pair jet space through order \(8\):
\[
\mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}.
\]

An element \(R\in \mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\) should represent the full centered local raw data before the canonical package is extracted.

Introduce a finite-dimensional gauge group
\[
\mathcal G_{\le 8}
\]
acting on \(\mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\), with Lie algebra \(\mathfrak g_{\le 8}\).

Introduce the canonical package space
\[
\mathcal P_{\le 8}
=
\mathcal J_{\le 8}(c)\oplus \mathcal J_{\le 8}(A_5^{\mathfrak f})\oplus \mathcal J_{\le 8}(\Delta_7).
\]

The missing object is a normalization map
\[
\mathcal N:\mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\to \mathcal P_{\le 8},
\qquad
R\mapsto (c,A_5^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7),
\]
defined by explicit equations.

That is the object the paper currently lacks.

## 2. The exact reflection structure to impose

Let
\[
\mathsf T:\mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\to \mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}
\]
be centered reflection \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\) on raw jets.

Let the target involution be
\[
\mathsf T_{\rm can}(c,A,\Delta)
=
\bigl(c(-\xi),-A(-\xi),-\Delta(-\xi)\bigr).
\]

This is the parity package you want.

Then the whole dream identity reduces to proving

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N(\mathsf T R)=\mathsf T_{\rm can}\mathcal N(R)
}
\]
through the low jets.

If \(R\) is reflection-fixed, this gives
\[
\mathcal N(R)=\mathsf T_{\rm can}\mathcal N(R),
\]
hence
\[
c(-\xi)=c(\xi),\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(-\xi)=-A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi),\qquad
\Delta_7(-\xi)=-\Delta_7(\xi).
\]

And then
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}\ \text{even},
\]
so
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{odd},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}\ \text{even}.
\]

That kills the explicit low-order bad list.

## 3. The parity-bad vector

Write the centered jets as
\[
c(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 c_j\xi^j,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 B_j\xi^j,
\qquad
\Delta_7(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 d_j\xi^j.
\]

The coefficients you need to kill are
\[
\mathbf p_{\rm bad}
=
(c_1,c_3,c_5,c_7;\ B_0,B_2,B_4,B_6,B_8;\ d_0,d_2,d_4,d_6,d_8).
\]

A low-jet parity theorem is exactly the statement
\[
\boxed{\mathbf p_{\rm bad}=0.}
\]

That already excludes:

- nonmixed \(n=4,6,8\),
- mixed \((m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\).

## 4. The exact proposition sequence to add to the notes

This is what I would now treat as the real attack package.

### Proposition A. Raw centered jet normalization problem
There exists a finite-dimensional raw centered jet space \(\mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\), a finite-dimensional gauge action \(\mathcal G_{\le 8}\curvearrowright \mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\), and a normalization map
\[
\mathcal N:\mathcal J_{\le 8}^{\rm raw}\to \mathcal P_{\le 8},
\]
whose output is the centered low-jet package \((c,A_5^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7)\).

This is just the missing formal setup.

### Proposition B. Low-jet uniqueness
For raw jets near the centered basepoint, the normalization equations defining \((c,A_5^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7)\) have a unique solution through order \(8\).

This is the finite-dimensional uniqueness you need.

### Proposition C. Reflection-equivariance criterion
If the normalization equations are equivariant under centered reflection, in the sense that reflecting the raw jet and then normalizing gives the same result as normalizing and then applying
\[
(c,A,\Delta)\mapsto(c(-\xi),-A(-\xi),-\Delta(-\xi)),
\]
then every reflection-fixed raw centered jet produces a normalized package satisfying the parity package.

### Corollary D. Vanishing of the parity-bad coefficients
Under Propositions A–C,
\[
\mathbf p_{\rm bad}=0.
\]

### Corollary E. Low-order 4-point exclusion
Under Corollary D, the explicit low-order bad list
\[
n=4,6,8,\qquad (m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)
\]
is impossible.

That is the clean theorem chain.

## 5. The linear algebra test you eventually want

Once the normalization equations are written as
\[
\Phi(p;R)=0,
\]
with
\[
p=(c,A_5^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7),
\]
you linearize at the centered basepoint:
\[
D_p\Phi\cdot \delta p + D_R\Phi\cdot \delta R = 0.
\]

Split \(\delta p\) into parity-good and parity-bad pieces:
\[
\delta p=(\delta p_{\rm good},\delta p_{\rm bad}).
\]

The dream identity through low order reduces to showing that the parity-bad block satisfies a homogeneous invertible system
\[
M_{\rm bad}\,\delta p_{\rm bad}=0,
\qquad
\det M_{\rm bad}\neq 0.
\]

Then
\[
\delta p_{\rm bad}=0.
\]

So the future concrete computation is just: write \(M_{\rm bad}\).

## 6. The strongest current conclusion

The attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The dream-identity route has now been reduced to proving reflection-equivariance and uniqueness of the centered low-jet normalization map.}
}
\]

Not a branch theorem. Not another identity in \(u_5,\Delta_7\). A finite-dimensional normalization theorem.

That is as sharp as this route gets.

The next useful step is to draft these propositions in the paper’s notation as conditional statements, so the future jet computation has a place to land.

Yes. Here is the clean package to add to your attack notes, followed by the direct jet computation.

## 1. The abstract propositions

These are the exact statements the parity route needs.

### Proposition A. Centered low-jet normalization problem
Let \(\mathcal J^{\mathrm{raw}}_{\le 8}\) be the raw centered one-pair jet space through order \(8\), and let \(\mathcal G_{\le 8}\) be the finite-dimensional gauge group acting on it. Let
\[
\mathcal N:\mathcal J^{\mathrm{raw}}_{\le 8}\to \mathcal P_{\le 8}
\]
be a normalization map with target
\[
\mathcal P_{\le 8}
=
\mathcal J_{\le 8}(c)\oplus \mathcal J_{\le 8}(A_5^{\mathfrak f})\oplus \mathcal J_{\le 8}(\Delta_7).
\]

Assume \(\mathcal N\) is defined by explicit normalization equations and is locally unique.

### Proposition B. Low-jet centered reflection equivariance
Let \(\mathsf T\) be centered reflection \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\) on raw jets, and let
\[
\mathsf T_{\mathrm{can}}(c,A,\Delta)
=
\bigl(c(-\xi),-A(-\xi),-\Delta(-\xi)\bigr).
\]
If the normalization equations are reflection-equivariant and the normalized low-jet representative is unique, then
\[
\mathcal N(\mathsf T R)=\mathsf T_{\mathrm{can}}\mathcal N(R).
\]

In particular, for a reflection-fixed centered raw jet \(R\),
\[
c(-\xi)=c(\xi),\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(-\xi)=-A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi),\qquad
\Delta_7(-\xi)=-\Delta_7(\xi)
\]
through order \(8\).

### Corollary C. Low-jet parity package
Writing
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5 I+v_5 S,
\]
the parity package implies, through the needed low orders,
\[
c \text{ even},\qquad u_5 \text{ odd},\qquad v_5 \text{ odd},\qquad \Delta_7 \text{ odd}.
\]

Hence
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}\ \text{even}.
\]

Therefore
\[
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}\ \text{even},
\]
through the low orders relevant to the explicit bad list.

### Corollary D. Low-order \(4\)-point exclusion
Under the low-jet parity package, the nonmixed dangerous cases
\[
n=4,6,8
\]
and the mixed dangerous cases
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)
\]
are excluded.

That is the abstract theorem chain.

---

## 2. Direct jet computation

Now do the computation directly in a centered coordinate \(\xi\).

Write
\[
c(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 c_j\xi^j,
\qquad
u_5(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 u_j\xi^j,
\qquad
v_5(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 v_j\xi^j,
\qquad
\Delta_7(\xi)=\sum_{j=0}^8 d_j\xi^j.
\]

The parity-bad coefficients are
\[
\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}
=
(c_1,c_3,c_5,c_7;\ u_0,u_2,u_4,u_6,u_8;\ v_0,v_2,v_4,v_6,v_8;\ d_0,d_2,d_4,d_6,d_8).
\]

If these vanish, then
\[
c(\xi)=c_0+c_2\xi^2+c_4\xi^4+c_6\xi^6+c_8\xi^8+O(\xi^9),
\]
\[
u_5(\xi)=u_1\xi+u_3\xi^3+u_5\xi^5+u_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
\[
v_5(\xi)=v_1\xi+v_3\xi^3+v_5\xi^5+v_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
\[
\Delta_7(\xi)=d_1\xi+d_3\xi^3+d_5\xi^5+d_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9).
\]

Now expand the normalized quantities.

### 2.1 Expansion of \(x=v_5/c\)

Since \(c_0\neq 0\),
\[
\frac1{c(\xi)}
=
\frac1{c_0}
-\frac{c_2}{c_0^2}\xi^2
+\frac{c_2^2-c_0c_4}{c_0^3}\xi^4
+\frac{-c_2^3+2c_0c_2c_4-c_0^2c_6}{c_0^4}\xi^6
+O(\xi^8).
\]

Multiplying by \(v_5\),
\[
x(\xi)=\frac{v_5}{c}
=
x_1\xi+x_3\xi^3+x_5\xi^5+x_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
with
\[
x_1=\frac{v_1}{c_0},
\]
\[
x_3=\frac{v_3}{c_0}-\frac{c_2v_1}{c_0^2},
\]
\[
x_5=\frac{v_5}{c_0}-\frac{c_2v_3}{c_0^2}+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)v_1}{c_0^3},
\]
\[
x_7=\frac{v_7}{c_0}-\frac{c_2v_5}{c_0^2}
+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)v_3}{c_0^3}
+\frac{(-c_2^3+2c_0c_2c_4-c_0^2c_6)v_1}{c_0^4}.
\]

So with \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0\), \(x\) is automatically odd through order \(7\).

### 2.2 Expansion of \(Y=u_5/c\)

The same reciprocal gives
\[
Y(\xi)=\frac{u_5}{c}
=
y_1\xi+y_3\xi^3+y_5\xi^5+y_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
with
\[
y_1=\frac{u_1}{c_0},
\]
\[
y_3=\frac{u_3}{c_0}-\frac{c_2u_1}{c_0^2},
\]
\[
y_5=\frac{u_5}{c_0}-\frac{c_2u_3}{c_0^2}+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)u_1}{c_0^3},
\]
\[
y_7=\frac{u_7}{c_0}-\frac{c_2u_5}{c_0^2}
+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)u_3}{c_0^3}
+\frac{(-c_2^3+2c_0c_2c_4-c_0^2c_6)u_1}{c_0^4}.
\]

So again, \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0\) forces \(Y\) odd through order \(7\).

### 2.3 Expansion of \(S=\Delta_7/(c\,v_5)\)

First compute
\[
c(\xi)v_5(\xi)
=
g_1\xi+g_3\xi^3+g_5\xi^5+g_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
where
\[
g_1=c_0v_1,
\]
\[
g_3=c_0v_3+c_2v_1,
\]
\[
g_5=c_0v_5+c_2v_3+c_4v_1,
\]
\[
g_7=c_0v_7+c_2v_5+c_4v_3+c_6v_1.
\]

Factor out \(\xi\):
\[
c\,v_5=\xi\,(g_1+g_3\xi^2+g_5\xi^4+g_7\xi^6+O(\xi^8)).
\]

Likewise
\[
\Delta_7(\xi)=\xi\,(d_1+d_3\xi^2+d_5\xi^4+d_7\xi^6+O(\xi^8)).
\]

Therefore
\[
S(\xi)=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
=
s_0+s_2\xi^2+s_4\xi^4+s_6\xi^6+O(\xi^8),
\]
with
\[
s_0=\frac{d_1}{g_1}=\frac{d_1}{c_0v_1},
\]
\[
s_2=\frac{d_3g_1-d_1g_3}{g_1^2},
\]
\[
s_4=\frac{d_5g_1^2-d_3g_1g_3+d_1(g_3^2-g_1g_5)}{g_1^3},
\]
and similarly for \(s_6\).

So \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0\) forces \(S\) even through order \(6\).

This is the key direct jet computation.

---

## 3. What this implies for the \(4\)-point invariants

Now compute
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'.
\]

Since \(Y\) is odd,
\[
Y''(\xi)=6y_3\xi+20y_5\xi^3+42y_7\xi^5+O(\xi^7),
\]
which is odd.

Since \(S\) is even,
\[
S''(\xi)=2s_2+12s_4\xi^2+30s_6\xi^4+O(\xi^6),
\]
which is even.

Hence
\[
\mathcal Z(\xi)=\frac{Y''}{S''}
=
z_1\xi+z_3\xi^3+z_5\xi^5+O(\xi^7),
\]
so \(\mathcal Z\) is odd, and therefore
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\mathcal Z'(\xi)
=
z_1+3z_3\xi^2+5z_5\xi^4+O(\xi^6),
\]
is even.

That is exactly the dream identity through low jets.

---

## 4. Why this kills the explicit dangerous list

### Nonmixed

In the normalized nonmixed chart,
\[
Q_v(\eta)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\eta),\eta,\eta^2\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal R(\eta)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\eta).
\]

If \(\mathcal R\) is even through the relevant low orders, then \(\widetilde Y\) cannot begin in degrees
\[
4,\ 6,\ 8,
\]
so the explicit nonmixed dangerous cases disappear.

### Mixed

If \(Y\) is odd and \(S\) is even through the low orders, then the first nonzero exponent \(n\) in the mixed model
\[
Q_v(\xi)\sim(\xi^n,\xi,\xi^m)
\]
must be odd. Therefore the explicit low-order dangerous mixed list
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)
\]
is impossible.

---

## 5. The exact finite-dimensional target

So the whole low-order \(4\)-point problem really is reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}=0.
}
\]

More explicitly, if the normalization equations force
\[
c_1=c_3=c_5=c_7=0,
\]
\[
u_0=u_2=u_4=u_6=u_8=0,
\qquad
v_0=v_2=v_4=v_6=v_8=0,
\]
\[
d_0=d_2=d_4=d_6=d_8=0,
\]
then the explicit low-order dangerous \(4\)-point obstruction list is gone.

So the next actual computation is exactly what I said before:

1. write the normalization equations through order \(8\),
2. linearize them in centered coordinates,
3. isolate the subsystem for those parity-bad coefficients,
4. check whether it is homogeneous and invertible.

That is now completely concrete.

The main thing we gained by doing the jet computation directly is that you can now see exactly how the parity package propagates through
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
and therefore exactly why killing \(\mathbf p_{\mathrm{bad}}\) is enough.

## Main new conclusion

For the low-order \(4\)-point parity attack, the only coefficients you really need to control are the parity-bad jets of
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Delta_7.
\]

The scalar \(c\) is not the main obstruction.

Why? Because in the current file:

- \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is already the canonical first residual fixed-sector datum;
- \(\Delta_7\) is already canonical and gauge-invariant under the symmetry-preserving normalization gauge;
- and on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, the lifted \(4\)-point branch is built from
  \[
  x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
  Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
  S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
  \]

So once \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S\) and \(\Delta_7\) have the right odd/even low jets, the induced parities of \(x,Y,S\) follow formally up to the needed order, regardless of the full all-orders behavior of \(c\), provided \(c(0)\neq 0\) and no odd terms of \(c\) enter below the orders you care about.

That shifts the attack.

---

## 1. What the current equations already tell you

From the current draft, the exact gauge laws are:

\[
A_5^{\rm new}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3],
\]
and on the first residual quotient the scalar renormalization disappears, leaving only the normalization shadow from the commutator sector.

At septic order, under symmetry-preserving gauge,
\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\rm new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
but
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is gauge-invariant.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_7 \text{ is already canonical, and its parity-bad coefficients cannot be removed by the existing symmetry-preserving gauge.}
}
\]

That is important. It means any low-order parity theorem for \(\Delta_7\) must come from raw/source symmetry, not from gauge choices.

Likewise \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is already the canonical fixed-sector quotient datum. So its parity-bad jets are also intrinsic at the current stage.

Thus the dream-identity route is **not** about choosing a better gauge inside the present package. It is about proving a deeper symmetry of the canonical package itself.

---

## 2. The minimal low-jet target

You do **not** need to kill every parity-bad coefficient of \(c\).

The explicit low-order dangerous \(4\)-point list disappears already if you can prove:

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)=B_1\xi+B_3\xi^3+B_5\xi^5+B_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
and
\[
\Delta_7(\xi)=d_1\xi+d_3\xi^3+d_5\xi^5+d_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9),
\]
in a centered coordinate, together with only the weak scalar condition
\[
c(\xi)=c_0+c_1\xi+c_2\xi^2+\cdots,
\qquad c_0\neq 0.
\]

Because then:

- \(u_5,v_5\) start in odd order;
- so
  \[
  x=\frac{v_5}{c}
  =
  \frac{1}{c_0}\bigl(v_1\xi+v_3\xi^3+v_5\xi^5+\cdots\bigr)+O(\xi^2\cdot \text{odd}),
  \]
  and after re-centering/inverting the local odd coordinate, \(x\) is an odd local parameter to the needed low order;

- similarly
  \[
  Y=\frac{u_5}{c}
  \]
  has no even terms through degree \(8\);

- and
  \[
  S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
  \]
  is even through the relevant low orders because odd divided by odd has even leading parity, and the scalar denominator contributes only even corrections at the orders that matter once you re-expand in the odd parameter \(x\).

So the concrete low-order theorem you really need is:

\[
\boxed{
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ odd through degree }7
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Delta_7\text{ odd through degree }7
\text{ in a centered coordinate.}
}
\]

That is enough to kill:

- nonmixed \(n=4,6,8\),
- mixed \((m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\).

This is a sharper target than the full package parity theorem.

---

## 3. Why this is the right simplification

Because the current file already shows:

- \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is the canonical quintic fixed-sector residual;
- \(\Delta_7\) is the canonical septic scalar residual;
- and the lifted \(4\)-point branch only sees those objects via
  \[
  Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
  \]

So if a centered reflection theorem exists, the first meaningful statement to try to prove is not the whole slice theorem, but simply:

\[
\boxed{
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(-\xi)=-A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)+O(\xi^9),
\qquad
\Delta_7(-\xi)=-\Delta_7(\xi)+O(\xi^9).
}
\]

That is the finite-jet form of the dream identity.

---

## 4. What the current symmetry already gives — and why it is not enough

The current draft proves that the **raw cubic-normalized swap-symmetric quintic slice** is anti-fixed under the symmetric-placement involution. That is:

\[
J_0A_5J_0=-A_5
\]
at the raw level.

This is not the same as saying
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(-\xi)=-A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)
\]
in a centered local coordinate. But it does suggest something:

the quintic fixed-sector residual already lies in a sign-changing channel under the built-in involution.

So the most promising refinement is:

> can the current swap-symmetric anti-fixed law be transported, after centering and passage to the canonical fixed-sector package, into oddness of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) in the centered coordinate?

Likewise, on the septic side, the current file proves that \(\Delta_7\) comes only from transport-level sectors and that pure same-point septic pieces cancel out. That is also consistent with oddness, but far from enough to prove it.

So the next serious attack is:

- strengthen the anti-fixed quintic law into a **centered oddness law** for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\),
- strengthen the transport-only septic statement into a **centered oddness law** for \(\Delta_7\).

That is the concrete finite-jet version of the dream identity.

---

## 5. The strongest concrete target now

The attack is now reduced to these two finite-jet propositions:

### Quintic finite-jet oddness theorem
In a centered local coordinate \(\xi\),
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)=B_1\xi+B_3\xi^3+B_5\xi^5+B_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9).
\]

### Septic finite-jet oddness theorem
In the same centered coordinate,
\[
\Delta_7(\xi)=d_1\xi+d_3\xi^3+d_5\xi^5+d_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9).
\]

If both hold, the currently explicit low-order dangerous \(4\)-point list is gone.

That is now the sharpest thing I can honestly say.

## 6. Bottom line

So the attack has moved the goalposts in a useful way:

You do **not** need the full raw normalization equations yet.

You do **not** need a complete parity theorem for \(c\).

You need a centered finite-jet oddness theorem for the two canonical residual objects
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Delta_7.
\]

That is the next exact thing to hunt.

If you want, I can next formalize these two propositions and try to derive the first few coefficients that must vanish from the current anti-fixed / transport-only statements, to see whether any partial oddness is already forced.

## 1. What you can prove right now from the existing septic analysis

The current draft proves two facts:

First, pure same-point septic contributions are even in the transport parameter \(s\) and vanish in the odd two-point germ. That is exactly Lemma `parity-elimination-pure-septic`. 

Second, the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\)-part of \(\Delta_7\) comes entirely from the direct \(K_1\)-transport sector:
\[
[\Delta_7]^{[1]}=[\Delta_{7,K_1}]^{[1]}.
\]
That is Corollary `weight-one-septic-reduction`. 

Those two statements together give a real partial parity consequence:

### Partial septic oddness theorem
In the centered transport/separation variable \(s\),
\[
\boxed{
[\Delta_7]^{[1]}(s)\ \text{is odd in }s.
}
\]

### Why this is true
The odd two-point germ is defined by projection to the odd part under
\[
s\mapsto -s.
\]
The weight-one piece of \(\Delta_7\) survives only through the \(K_1\)-transport channel, which is part of that odd germ, while all pure same-point septic terms vanish because they are even in \(s\). So the surviving weight-one scalar must itself lie in the odd channel.

Equivalently, its Taylor expansion has only odd powers:
\[
[\Delta_7]^{[1]}(s)=\alpha_1 s+\alpha_3 s^3+\alpha_5 s^5+\cdots.
\]

That is a real theorem already latent in the file.

## 2. What this does and does not buy you

It gives a useful but limited consequence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The highest-new septic contribution cannot be responsible for any even-power low-order obstruction in the centered separation variable.}
}
\]

So, for example, the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\) piece of \(\Delta_7\) cannot contribute a constant, quadratic, quartic, or sextic term in that centered variable.

But this is **not** enough to kill the dangerous \(4\)-point patterns, because:

- it controls only \([\Delta_7]^{[1]}\), not the full \(\Delta_7\);
- it says nothing yet about the low-order parity of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\);
- and the dangerous low-order nonmixed/mixed patterns are about the full canonical package after normalization, not only the highest-new septic slice.

So this is real progress, but only partial.

The tempting parallel statement would be:

A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\ \text{odd in the centered variable }s.
\]

But the current file does **not** prove that.

What it proves is the raw anti-fixed symmetry
\[
J_0A_5J_0=-A_5
\]
for the cubic-normalized swap-symmetric raw corrected germ. That is Lemma `raw-quintic-slice-antifixed`. 

This is a symmetry in the **matrix channel**, not an oddness theorem in the centered source coordinate. It gives tracelessness and anti-fixedness, but it does **not** imply
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(-s)=-A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s).
\]

So at the moment, there is no centered finite-jet oddness theorem for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) available from the current draft.

}

but

That means the parity route is still blocked at exactly the same place:

  not just for the highest-new septic piece.

Try to show that

through the orders relevant to

In other words: isolate not the full package, but the **parity-bad part modulo the already-understood lower channels**.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 01:23:14)

I’m going straight into the current TeX now to see whether the lower-weight septic sectors are explicit enough to extend the oddness of \([\Delta_7]^{[1]}\), or whether we hit a real missing-definition wall.

_Thought for 2m 13s_

I found an important correction, and it sharpens the whole parity attack.

## Main attack result: the earlier parity package was miscentered

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, one has
\[
v_5(0)\neq 0.
\]
So the earlier dream package
\[
c \text{ even},\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ odd},\qquad \Delta_7\text{ odd}
\]
in a centered coordinate \(\xi\) cannot literally be right on that patch, because “\(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) odd” would force \(v_5(0)=0\).

So the correct parity target is **not** parity of the raw package itself. It is parity of the **affinely centered normalized variables**.

That is a real correction, and it matters.

---

# 1. The correct centered variables

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c}.
\]

Fix the basepoint \(h_0\), and write
\[
x_0:=x(h_0).
\]
The correctly centered first coordinate is
\[
\widehat x:=x-x_0.
\]

This is the thing that should be odd, not \(x\) itself and certainly not \(v_5\) itself.

Likewise, since coplanarity is unchanged by
\[
Y\mapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S,
\]
the correctly centered first lifted component is not \(Y\) itself but its class modulo
\[
\operatorname{span}\{1,\widehat x,S\}.
\]

So the dream identity has to be reformulated in terms of:

- \(\widehat x\),
- \(\lambda\) or \(S\),
- and \(Y\) modulo \(\operatorname{span}\{1,\widehat x,S\}\).

---

# 2. Corrected sufficient parity package

Here is the **right** finite-jet package that would suffice.

In a centered coordinate \(\xi\), assume:

### (P1) \(c\) is even
\[
c(-\xi)=c(\xi).
\]

### (P2) the centered first coordinate is odd
\[
\widehat x(\xi)=x(\xi)-x_0
=
\frac{v_5(\xi)}{c(\xi)}-x_0
\]
is odd.

Equivalently,
\[
v_5(\xi)-x_0\,c(\xi)
\]
is odd.

### (P3) \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) is even
\[
\lambda(-\xi)=\lambda(\xi).
\]

Since \(S=\lambda/c\), this implies
\[
S(-\xi)=S(\xi),
\]
because even divided by even is even.

### (P4) \(Y\) is odd modulo the affine gauge
There exist constants \(\alpha,\beta,\gamma\) such that
\[
\widetilde Y(\xi):=Y(\xi)-\alpha-\beta \widehat x(\xi)-\gamma S(\xi)
\]
is odd.

---

# 3. Why this is the correct dream identity

Under (P1)–(P4),

- \(\widehat x\) is odd;
- \(S\) is even;
- \(\widetilde Y\) is odd.

Therefore
\[
\widetilde Y'' \text{ is odd},\qquad S'' \text{ is even},
\]
so
\[
\mathcal Z:=\frac{\widetilde Y''}{S''}
\]
is odd, and hence
\[
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
\]
is even.

So this corrected package implies exactly the dream identity you want, but in the **right centered form**.

---

# 4. Consequences for the explicit low-order bad list

This corrected package kills the currently dangerous low-order \(4\)-point list.

## Nonmixed

In the nonmixed normalization,
\[
Q_v(\eta)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\eta),\,\eta,\,\eta^2\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal R(\eta)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\eta).
\]

If \(\widetilde Y\) is odd, then its first nonzero degree is odd, so the bad cases
\[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8
\]
are impossible.

Equivalently, \(\mathcal R\) is even, so
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\notin\{1,3,5\}.
\]

## Mixed

If \(\widetilde Y\) is odd, then the first exponent \(n\) is odd.  
If \(S\) is even, then the first exponent \(m\) is even.

So the explicit mixed low-order dangerous list
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
is impossible.

Thus the corrected parity package still kills the full explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list.

---

# 5. The correct finite-jet coefficient form

Now write the centered jets through the needed orders.

### Even scalar
\[
c(\xi)=c_0+c_2\xi^2+c_4\xi^4+c_6\xi^6+O(\xi^8).
\]

### Centered odd first coordinate
\[
x(\xi)=x_0+x_1\xi+x_3\xi^3+x_5\xi^5+x_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
v_5(\xi)=x_0\,c(\xi)+b_1\xi+b_3\xi^3+b_5\xi^5+b_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9).
\]

### Even \(\lambda\)
\[
\lambda(\xi)=\lambda_0+\lambda_2\xi^2+\lambda_4\xi^4+\lambda_6\xi^6+O(\xi^8).
\]

Then
\[
S(\xi)=\frac{\lambda(\xi)}{c(\xi)}
=s_0+s_2\xi^2+s_4\xi^4+s_6\xi^6+O(\xi^8)
\]
is even.

### Odd \(Y\) modulo the affine gauge
\[
Y(\xi)=\alpha+\beta \widehat x(\xi)+\gamma S(\xi)+y_1\xi+y_3\xi^3+y_5\xi^5+y_7\xi^7+O(\xi^9).
\]

This is the **actual** low-jet parity theorem you want.

Not oddness of raw \(v_5\) or raw \(\Delta_7\).  
Oddness/evenness of the **centered normalized variables**.

---

# 6. Why this is better than the earlier package

Because it is compatible with the actual geometry of a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch.

At the basepoint:

- \(c(0)\neq 0\),
- \(v_5(0)\neq 0\),
- so \(x(0)=x_0\neq\) necessarily \(0\).

The correct symmetry is therefore around the **centered coordinate**
\[
\widehat x=x-x_0,
\]
not around raw \(v_5\).

Similarly, the first lifted coordinate is only meaningful modulo
\[
\operatorname{span}\{1,\widehat x,S\},
\]
so oddness of raw \(Y\) is too strong; oddness of \(Y\) modulo this gauge is the right statement.

That is the corrected dream identity.

---

# 7. What remains to prove

The whole attack has now become:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove the centered low-jet parity package for }
c,\ \widehat x,\ \lambda,\ Y \bmod \operatorname{span}\{1,\widehat x,S\}.
}
\]

This is much sharper than the previous naive parity package.

And importantly, this is the one you can actually hope to get from a centered reflection-equivariant normalization theorem.

---

# 8. The strongest next theorem target

So the next exact theorem should be:

### Centered low-jet reflection theorem
In a centered coordinate \(\xi\), the canonical normalized one-pair package satisfies, through the low orders needed for the dangerous \(4\)-point list,

\[
c(\xi)\ \text{even},
\qquad
x(\xi)-x_0\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\lambda(\xi)=\frac{\Delta_7(\xi)}{v_5(\xi)}\ \text{even},
\]
and
\[
Y(\xi)-\alpha-\beta(x(\xi)-x_0)-\gamma S(\xi)\ \text{odd}
\]
for suitable constants \(\alpha,\beta,\gamma\).

If that theorem holds, the explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is gone.

---

So the attack did produce a real correction and a more accurate target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The dream identity should be formulated in the centered normalized variables }(\widehat x,\lambda,Y\bmod\{1,\widehat x,S\}),\ \text{not in the raw package }(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7).
}
\]

That is the correct next thing to prove.

_Thought for 5m 56s_

I pushed the computation directly, and I found a genuinely useful new package of **exact low-jet obstruction coefficients** for the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch.

This is not in the paper, and it is the sharpest concrete attack I can currently extract from the existing framework.

---

## 1. The right finite-jet object on the nonmixed branch

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, let
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\qquad
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\qquad
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.
\]

At a **nonmixed** point, \(S''(0)\neq 0\), so \(\mathcal Z\) is analytic.

Now \(\mathcal Z\) is **not** fully gauge-invariant: under the affine coplanarity gauge
\[
Y\mapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S
\]
one has
\[
\mathcal Z\mapsto \mathcal Z+\gamma.
\]
So only the **constant term** of \(\mathcal Z\) is gauge-dependent. All higher Taylor coefficients of \(\mathcal Z\) are gauge-invariant.

That means the true nonmixed finite-jet obstructions are the even Taylor coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6
\]
in the expansion
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=z_0+z_1x+z_2x^2+z_3x^3+z_4x^4+z_5x^5+z_6x^6+O(x^7).
\]

These are canonical.

And they are exactly what govern the dangerous low-order nonmixed list:

- \(n=4\) iff \(z_2\neq 0\),
- \(n=6\) iff \(z_2=0\) but \(z_4\neq 0\),
- \(n=8\) iff \(z_2=z_4=0\) but \(z_6\neq 0\).

Equivalently, since
\[
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z',
\]
these correspond to odd-order zeros of \(\mathcal R\) of orders \(1,3,5\).

So the whole nonmixed low-order problem reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
z_2=z_4=z_6=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest exact finite-jet target.

---

## 2. Exact formulas for \(z_2,z_4,z_6\)

Write the local \(x\)-jets of \(S\) and \(Y\) at the nonmixed point as
\[
s_k:=S^{(k)}(0),\qquad y_k:=Y^{(k)}(0),
\qquad s_2\neq 0.
\]

Then by direct Taylor division of
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\]
the first three even gauge-invariant coefficients are:

### Quadratic obstruction
\[
\boxed{
z_2=
\frac{
s_2^2y_4-2s_2s_3y_3+\bigl(2s_3^2-s_2s_4\bigr)y_2
}{
2\,s_2^3
}.
}
\]

### Quartic obstruction
\[
\boxed{
z_4=
\frac{
s_2^4y_6
-s_2^3(4s_3y_5+6s_4y_4+4s_5y_3+s_6y_2)
+2s_2^2(6s_3^2y_4+12s_3s_4y_3+4s_3s_5y_2+3s_4^2y_2)
-12s_2s_3^2(2s_3y_3+3s_4y_2)
+24s_3^4y_2
}{
24\,s_2^5
}.
}
\]

### Sextic obstruction
\[
\boxed{
z_6=
\frac{\mathcal P_8(s_2,\dots,s_8;y_2,\dots,y_8)}{720\,s_2^7},
}
\]
where
\[
\begin{aligned}
\mathcal P_8
={}&
s_2^6y_8
-s_2^5(6s_3y_7+15s_4y_6+20s_5y_5+15s_6y_4+6s_7y_3+s_8y_2)\\
&\quad
+2s_2^4(15s_3^2y_6+60s_3s_4y_5+60s_3s_5y_4+30s_3s_6y_3+6s_3s_7y_2
+45s_4^2y_4+60s_4s_5y_3+15s_4s_6y_2+10s_5^2y_2)\\
&\quad
-30s_2^3(4s_3^3y_5+18s_3^2s_4y_4+12s_3^2s_5y_3+3s_3^2s_6y_2
+18s_3s_4^2y_3+12s_3s_4s_5y_2+3s_4^3y_2)\\
&\quad
+120s_2^2s_3^2(3s_3^2y_4+12s_3s_4y_3+4s_3s_5y_2+9s_4^2y_2)\\
&\quad
-360s_2s_3^4(2s_3y_3+5s_4y_2)
+720s_3^6y_2.
\end{aligned}
\]

These formulas are exact.

And now the nonmixed low-order 4-point problem has been reduced to a finite list of polynomial identities:

\[
\boxed{
z_2=0,\qquad z_4=0,\qquad z_6=0.
}
\]

That is much sharper than “prove a parity theorem.”

---

## 3. Check against the normalized nonmixed chart

In the normalized nonmixed chart
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
you have
\[
S(\xi)=\xi^2,
\qquad
s_2=2,\qquad
s_3=s_4=s_5=\cdots=0.
\]

Then the obstruction formulas collapse to
\[
z_2=\frac{y_4}{4},
\qquad
z_4=\frac{y_6}{48},
\qquad
z_6=\frac{y_8}{1440}.
\]

So these really are the coordinate-free versions of the naive conditions
\[
y_4=y_6=y_8=0.
\]

That is exactly what you wanted: explicit nonmixed low-order jet obstructions written in arbitrary \(x\)-coordinates, not just in the fully normalized chart.

---

## 4. Mixed branch: what you can still say exactly

At a mixed point, \(S''(0)=0\), so the Taylor coefficients \(z_2,z_4,z_6\) do not make sense directly.

But the ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}
\]
still controls the branch, and the dangerous mixed low-order list is exactly
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\},
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)\in\{(1,0),(1,2),(2,1)\}.
\]

In terms of raw \(Y\)-jets:

- if \(r=1\), then \(S''\sim s_3x\), and the dangerous cases are
  \[
  \ord_0 Y''=2 \quad\text{or}\quad 4,
  \]
  i.e.
  \[
  y_2=y_3=0,\ y_4\neq0
  \quad\text{or}\quad
  y_2=y_3=y_4=y_5=0,\ y_6\neq0;
  \]

- if \(r=2\), then \(S''\sim \frac12 s_4x^2\), and the dangerous case is
  \[
  \ord_0 Y''=4,
  \]
  i.e.
  \[
  y_2=y_3=y_4=y_5=0,\ y_6\neq0.
  \]

So the mixed low-order obstruction list is also a finite jet problem, but because \(S''(0)=0\), the right invariants are order conditions on the quotient \(\mathcal Z\), not the finite coefficients \(z_2,z_4,z_6\).

---

## 5. The real upshot

This is the strongest attack result I can give now:

### Nonmixed branch
The low-order dangerous cases are governed by the three exact gauge-invariant obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6
\]
given above.

To kill the explicit nonmixed bad list, it is enough to prove
\[
z_2=z_4=z_6=0.
\]

### Mixed branch
The low-order dangerous cases are governed by the order conditions
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

To kill the explicit mixed bad list, it is enough to prove these three order patterns cannot occur.

So the parity route has now been reduced to a **finite polynomial obstruction problem** on the nonmixed side and a **finite order-gap problem** on the mixed side.

That is much more concrete than before.

---

## 6. Honest limit

What I still **cannot** do from the current file is prove
\[
z_2=z_4=z_6=0
\]
or rule out the mixed order patterns. The draft still does not contain the RH-specific source/matrix-level identities needed for that.

But now the attack has fully isolated the exact coefficients and order conditions that must be killed.

If you want, the next thing I can do is formalize these \(z_2,z_4,z_6\) as named invariants and derive their transformation behavior under the remaining normalization freedoms, so we can see whether any of them already vanish for structural reasons.

**the present draft lets you prove only a partial oddness statement for the septic side, and it does not let you upgrade that to full low-jet oddness of either \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) or \(\Delta_7\).** The obstruction is real: the file gives parity elimination for pure same-point septic terms and reduction of the weight-one septic slice to the direct transport channel, but it does not expose the remaining lower-weight septic sectors explicitly enough to control their parity. 

What you can prove now is this:

Let \(s\) be the centered transport/separation variable. Then the current file’s septic analysis implies
\[
[\Delta_7]^{[1]}(s)
\]
is odd in \(s\). The reason is exactly the combination of:
pure same-point septic pieces are even and therefore vanish in the odd two-point germ, while the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\) part is entirely carried by the direct \(K_1\)-transport sector. So
\[
[\Delta_7]^{[1]}(s)=\alpha_1 s+\alpha_3 s^3+\alpha_5 s^5+\cdots.
\]
That is a real theorem already latent in the file. 

The analogous statement for the quintic side does **not** follow from the current anti-fixed lemma. What the file proves there is the raw matrix symmetry
\[
J_0A_5J_0=-A_5,
\]
which is a statement in the anti-fixed representation channel, not an oddness theorem in a centered source coordinate. So at present there is no theorem in the file implying
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(-s)=-A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s).
\]
That is why the parity route still stalls on the quintic side. 

So the strongest direct attack result from the current file is:

\[
\boxed{
[\Delta_7]^{[1]} \text{ is odd in the centered separation variable,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current draft does not yet force full low-jet oddness of }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ or }\Delta_7.
}
\]

From there, the right next move is not another generic branch argument. It is to isolate the **first parity-bad low jets** and target them directly.

Here is the clean finite-jet target in centered coordinate \(\xi\):

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(\xi)=B_0+B_1\xi+B_2\xi^2+B_3\xi^3+B_4\xi^4+B_5\xi^5+B_6\xi^6+B_7\xi^7+\cdots,
\]
\[
\Delta_7(\xi)=d_0+d_1\xi+d_2\xi^2+d_3\xi^3+d_4\xi^4+d_5\xi^5+d_6\xi^6+d_7\xi^7+\cdots.
\]

The coefficients you need to kill are exactly
\[
B_0,B_2,B_4,B_6
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
d_0,d_2,d_4,d_6.
\]

If those vanish, then through the relevant low orders:

- \(u_5,v_5\) are odd,
- \(\Delta_7\) is odd,
- and after passing to
  \[
  x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
  Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
  S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
  \]
  the nonmixed bad list \(n=4,6,8\) and the mixed bad list \((m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\) disappear.

So the concrete sharpened theorem targets are:

\[
\boxed{
B_0=B_2=B_4=B_6=0,
}
\qquad
\boxed{
d_0=d_2=d_4=d_6=0.
}
\]

Those are strictly weaker than full all-orders parity, and they are enough for the current low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list.

What is missing from the file to prove those vanishings is explicit control of:

1. the lower-weight septic sectors beyond \([\Delta_7]^{[1]}\),
2. the way the anti-fixed raw quintic slice passes into the canonical fixed-sector residual \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\),
3. or a centered reflection-equivariant normalization theorem.

So the attack has now reduced the parity route to a very finite problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{kill the first even coefficients of }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ and }\Delta_7.
}

That is the sharpest thing the current file supports.

## We can now write the **mixed low-order obstruction coefficients explicitly**

This is the mixed analogue of the nonmixed coefficients \(z_2,z_4,z_6\). It is the sharpest concrete attack I can extract from the present framework.

Work in the local \(x\)-coordinate on a good \(v_5\)-patch, and write
\[
S''(x)=\sum_{j\ge 0}\frac{s_{j+2}}{j!}x^j,\qquad
Y''(x)=\sum_{j\ge 0}\frac{y_{j+2}}{j!}x^j,
\]
where
\[
s_k=S^{(k)}(0),\qquad y_k=Y^{(k)}(0).
\]

Recall
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''},\qquad \mathcal R=\mathcal Z'.
\]

## 1. Mixed case \(r=1\)

Here
\[
\ord_0 K_v=1
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
s_2=0,\ s_3\neq 0.
\]
So
\[
S''(x)=s_3x+\frac{s_4}{2}x^2+\frac{s_5}{6}x^3+\frac{s_6}{24}x^4+\cdots.
\]

A direct division gives
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{y_2}{s_3}\frac1x
+
\left(\frac{y_3}{s_3}-\frac{s_4y_2}{2s_3^2}\right)
+
\kappa_{1,1}\,x
+
\kappa_{1,2}\,x^2
+
\kappa_{1,3}\,x^3
+O(x^4),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{1,1}
=
\frac{y_4}{2s_3}
-\frac{s_4y_3}{2s_3^2}
-\frac{s_5y_2}{6s_3^2}
+\frac{s_4^2y_2}{4s_3^3},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{1,2}
=
\frac{y_5}{6s_3}
-\frac{s_4y_4}{4s_3^2}
-\frac{s_5y_3}{6s_3^2}
-\frac{s_6y_2}{24s_3^2}
+\frac{s_4^2y_3}{4s_3^3}
+\frac{s_4s_5y_2}{6s_3^3}
-\frac{s_4^3y_2}{8s_3^4},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\kappa_{1,3}
={}&
\frac{y_6}{24s_3}
-\frac{s_4y_5}{12s_3^2}
-\frac{s_5y_4}{12s_3^2}
-\frac{s_6y_3}{24s_3^2}
+\frac{s_4^2y_4}{8s_3^3}
+\frac{s_4s_5y_3}{6s_3^3} \\
&\quad
+\frac{s_4s_6y_2}{24s_3^3}
+\frac{s_5^2y_2}{36s_3^3}
-\frac{s_4^3y_3}{8s_3^4}
-\frac{s_4^2s_5y_2}{8s_3^4}
+\frac{s_4^4y_2}{16s_3^5}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

Now the dangerous mixed low-order patterns for \(r=1\) are exactly:

- \(\ord_0\mathcal Z=1\), which after the necessary analyticity conditions \(y_2=y_3=0\) becomes

  \]

  \[
  \boxed{\kappa_{1,3}=\frac{y_6}{24s_3}\neq 0.}
  \]

So the two dangerous \(r=1\) cases reduce to the two explicit coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3}.
\]

Equivalently, killing the mixed low-order \(r=1\) branch means proving
\[
\boxed{\kappa_{1,1}=0,\qquad \kappa_{1,3}=0.}
\]

## 2. Mixed case \(r=2\)

Here
\[
\ord_0 K_v=2
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
s_2=s_3=0,\ s_4\neq 0.
\]
So
\[
S''(x)=\frac{s_4}{2}x^2+\frac{s_5}{6}x^3+\frac{s_6}{24}x^4+\cdots.
\]

A direct division gives
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{2y_2}{s_4}\frac1{x^2}
+
\left(\frac{2y_3}{s_4}-\frac{2s_5y_2}{3s_4^2}\right)\frac1x
+
\left(
\frac{y_4}{s_4}
-\frac{2s_5y_3}{3s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_2}{6s_4^2}
+\frac{2s_5^2y_2}{9s_4^3}
\right)
+\kappa_{2,1}x+\kappa_{2,2}x^2+O(x^3),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,1}
=
\frac{y_5}{3s_4}
-\frac{s_5y_4}{3s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_3}{6s_4^2}
+\frac{2s_5^2y_3}{9s_4^3},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{y_6}{12s_4}
-\frac{s_5y_5}{9s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_4}{12s_4^2}
+\frac{s_5^2y_4}{9s_4^3}.
}
\]

The dangerous mixed low-order case for \(r=2\) is exactly
\[
\ord_0\mathcal Z=2,
\]
which after the necessary analyticity/vanishing conditions
\[
y_2=y_3=y_4=y_5=0
\]
becomes
\[
\boxed{\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{y_6}{12s_4}\neq 0.}
\]

So the dangerous \(r=2\) case is governed by the single coefficient
\[
\kappa_{2,2}.
\]

Equivalently, killing the mixed low-order \(r=2\) branch means proving
\[
\boxed{\kappa_{2,2}=0.}
\]

---

## 3. Sharp finite list of mixed jet obstructions

So the mixed low-order \(4\)-point problem has now been reduced to three exact coefficients:

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]

More precisely:

- \((m,n)=(3,4)\) is equivalent to \(\kappa_{1,1}\neq 0\),
- \((m,n)=(3,6)\) is equivalent to \(\kappa_{1,3}\neq 0\),
- \((m,n)=(4,6)\) is equivalent to \(\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0\).

So to kill the explicit mixed dangerous list, it is enough to prove
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{1,1}=\kappa_{1,3}=\kappa_{2,2}=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest mixed finite-jet target I can currently derive.

---

## 4. Comparison with the nonmixed side

Earlier we reduced the nonmixed low-order bad list to the three gauge-invariant coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]

Now we have the mixed side reduced to
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

So the entire explicit low-order \(4\)-point endgame has been reduced to a **finite list of six exact jet coefficients**:

\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]

That is the sharpest concrete attack result so far.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 02:08:28)

I’m going into the actual TeX now to extract the explicit \(K_1\)-transport ingredients and set up a centered local parameter so we can at least write the Taylor-coefficient groundwork cleanly, even if the draft does not yet name those coefficients.

_Thought for 2m 46s_

Yes. Here is the actual groundwork you can use.

The right move is to work in the **centered symmetric-placement variable**
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
and treat \(s\mapsto -s\) as swapping the two microscopic points. Then every \(2\times 2\) symmetric coefficient matrix
\[
X_n(s)=\begin{pmatrix}a_n(s)&b_n(s)\\ b_n(s)&c_n(s)\end{pmatrix}
\]
satisfies
\[
a_n(-s)=c_n(s),\qquad b_n(-s)=b_n(s),\qquad c_n(-s)=a_n(s).
\]

So define the even/odd half-sum/half-difference variables
\[
\bar a_n:=\frac{a_n+c_n}{2}\quad\text{(even)},\qquad
\delta a_n:=\frac{c_n-a_n}{2}\quad\text{(odd)},
\]
and similarly for every diagonal pair, while the off-diagonal entry is always even.

Concretely, for the matrices already in the paper:
\[
X_1=\begin{pmatrix}u&v\\v&w\end{pmatrix},\quad
X_2=\begin{pmatrix}a&b\\b&c\end{pmatrix},\quad
X_4=\begin{pmatrix}p&r\\r&s\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
X_5=\begin{pmatrix}\alpha_5&\beta_5\\ \beta_5&\gamma_5\end{pmatrix},\quad
X_6=\begin{pmatrix}\mu_6&\nu_6\\ \nu_6&\lambda_6\end{pmatrix},
\]
set
\[
\bar u=\frac{u+w}{2},\quad \delta u=\frac{u-w}{2},\qquad
\bar a=\frac{a+c}{2},\quad \delta a=\frac{c-a}{2},
\]
\[
\bar p=\frac{p+s}{2},\quad \delta p=\frac{p-s}{2},\qquad
\bar\alpha_5=\frac{\alpha_5+\gamma_5}{2},\quad \delta\alpha_5=\frac{\gamma_5-\alpha_5}{2},
\]
\[
\bar\mu_6=\frac{\mu_6+\lambda_6}{2},\quad \delta\mu_6=\frac{\lambda_6-\mu_6}{2},
\]
and for the baseline diagonal block
\[
X_0=\diag(x_1,x_2),\qquad
\bar x=\frac{x_1+x_2}{2},\quad \delta x=\frac{x_2-x_1}{2}.
\]

Then the parity is:

- even:
\[
\bar x,\ \bar u,\ v,\ \bar a,\ b,\ \bar p,\ r,\ \bar\alpha_5,\ \beta_5,\ \bar\mu_6,\ \nu_6
\]
- odd:
\[
\delta x,\ \delta u,\ \delta a,\ \delta p,\ \delta\alpha_5,\ \delta\mu_6.
\]

That much is formal from centered symmetric placement.

Now rewrite the canonical quintic and septic transport formulas in these variables.

## 1. Quintic fixed-sector package

From the file,
\[
u_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=v(\gamma-\alpha)+\beta(u-w),
\qquad
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=\gamma u-\alpha w.
\]

Using
\[
\gamma-\alpha=2\,\delta\alpha,\qquad
u-w=2\,\delta u,
\]
and
\[
\gamma u-\alpha w
=
2(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\delta\alpha\,\bar u),
\]
you get
\[
\boxed{
u_5=2\bigl(v\,\delta\alpha+\beta\,\delta u\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
v_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\delta\alpha\,\bar u\bigr).
}
\]

So both \(u_5\) and \(v_5\) are **odd functions of \(s\)**.

This is the first real Taylor groundwork fact.

Write the even variables as
\[
E(s)=E_0+E_2 s^2+E_4 s^4+E_6 s^6+\cdots
\]
and the odd variables as
\[
O(s)=O_1 s+O_3 s^3+O_5 s^5+O_7 s^7+\cdots.
\]

Then
\[
u_5(s)=U_1 s+U_3 s^3+U_5 s^5+U_7 s^7+\cdots
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
U_3=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_3+v_2\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_3+\beta_2\,\delta u_1\bigr),
}
\]
and similarly
\[
\boxed{
U_5=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_5+v_2\,\delta\alpha_3+v_4\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_5+\beta_2\,\delta u_3+\beta_4\,\delta u_1\bigr).
}
\]

Likewise
\[
v_5(s)=V_1 s+V_3 s^3+V_5 s^5+V_7 s^7+\cdots
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
V_1=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_0\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V_3=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_0\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_5+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_4\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_4+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u_0\bigr).
}
\]

So the quintic canonical package has a fully explicit **odd Taylor expansion** in centered \(s\).

## 2. Septic \(K_1\)-transport package

From the exact formulas in the file,
\[
u_{7,K_1}
=
\kappa\Bigl(
(x_2-x_1)\nu_6
+
\beta_5(u-w)+v(\gamma_5-\alpha_5)
+
b(p-s)+r(c-a)
\Bigr),
\]
\[
v_{7,K_1}
=
\kappa\Bigl(
x_2\mu_6-x_1\lambda_6
+
\gamma_5u-\alpha_5w
+
cp-as
\Bigr).
\]

Rewrite each term.

Since
\[
x_2-x_1=2\delta x,\quad
u-w=2\delta u,\quad
\gamma_5-\alpha_5=2\delta\alpha_5,\quad
p-s=2\delta p,\quad
c-a=2\delta a,
\]
you get
\[
\boxed{
u_{7,K_1}
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x\,\nu_6+\beta_5\,\delta u+v\,\delta\alpha_5+b\,\delta p+r\,\delta a
\bigr).
}
\]

For the \(S\)-component, use
\[
x_2\mu_6-x_1\lambda_6
=
2(\delta x\,\bar\mu_6-\bar x\,\delta\mu_6),
\]
\[
\gamma_5u-\alpha_5w
=
2(\bar\alpha_5\,\delta u+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u),
\]
\[
cp-as
=
2(\bar a\,\delta p+\delta a\,\bar p).
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
v_{7,K_1}
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x\,\bar\mu_6-\bar x\,\delta\mu_6
+\bar\alpha_5\,\delta u+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u
+\bar a\,\delta p+\delta a\,\bar p
\bigr).
}
\]

Therefore \(u_{7,K_1}\) and \(v_{7,K_1}\) are also **odd functions of \(s\)**.

Write
\[
u_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat U_1 s+\widehat U_3 s^3+\widehat U_5 s^5+\cdots,
\qquad
v_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat V_1 s+\widehat V_3 s^3+\widehat V_5 s^5+\cdots.
\]

Then the leading coefficients are

\[
\boxed{
\widehat U_1
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\,\nu_{6,0}
+\beta_{5,0}\,\delta u_1
+v_0\,\delta\alpha_{5,1}
+b_0\,\delta p_1
+r_0\,\delta a_1
\bigr),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\widehat V_1
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\,\bar\mu_{6,0}
-\bar x_0\,\delta\mu_{6,1}
+\bar\alpha_{5,0}\,\delta u_1
+\delta\alpha_{5,1}\,\bar u_0
+\bar a_0\,\delta p_1
+\delta a_1\,\bar p_0
\bigr).
}
\]

The cubic coefficients are

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\widehat U_3
=
2\kappa\bigl(
&\delta x_1\nu_{6,2}+\delta x_3\nu_{6,0}
+\beta_{5,0}\delta u_3+\beta_{5,2}\delta u_1
+v_0\delta\alpha_{5,3}+v_2\delta\alpha_{5,1}\\
&+b_0\delta p_3+b_2\delta p_1
+r_0\delta a_3+r_2\delta a_1
\bigr),
\end{aligned}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\widehat V_3
=
2\kappa\bigl(
&\delta x_1\bar\mu_{6,2}+\delta x_3\bar\mu_{6,0}
-\bar x_0\delta\mu_{6,3}-\bar x_2\delta\mu_{6,1}\\
&+\bar\alpha_{5,0}\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_{5,2}\delta u_1
+\delta\alpha_{5,1}\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_{5,3}\bar u_0\\
&+\bar a_0\delta p_3+\bar a_2\delta p_1
+\delta a_1\bar p_2+\delta a_3\bar p_0
\bigr).
\end{aligned}
}
\]

So the septic canonical package is also fully explicit as an odd Taylor series in centered \(s\).

## 3. The determinant \(\Delta_7\)

Since the current file proves
\[
\Delta_7=\Delta_{7,K_1}=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1},
\]
and each factor \(u_5,v_5,u_{7,K_1},v_{7,K_1}\) is odd in \(s\), it follows formally that

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_7(s)\ \text{is even in }s.
}
\]

More precisely, with
\[
u_5=U_1 s+U_3 s^3+U_5 s^5+\cdots,\quad
v_5=V_1 s+V_3 s^3+V_5 s^5+\cdots,
\]
\[
u_{7,K_1}=\widehat U_1 s+\widehat U_3 s^3+\widehat U_5 s^5+\cdots,\quad
v_{7,K_1}=\widehat V_1 s+\widehat V_3 s^3+\widehat V_5 s^5+\cdots,
\]
you get
\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2 s^2+D_4 s^4+D_6 s^6+\cdots
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
}
\]

These are the actual Taylor coefficients you asked to get to.

## 4. What this tells you

This is the strongest concrete groundwork you can extract from the current formulas:

- \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is **odd** in the centered symmetric-placement separation variable \(s\);
- \(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\) is **odd** in \(s\);
- \(\Delta_7\) is **even** in \(s\), with explicit coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\) above.

So there is no longer any ambiguity about the Taylor-coefficient structure in the centered separation variable. You now have the first three obstruction coefficients on the septic side explicitly.

## 5. Important caveat

This is in the **symmetric-placement separation variable \(s\)**.

It is not yet the same thing as the local coordinate on a good \(v_5\)-patch used later for the lifted \(4\)-point branch, and that mismatch is exactly why the earlier “odd \(\Delta_7\)” dream package was off. What we have now is the correct raw Taylor groundwork in the natural symmetric variable.

So the next translation step, if you want to keep pushing, is:

- relate the centered separation variable \(s\) to the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\),
- then rewrite the coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\) as coefficients in \(x\).

That is now an honest concrete calculation rather than a vague hope.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 02:14:50)

_Thought for 1m 3s_

I pushed the centered-separation calculations one layer further, and there is real progress.

The clean next step is to stay in the **centered symmetric-placement variable** \(s\), compute the canonical Taylor coefficients there, and then explicitly change variables from \(s\) to the odd coordinate
\[
x(s):=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}.
\]

This does **not** yet put us on a good \(v_5\neq 0\) patch; it is still the collision-side local expansion. But it gives the exact low-jet algebra you asked for.

---

## 1. Starting point in the centered separation variable \(s\)

From the previous computation, we already have:

\[
c(s)=c_0+c_2 s^2+c_4 s^4+c_6 s^6+O(s^8),
\]

\[
u_5(s)=U_1 s+U_3 s^3+U_5 s^5+U_7 s^7+O(s^9),
\]

\[
v_5(s)=V_1 s+V_3 s^3+V_5 s^5+V_7 s^7+O(s^9),
\]

\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2 s^2+D_4 s^4+D_6 s^6+O(s^8),
\]
where
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
\]

So in the raw centered symmetric variable:

- \(c\) is even,
- \(u_5,v_5\) are odd,
- \(\Delta_7\) is even.

That part is now explicit.

---

## 2. Compute \(x(s)=v_5(s)/c(s)\)

Since \(c_0\neq 0\),
\[
\frac1{c(s)}
=
\frac1{c_0}
-\frac{c_2}{c_0^2}s^2
+\frac{c_2^2-c_0c_4}{c_0^3}s^4
+\frac{-c_2^3+2c_0c_2c_4-c_0^2c_6}{c_0^4}s^6
+O(s^8).
\]

Multiplying by \(v_5(s)\) gives
\[
x(s)=x_1 s+x_3 s^3+x_5 s^5+x_7 s^7+O(s^9),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
x_1=\frac{V_1}{c_0},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
x_3=\frac{V_3}{c_0}-\frac{c_2V_1}{c_0^2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
x_5=\frac{V_5}{c_0}-\frac{c_2V_3}{c_0^2}
+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)V_1}{c_0^3},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
x_7=\frac{V_7}{c_0}-\frac{c_2V_5}{c_0^2}
+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)V_3}{c_0^3}
+\frac{(-c_2^3+2c_0c_2c_4-c_0^2c_6)V_1}{c_0^4}.
}
\]

So \(x(s)\) is an odd local coordinate whenever \(x_1\neq 0\), i.e. whenever \(V_1\neq 0\).

---

## 3. Invert the odd coordinate: \(s=s(x)\)

If
\[
x=x_1 s+x_3 s^3+x_5 s^5+x_7 s^7+O(s^9),
\]
then the odd inverse has the form
\[
s=\sigma_1 x+\sigma_3 x^3+\sigma_5 x^5+\sigma_7 x^7+O(x^9),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_1=\frac1{x_1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_3=-\frac{x_3}{x_1^4},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_5=\frac{3x_3^2-x_1x_5}{x_1^7},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_7=\frac{-12x_3^3+8x_1x_3x_5-x_1^2x_7}{x_1^{10}}.
}
\]

This is the exact coordinate-change groundwork.

---

## 4. Expand \(Y=u_5/c\) in \(s\), then in \(x\)

First in \(s\):
\[
Y(s)=\frac{u_5(s)}{c(s)}=Y_1 s+Y_3 s^3+Y_5 s^5+Y_7 s^7+O(s^9),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
Y_1=\frac{U_1}{c_0},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
Y_3=\frac{U_3}{c_0}-\frac{c_2U_1}{c_0^2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
Y_5=\frac{U_5}{c_0}-\frac{c_2U_3}{c_0^2}
+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)U_1}{c_0^3},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
Y_7=\frac{U_7}{c_0}-\frac{c_2U_5}{c_0^2}
+\frac{(c_2^2-c_0c_4)U_3}{c_0^3}
+\frac{(-c_2^3+2c_0c_2c_4-c_0^2c_6)U_1}{c_0^4}.
}
\]

Now substitute \(s=s(x)\). Then
\[
Y(x)=\widetilde Y_1 x+\widetilde Y_3 x^3+\widetilde Y_5 x^5+\widetilde Y_7 x^7+O(x^9),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y_1=\frac{Y_1}{x_1}=\frac{U_1}{V_1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y_3=\frac{Y_3x_1-Y_1x_3}{x_1^4},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y_5=\frac{Y_5x_1^2-3Y_3x_1x_3+Y_1(3x_3^2-x_1x_5)}{x_1^7},
}
\]
and similarly
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde Y_7=
\frac{
Y_7x_1^3-5Y_5x_1^2x_3+Y_3(12x_3^2-3x_1x_5)x_1
+Y_1(-12x_3^3+8x_1x_3x_5-x_1^2x_7)
}{x_1^{10}}.
}
\]

So \(Y\) remains odd after passing from \(s\) to the odd coordinate \(x\), exactly as expected.

---

## 5. Expand \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\)

This is the right object to look at next, because
\[
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c}.
\]

Since \(\Delta_7\) is even and \(v_5\) is odd in \(s\), \(\lambda\) is odd in \(s\).

Write
\[
\lambda(s)=L_1 s+L_3 s^3+L_5 s^5+O(s^7).
\]

A direct series division gives:
\[
\boxed{
L_1=\frac{D_2}{V_1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
L_3=\frac{D_4V_1-D_2V_3}{V_1^2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
L_5=\frac{D_6V_1^2-D_4V_1V_3+D_2(V_3^2-V_1V_5)}{V_1^3}.
}
\]

Now convert to the odd \(x\)-coordinate:
\[
\lambda(x)=\widetilde L_1 x+\widetilde L_3 x^3+\widetilde L_5 x^5+O(x^7),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde L_1=\frac{L_1}{x_1}=\frac{c_0D_2}{V_1^2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde L_3=\frac{L_3x_1-L_1x_3}{x_1^4},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde L_5=\frac{L_5x_1^2-3L_3x_1x_3+L_1(3x_3^2-x_1x_5)}{x_1^7}.
}
\]

So \(\lambda\) is also odd in the collision-side odd coordinate \(x\).

---

## 6. Expand \(S=\lambda/c\)

Now
\[
S(x)=\frac{\lambda(x)}{c(x)}.
\]

Since \(c(x)\) is even in \(x\) and \(\lambda(x)\) is odd in \(x\), we get
\[
S(x)=S_1 x+S_3 x^3+S_5 x^5+O(x^7),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
S_1=\frac{\widetilde L_1}{c_0}=\frac{D_2}{V_1^2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
S_3=\frac{\widetilde L_3}{c_0}-\frac{c_2}{c_0^2}\widetilde L_1,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
S_5=\frac{\widetilde L_5}{c_0}-\frac{c_2}{c_0^2}\widetilde L_3
+\frac{c_2^2-c_0c_4}{c_0^3}\widetilde L_1.
}
\]

So in the collision-side odd coordinate, \(S\) is **odd**, not even.

This is exactly why the earlier parity package needed correction: the symmetric-placement separation variable is not the same normalization regime as the nonmixed \(v_5\neq 0\) patch where one later takes \(S\sim x^2\).

---

## 7. What this now tells you

This is the strongest concrete push forward:

- you now have explicit low Taylor coefficients for
  \[
  x(s),\quad s(x),\quad Y(x),\quad \lambda(x),\quad S(x)
  \]
  in terms of the RH-specific witness coefficients
  \[
  U_1,U_3,U_5,\quad V_1,V_3,V_5,\quad D_2,D_4,D_6.
  \]

- in the centered symmetric-placement regime:
  \[
  Y(x)\ \text{is odd},\qquad \lambda(x)\ \text{is odd},\qquad S(x)\ \text{is odd}.
  \]

So this regime is **not** the nonmixed lifted chart. It is the raw collision chart.

That is actually a useful clarification: it tells you the parity structure of the raw centered two-point expansion, and it shows exactly what must be changed when passing to the lifted nonmixed normalization.

---

## 8. The next exact computation

The next thing to do is **not** more Taylor division here. It is to compute the passage from this raw collision-side odd chart to the nonmixed lifted chart in which one normalizes
\[
Q_v(\eta)=(\widetilde Y(\eta),\eta,\eta^2).
\]

That means:

1. take the raw odd local coordinate \(x\),
2. take the raw odd function \(S(x)\),
3. assume nonmixed \(S''\neq 0\) in the relevant chart,
4. perform the analytic Morse reparametrization
   \[
   x\mapsto \eta
   \]
   that sends \(S\) to \(\eta^2\),
5. then rewrite \(Y\) in that chart.

That is now the real bridge calculation. The groundwork to do it is finally in place.

_Thought for 1m 8s_

Here is the strongest concrete thing I can prove now from the calculations.

## Key local theorem at the centered diagonal base

Work in the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\), with microscopic points
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2}.
\]
From the exact symmetry relations of the coefficient matrices, the canonical low-order quantities satisfy:

- \(c(s)\) is even,
- \(u_5(s)\) is odd,
- \(v_5(s)\) is odd,
- \(\Delta_7(s)\) is even.

From the explicit expansions we already derived,
\[
x(s):=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}
=
x_1 s+x_3 s^3+x_5 s^5+\cdots
\]
is odd, so whenever \(x_1\neq 0\) it can be inverted:
\[
s=s(x)=\sigma_1 x+\sigma_3 x^3+\sigma_5 x^5+\cdots,
\]
also odd.

Substituting back gives:

- \(Y(x)=u_5/c\) is odd,
- \(\lambda(x)=\Delta_7/v_5\) is odd,
- hence
  \[
  S(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda(x)}{c(x)}
  \]
  is odd.

So in the collision-side centered chart,
\[
Q(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x))
\]
has both nontrivial components \(Y,S\) odd.

That already forces a very strong consequence.

---

## 1. Nonmixed points are impossible at the centered diagonal base

Because \(S(x)\) is odd, after subtracting its linear term by an affine target change,
\[
\widetilde S(x):=S(x)-S_1 x
\]
is still odd and starts at order at least \(3\):
\[
\widetilde S(x)=\widetilde s_3 x^3+\widetilde s_5 x^5+\cdots.
\]

Therefore
\[
\widetilde S''(0)=0.
\]

But on a good patch,
\[
K_v=(x')^3 S''.
\]
So at the centered diagonal base,
\[
\boxed{K_v(0)=0.}
\]

That means the centered diagonal local model can **never** be nonmixed. So the dangerous nonmixed low-order cases
\[
n=4,6,8
\]
cannot arise directly from the symmetric diagonal base.

That is a real theorem.

---

## 2. The centered diagonal base is automatically in the mixed regime with odd \(m\)

Since \(\widetilde S\) is odd and has no linear term, its first nonzero exponent is an odd integer
\[
m\ge 3.
\]
So after affine normalization, the lifted germ has
\[
Q(x)\sim (\text{odd},\,x,\,x^m),
\qquad m\in\{3,5,7,\dots\}.
\]

In particular:

- \(m=4\) is impossible;
- more generally, any mixed model with even \(m\) is impossible at this centered base.

So one of the explicit dangerous mixed cases,
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\]
is already ruled out.

---

## 3. After gauge reduction, the first surviving exponent \(n\) is also odd

Because \(Y(x)\) is odd, we can subtract its linear term:
\[
\widetilde Y_1(x):=Y(x)-Y_1 x.
\]
This remains odd.

Now use the remaining affine coplanarity gauge \(Y\mapsto Y-\gamma \widetilde S\).

If \(m=3\), choose \(\gamma\) to kill the cubic term of \(\widetilde Y_1\). Then the first surviving term of the normalized first component is odd of degree at least \(5\):
\[
n\in\{5,7,9,\dots\}.
\]
So when \(m=3\), the dangerous even cases
\[
(3,4),\qquad (3,6)
\]
are impossible.

If \(m\ge 5\), then \(m\) is already odd and \(Y\) is odd, so the first surviving \(n\) is automatically odd. Again, no dangerous even \(n\) occurs.

Therefore the full explicit low-order mixed bad list
\[
(3,4),\qquad (3,6),\qquad (4,6)
\]
is impossible in the centered diagonal regime.

So we get:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At the centered symmetric diagonal base, none of the explicit low-order dangerous mixed patterns can occur.}
}
\]

---

## 4. What this does and does not solve

This is a real advance, but it is local to the **centered diagonal/collision model**.

It proves:

- the centered diagonal base is automatically mixed, never nonmixed;
- after the natural affine gauge reductions, both leading exponents in the mixed normal form are odd;
- hence the explicit low-order dangerous list
  \[
  n=4,6,8,\qquad (m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)
  \]
  is excluded there.

What it does **not** yet prove is that the same exclusion holds at an arbitrary nearby good-patch point that is not itself the diagonal base. So this does not finish the full 4-point branch.

But it does show something important:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The explicit low-order dangerous patterns are not born directly at the symmetric diagonal base.}
}
\]

If they exist at all, they have to arise only **after leaving** that centered collision regime.

---

## 5. The clean theorem statement

You can package the calculation as:

### Proposition
At a centered symmetric diagonal basepoint, in the odd local coordinate \(x=v_5/c\) induced from the centered separation variable, the lifted germ
\[
Q(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x))
\]
satisfies:

1. \(Y(x)\) is odd;
2. \(S(x)\) is odd;
3. after affine normalization \(S\mapsto S-S_1x\), the first nonzero exponent of \(S\) is odd and at least \(3\);
4. after affine normalization \(Y\mapsto Y-Y_1x-\gamma S\), the first surviving exponent of \(Y\) is odd.

Consequently, the centered diagonal base cannot realize the explicit dangerous nonmixed cases \(n=4,6,8\) nor the explicit dangerous mixed cases \((3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\).

### Proof
Exactly the chain above.

---

## 6. Why this matters strategically

This gives you a sharper roadmap.

The low-order dangerous \(4\)-point patterns are **not** a first-contact phenomenon at the centered diagonal base. So the next remaining question is:

> can such patterns appear only after transport away from the centered diagonal base, and if so, what mechanism breaks the odd/odd parity package?

That is now the right place to attack.

The next concrete calculation would be to perturb away from the centered diagonal base and track the first even terms that can appear in the normalized \(Y\)- and \(S\)-jets. That would tell you whether the dangerous patterns can emerge at first order off the diagonal, or only at higher order.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 02:37:36)

_Thought for 2m 6s_

Here is the next real calculation.

The centered symmetric-placement expansion is strong enough to prove a **local exclusion theorem at the diagonal base**, and to pin down the only way dangerous 4-point patterns could still appear: they would have to be created only after moving away from that diagonal base.

## 1. What the centered expansion already forces

Using the centered variable \(s\) with microscopic points
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
the symmetry relations give

\[
c(s)\ \text{even},\qquad
u_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad
v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\Delta_7(s)\ \text{even}.
\]

Write
\[
x(s):=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}.
\]
Then \(x(s)\) is odd, so when \(x_1\neq 0\) it inverts to an odd local coordinate
\[
s=s(x).
\]

Substituting back, you get in the collision-side odd coordinate \(x\):
\[
Y(x):=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\lambda(x):=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\ \text{odd},
\qquad
S(x):=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda(x)}{c(x)}\ \text{odd}.
\]

So the raw centered collision germ has the form
\[
Q(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x)),
\]
with both \(Y\) and \(S\) odd.

## 2. Affine normalization at the diagonal base

Now use the affine freedoms that preserve coplanarity.

First subtract the linear term from \(S\):
\[
\widetilde S(x):=S(x)-S_1x.
\]
Since \(S\) is odd, \(\widetilde S\) is still odd, so
\[
\widetilde S(x)=\sigma_m x^m+\sigma_{m+2}x^{m+2}+\cdots,
\qquad
m\ge 3,\quad m\ \text{odd}.
\]

Next subtract the linear term from \(Y\):
\[
Y_1(x):=Y(x)-Y_1x.
\]
Again \(Y_1\) is odd.

Then use the remaining affine gauge \(Y\mapsto Y-\gamma \widetilde S\) to kill the first possible overlap with \(\widetilde S\). The resulting normalized first component still has only odd powers:
\[
\widetilde Y(x)=\upsilon_n x^n+\upsilon_{n+2}x^{n+2}+\cdots,
\qquad
n>m,\quad n\ \text{odd}.
\]

So the normalized collision-side germ is always of the form
\[
\boxed{
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\ n>m,\ m,n\ \text{odd}.
}
\]

That is the key local theorem.

## 3. Immediate consequence: the explicit low-order bad list is impossible at the diagonal base

Because \(m,n\) are both odd, the currently dangerous low-order patterns cannot occur there.

In particular:

- nonmixed bad cases
  \[
  n=4,6,8
  \]
  are impossible;

- mixed bad cases
  \[
  (m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
  \]
  are impossible.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The explicit low-order dangerous 4-point patterns cannot be born at the centered symmetric diagonal base.}
}
\]

That is a real advance.

## 4. What this says in invariant language

Since \(\widetilde S\) is odd with first nonzero term \(x^m\), \(m\) odd \(\ge 3\), we have
\[
K_v\propto S''.
\]
Therefore at the diagonal base,
\[
\ord_0 K_v = m-2
\]
is always odd.

Likewise, with \(\widetilde Y\sim x^n\), \(n\) odd,
\[
\ord_0 T_v = n+m-5
\]
is also odd.

So at the diagonal base:

- the nonmixed regime \(K_v(0)\neq 0\) cannot happen at all;
- the mixed regime is possible, but only with
  \[
  r=\ord_0 K_v\ \text{odd},\qquad s=\ord_0 T_v\ \text{odd}.
  \]

That already excludes the explicit mixed low-order list
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
because all three violate this parity rule.

So you can state this even more sharply as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At the centered diagonal base, }r\text{ and }s\text{ are both odd.}
}
\]

## 5. The next obstruction now becomes very concrete

Since the explicit low-order bad list cannot occur at the diagonal base, the only remaining way it could appear is:

> after transporting away from the diagonal base and re-centering at a nearby nonzero point.

So the next real calculation is a perturbation calculation.

Let the normalized collision germ be
\[
\widetilde S(x)=\sigma_3x^3+\sigma_5x^5+\sigma_7x^7+\cdots,
\]
\[
\widetilde Y(x)=\upsilon_5x^5+\upsilon_7x^7+\upsilon_9x^9+\cdots
\]
in the generic \(m=3\) case after killing the cubic overlap.

Now shift the basepoint to \(x=x_0\neq 0\) and write
\[
x=x_0+\eta.
\]

Then the first coefficients of the recentered jets are:

\[
\widetilde S''(x_0)=6\sigma_3x_0+20\sigma_5x_0^3+42\sigma_7x_0^5+\cdots,
\]
so for \(x_0\neq 0\) and \(\sigma_3\neq 0\), the shifted point is generically **nonmixed**.

Also
\[
\widetilde Y'''(x_0)=60\upsilon_5x_0^2+210\upsilon_7x_0^4+504\upsilon_9x_0^6+\cdots.
\]

So the nearby nonmixed branch is controlled by zeros of the even function
\[
x\longmapsto \widetilde Y'''(x).
\]

This gives a new sharp reduction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Near a generic diagonal-base mixed point with }m=3,\ 
\text{any nearby nonmixed odd-order }T_v\text{-zero must come from a nonzero root of }
\widetilde Y'''(x).
}
\]

And because \(\widetilde Y\) is odd, \(\widetilde Y'''\) is even. So any nearby nonmixed zero appears in symmetric pairs \(\pm x_0\).

That does **not** yet exclude orders \(1,3,5\), but it is much tighter than before.

## 6. The next explicit calculation to do

There are now two concrete perturbative targets.

First, in the generic \(m=3\) case, compute whether \(\widetilde Y'''(x)\) can have nonzero zeros of low odd multiplicity near the base. Since \(\widetilde Y'''\) is even, its nonzero roots come in pairs and their multiplicities are unconstrained by parity alone. So this is the place where a genuine RH-specific identity would have to enter.

Second, in the higher-order diagonal-base cases \(m\ge 5\), the same shift analysis should show what nonmixed orders can be produced after moving off the base.

So the attack has now reached this point:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The explicit low-order bad patterns are excluded at the centered diagonal base itself.}
}
\]

What remains is a **transport-away-from-the-diagonal** problem: can those patterns be created at nearby shifted points?

That is the exact next place to push.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 02:49:31)

_Thought for 2m 34s_

I pushed the transport-away-from-diagonal calculation through, and there is a real payoff:

## Strong local exclusion theorem near the centered diagonal base

Once you put the centered diagonal germ into its odd/odd normal form, the dangerous \(4\)-point patterns do **not** just fail at the basepoint itself — they cannot appear at any sufficiently nearby shifted point either.

That is the strongest honest attack result so far.

---

## 1. General odd/odd diagonal normal form

At the centered symmetric diagonal base, after the affine normalizations already discussed, the local lifted germ has the form
\[
Q(x)\sim (Y(x),x,S(x)),
\]
with
\[
Y(x)=x^n B(x^2),\qquad S(x)=x^m A(x^2),
\]
where

- \(m\ge 3\) is odd,
- \(n>m\) is odd,
- \(A(0)\neq 0\),
- \(B(0)\neq 0\).

Set
\[
u:=x^2.
\]

Then the exact second-derivative formulas are
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\,\Sigma_m[A](u),
\qquad
Y''(x)=x^{n-2}\,\Sigma_n[B](u),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_k[F](u):=
k(k-1)F(u)+2(2k+1)uF'(u)+4u^2F''(u).
}
\]

So the canonical ratio is
\[
\mathcal Z(x):=\frac{Y''}{S''}
=
x^{\,n-m}\,H(u),
\qquad
H(u):=\frac{\Sigma_n[B](u)}{\Sigma_m[A](u)}.
\]

Because \(n-m\) is a positive even integer and
\[
H(0)=\frac{n(n-1)B(0)}{m(m-1)A(0)}\neq 0,
\]
this already shows \(\mathcal Z\) has the exact leading form
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z(x)=x^{\,n-m}\bigl(H_0+H_1x^2+H_2x^4+\cdots\bigr),
\qquad H_0\neq 0.
}
\]

Differentiate:
\[
\mathcal R(x):=\mathcal Z'(x)
=
x^{\,n-m-1}\,J(u),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
J(u):=(n-m)H(u)+2uH'(u).
}
\]

Since
\[
J(0)=(n-m)H(0)\neq 0,
\]
we get the exact leading behavior
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R(x)=x^{\,n-m-1}\bigl(J_0+J_1x^2+J_2x^4+\cdots\bigr),
\qquad J_0\neq 0.
}
\]

---

## 2. Consequence: no nearby nonmixed \(T_v=0\) points

Recall
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
\]
whenever \(K_v\neq 0\). Also
\[
K_v\propto S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2).
\]

Since \(\Sigma_m[A](0)=m(m-1)A(0)\neq 0\), there exists \(\varepsilon>0\) such that for
\[
0<|x|<\varepsilon,
\]
we have
\[
S''(x)\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
J(x^2)\neq 0.
\]

Hence
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\neq 0
\]
for all sufficiently small nonzero \(x\).

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
T_v(x)\neq 0
\qquad\text{for all sufficiently small nonzero }x.
}
\]

So there are **no nearby nonmixed \(T_v=0\) points at all**.

This is stronger than just excluding the explicit low-order bad list. It says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{After leaving the centered diagonal base by a sufficiently small amount, you do not encounter any }T_v=0\text{ points whatsoever.}
}
\]

In particular, the dangerous nonmixed low-order cases \(n=4,6,8\) cannot be created by tiny transport away from the diagonal base.

---

## 3. Consequence: no nearby mixed points either

Because
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),
\qquad
\Sigma_m[A](0)\neq 0,
\]
the only zero of \(S''\) in a sufficiently small neighborhood is \(x=0\) itself.

So
\[
\boxed{
K_v(x)\neq 0
\qquad\text{for all sufficiently small nonzero }x.
}
\]

Thus the diagonal base is the **only** nearby mixed point.

So the whole local picture near the centered diagonal base is:

- at \(x=0\): mixed point with odd/odd exponents \((m,n)\);
- for \(0<|x|<\varepsilon\): neither mixed nor \(T_v=0\).

There is simply no local birth of the dangerous \(4\)-point configurations in a punctured neighborhood.

---

## 4. Explicit generic case \(m=3,n=5\)

In the generic lowest-order odd/odd case,
\[
S(x)=a x^3+b x^5+c x^7+\cdots,
\qquad
Y(x)=p x^5+q x^7+r x^9+\cdots,
\qquad a,p\neq 0.
\]

Then the direct expansion gives
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{10p}{3a}x^2
+
\left(\frac{7q}{a}-\frac{100bp}{9a^2}\right)x^4
+O(x^6),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal R(x)
=
\frac{20p}{3a}x
+
\left(\frac{28q}{a}-\frac{400bp}{9a^2}\right)x^3
+O(x^5).
\]

So
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R(x)=x\bigl(C_0+C_2x^2+\cdots\bigr),
\qquad C_0=\frac{20p}{3a}\neq 0.
}
\]

This makes the local exclusion completely explicit: for \(x\neq 0\) small,
\[
\mathcal R(x)\neq 0.
\]

So in the generic \(m=3,n=5\) diagonal case, no nearby nonmixed \(T_v=0\) points exist at all.

---

## 5. What this means strategically

This is a real narrowing of the problem.

Earlier, the remaining possibility was:

> maybe the explicit low-order dangerous \(4\)-point patterns are not born at the diagonal base itself, but appear immediately after transporting slightly away from it.

The calculation above rules that out.

So the new conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered diagonal base has a punctured neighborhood free of }T_v=0\text{ points.}
}
\]

Therefore the dangerous \(4\)-point configurations, if they exist at all, must be created only **farther away**, not infinitesimally off the diagonal base.

That is a substantial improvement.

---

## 6. Clean theorem statement

You can package the calculation as:

### Proposition (diagonal-base punctured-neighborhood exclusion)
Let the centered diagonal lifted germ be normalized to
\[
Q(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x))
\]
with
\[
Y(x)=x^nB(x^2),\qquad S(x)=x^mA(x^2),
\]
where \(m\ge 3\), \(n>m\) are odd and \(A(0),B(0)\neq 0\).

Then there exists \(\varepsilon>0\) such that for
\[
0<|x|<\varepsilon,
\]
one has
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0.
\]

In particular, no nonmixed or mixed \(4\)-point obstruction point occurs in a punctured neighborhood of the centered diagonal base.

### Proof
Exactly the factorization above:
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=x^{n-m-1}J(x^2),
\]
with \(\Sigma_m[A](0)\neq 0\) and \(J(0)\neq 0\).

---

## 7. Honest remaining frontier

This still does **not** finish the global \(4\)-point branch. It shows only that the dangerous patterns cannot arise:

- at the centered diagonal base,
- nor in any sufficiently small punctured neighborhood around it.

So the remaining possibility is a **more global recurrence / transport** phenomenon at finite distance, not a local bifurcation off the diagonal base.

That is now the exact place the \(4\)-point attack has reached.
