## Assistant (2026-04-20 03:52:39)

_Thought for 12s_

Yes. Here is the cleanest consolidated summary of what emerged beyond the current draft.

I’ll separate it into what is now genuinely established, what was reduced to finite obstruction coefficients, what was shown to be a dead end, and what the sharp remaining targets are.

---

## 1. The lifted \(4\)-point branch has a canonical scalar invariant

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
the exact identities are
\[
K_v=(x')^3S''(x),
\]
and
\[
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr).
\]

So on every nonmixed patch \(K_v\neq 0\),
\[
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\qquad
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.
\]

This is the correct scalar invariant of the lifted \(4\)-point branch. The \(4\)-point local problem is best formulated in terms of \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\mathcal R\), not \(Y\) itself.

Also, \(\mathcal Z\) is invariant under the affine coplanarity gauge up to an additive constant:
\[
Y\mapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathcal Z\mapsto \mathcal Z+\gamma,
\qquad
\mathcal R\mapsto \mathcal R.
\]

So \(\mathcal R\) is fully canonical, and the nonconstant Taylor coefficients of \(\mathcal Z\) are canonical.

---

## 2. Exact nonmixed reduction

At a nonmixed point,
\[
K_v(0)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
one may analytically normalize to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\widetilde Y(0)=\widetilde Y'(0)=\widetilde Y''(0)=0.
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal Z(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y''(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi).
\]

So the dangerous nonmixed low-order \(4\)-point cases are exactly:
\[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8,
\]
equivalently
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R=1,\ 3,\ 5.
\]

This is the sharp exact reduction of the nonmixed \(4\)-point problem.

---

## 3. Exact mixed reduction

At a mixed point,
\[
K_v(0)=0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
the local model is
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,\quad n>m.
\]

If
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,\qquad s\ge 2r.
\]

Also
\[
\ord_0\mathcal Z=s-2r+1,
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal R=s-2r.
\]

So the dangerous mixed low-order list
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
is equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

So the mixed \(4\)-point problem was reduced to a finite explicit list of order patterns.

---

## 4. Exact finite obstruction coefficients on the nonmixed side

In an arbitrary nonmixed \(x\)-chart, write
\[
s_k:=S^{(k)}(0),\qquad y_k:=Y^{(k)}(0),\qquad s_2\neq 0.
\]

Then the first three even Taylor coefficients of
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=z_0+z_1x+z_2x^2+z_3x^3+z_4x^4+z_5x^5+z_6x^6+\cdots
\]
are canonical and govern the dangerous nonmixed list:

- \(n=4\) iff \(z_2\neq 0\),
- \(n=6\) iff \(z_2=0\) but \(z_4\neq 0\),
- \(n=8\) iff \(z_2=z_4=0\) but \(z_6\neq 0\).

The exact formulas are:

\[
z_2=
\frac{
s_2^2y_4-2s_2s_3y_3+\bigl(2s_3^2-s_2s_4\bigr)y_2
}{
2\,s_2^3
},
\]

\[
z_4=
\frac{
s_2^4y_6
-s_2^3(4s_3y_5+6s_4y_4+4s_5y_3+s_6y_2)
+2s_2^2(6s_3^2y_4+12s_3s_4y_3+4s_3s_5y_2+3s_4^2y_2)
-12s_2s_3^2(2s_3y_3+3s_4y_2)
+24s_3^4y_2
}{
24\,s_2^5
},
\]

and
\[
z_6=
\frac{\mathcal P_8(s_2,\dots,s_8;y_2,\dots,y_8)}{720\,s_2^7},
\]
with the explicit polynomial \(\mathcal P_8\) worked out.

So the nonmixed low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is equivalent to the finite system
\[
z_2=z_4=z_6=0.
\]

That is the cleanest nonmixed finite-jet target.

---

## 5. Exact finite obstruction coefficients on the mixed side

The mixed side was similarly reduced to three explicit coefficients.

### Case \(r=1\)

Here
\[
s_2=0,\qquad s_3\neq 0.
\]
The expansion of \(\mathcal Z\) begins
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{y_2}{s_3}\frac1x+\left(\frac{y_3}{s_3}-\frac{s_4y_2}{2s_3^2}\right)+\kappa_{1,1}x+\kappa_{1,2}x^2+\kappa_{1,3}x^3+\cdots.
\]

The dangerous low-order mixed cases for \(r=1\) are governed by
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},
\]
with exact formulas
\[
\kappa_{1,1}
=
\frac{y_4}{2s_3}
-\frac{s_4y_3}{2s_3^2}
-\frac{s_5y_2}{6s_3^2}
+\frac{s_4^2y_2}{4s_3^3},
\]
and an explicit formula for \(\kappa_{1,3}\).

Then:
- \((m,n)=(3,4)\) iff \(\kappa_{1,1}\neq 0\),
- \((m,n)=(3,6)\) iff \(\kappa_{1,3}\neq 0\).

### Case \(r=2\)

Here
\[
s_2=s_3=0,\qquad s_4\neq 0.
\]
The expansion gives coefficients \(\kappa_{2,1},\kappa_{2,2},\dots\), and the dangerous low-order case \((m,n)=(4,6)\) is governed by
\[
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{y_6}{12s_4}
-\frac{s_5y_5}{9s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_4}{12s_4^2}
+\frac{s_5^2y_4}{9s_4^3}.
\]

So the explicit mixed bad list is equivalent to the finite system
\[
\kappa_{1,1}=\kappa_{1,3}=\kappa_{2,2}=0.
\]

Thus the entire currently explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list was reduced to **six exact jet coefficients**:
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

---

## 6. A deeper exact identity below the lifted variables

There is a useful identity one layer below \((Y,S)\).

For any scalar \(f\), define
\[
J_f:=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c & v_5 & f\\
c' & v_5' & f'\\
c'' & v_5'' & f''
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then one has the exact formula
\[
\frac{d^2}{dx^2}\!\left(\frac{f}{c}\right)
=
\frac{c^3}{M^3}\,J_f,
\qquad
M=c\,v_5'-c'v_5.
\]

Applying this to \(f=u_5\) and \(f=\lambda:=\Delta_7/v_5\) gives
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_\lambda,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
}
\]

This says the \(4\)-point branch is governed by a ratio of two triple Wronskians in the original scalar data.

There is also the projective-chart ratio
\[
\Theta=\frac{W_{u_5}}{W},
\]
and the exact identity
\[
\Theta=\frac{\mathcal Z}{D(x)}
\]
for an explicit denominator \(D(x)\). In the mixed case,
\[
\ord_0\Theta=\ord_0\mathcal R,
\]
so \(\Theta\) adds no extra order information beyond \(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R\).

---

## 7. Realization lemma and negative result

A decisive negative result emerged:

Every analytic pair of germs \((\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)\) can be realized on some good \(v_5\)-patch by taking
\[
c\equiv 1,\qquad
v_5=1+\xi,\qquad
u_5=\widetilde Y(\xi),\qquad
\Delta_7=(1+\xi)\widetilde S(\xi).
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No obstruction to the low-order dangerous \(4\)-point patterns can come from identities involving only }c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7\text{ and their derivatives.}
}
\]

Any real RH-specific obstruction must come from deeper source-level or matrix-level structure, not from the lifted variables alone.

This was one of the most important negative results.

---

## 8. Exact source-level \(4\)-body theorem, conditional

A clean conditional theorem was isolated:

If there is a source-level corrected quotient-germ map on finite atomic sources and the pure \(4\)-body inclusion–exclusion remainder
\[
\mathcal I_4
=
\mathcal F_4-\sum \mathcal F_3+\sum \mathcal F_2-\sum \mathcal F_1
\]
is

- symmetric in the four labels,
- zero when any amplitude vanishes,
- zero on every partial diagonal \(h_i=h_j\),

then
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_4
=
\Bigl(\prod_{j=1}^4 a_j\Bigr)
\Bigl(\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(h_i-h_j)^2\Bigr)\,
\mathcal J_4
}
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal J_4\).

So the pure \(4\)-body remainder has a full amplitude factor and a discriminant-squared factor.

But testing this against the local models showed:

- on the nonmixed model \(Q(x)=(x^n,x,x^2)\), the geometric coplanarity branch scales like \(t^{n+3}\);
- on the mixed model \(Q(x)\sim(x^n,x,x^m)\), it scales like \(t^{m+n+1}\);
- whereas the discriminant-squared \(4\)-body correction scales like \(t^{12}\).

So this structural correction is too high-order to kill the **low-order** dangerous branches:
- nonmixed \(n=4,6,8\),
- mixed \(m+n\le 10\).

Thus the \(4\)-body theorem is conceptually right, but too weak to eliminate the explicit low-order bad list. That was another important negative result.

---

## 9. Corrected parity picture at the centered diagonal base

A major correction emerged here.

The earlier naive dream package
\[
c\text{ even},\quad A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ odd},\quad \Delta_7\text{ odd}
\]
was miscentered for a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch.

At the **centered symmetric-placement diagonal base**, the correct raw parity is instead:

- \(c(s)\) even,
- \(u_5(s)\) odd,
- \(v_5(s)\) odd,
- \(\Delta_7(s)\) even,

in the centered separation variable \(s\).

From the exact formulas, this gives in the collision-side odd coordinate
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
that \(x\) is odd, \(Y=u_5/c\) is odd, and \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) is odd, hence
\[
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
is also odd in that regime.

So at the diagonal base, after affine normalization one always gets an odd/odd local normal form
\[
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n>m\ge 3.
\]

This has two strong consequences:

- the diagonal base is automatically **mixed**, never nonmixed;
- the explicit low-order dangerous patterns
  \[
  n=4,6,8,\qquad (m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)
  \]
  are impossible there.

That was a real local exclusion theorem.

---

## 10. Punctured-neighborhood exclusion near the diagonal base

This was pushed further.

For the odd/odd diagonal normal form
\[
Y(x)=x^nB(x^2),\qquad S(x)=x^mA(x^2),
\qquad m,n\ \text{odd},\ n>m\ge 3,
\]
one gets exact factorisations
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),
\]
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=x^{n-m}H(x^2),
\]
\[
\mathcal R(x)=x^{n-m-1}J(x^2),
\]
with
\[
\Sigma_m[A](0)\neq 0,\qquad J(0)\neq 0.
\]

Therefore there exists \(\varepsilon>0\) such that for
\[
0<|x|<\varepsilon,
\]
one has
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0.
\]

So the centered diagonal base has a **punctured neighborhood free of \(K_v=0\) and \(T_v=0\) points**.

This means the dangerous \(4\)-point configurations are not only absent at the diagonal base itself; they cannot be born by an infinitesimal move away from it either.

That was one of the strongest local results obtained.

---

## 11. Exact centered-separation Taylor groundwork

The centered symmetric-placement formulas were pushed much further than the draft currently records.

In the centered separation variable \(s\), one has explicit odd/even expansions
\[
c(s)=c_0+c_2s^2+c_4s^4+c_6s^6+\cdots,
\]
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+U_5s^5+\cdots,
\]
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+V_5s^5+\cdots,
\]
\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2s^2+D_4s^4+D_6s^6+\cdots,
\]
with explicit formulas for
\[
U_1,U_3,U_5,\qquad V_1,V_3,V_5,\qquad D_2,D_4,D_6
\]
in terms of the symmetric-placement matrix coefficients.

In particular,
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
\]

Also explicit change-of-variable formulas were derived for

- \(x(s)=v_5/c\),
- the inverse \(s(x)\),
- \(Y(x)=u_5/c\),
- \(\lambda(x)=\Delta_7/v_5\),
- \(S(x)=\Delta_7/(c\,v_5)\),

all through low order.

This gives a complete Taylor bridge from the symmetric microscopic diagonal expansion to the collision-side odd chart.

---

## 12. Exact explicit RH-specific transport witnesses

The current file’s concrete witness slices were pushed to explicit formulas.

### Quintic witness
On the pure witness slice \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\), the canonical quintic fixed-sector witness has the explicit coefficient
\[
u_5^{(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})}
=
C_5\,\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)},
\qquad
C_5=\frac{du}{a^2b^2(a+b)^2}\neq 0
\]
up to the draft’s overall normalization/sign convention.

### Septic witness
On the direct \(K_1\)-transport \(q^{(7)}\)-slice,
\[
u_{7,K_1}^{(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(7)})}
=
C_7\,\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(7)},
\qquad
C_7=\frac{du}{a^2b^2(a+b)^2}\neq 0,
\]
again up to normalization/sign.

So both the quintic canonical residual and the highest-new septic scalar contain genuine odd RH-specific transport witnesses controlled by the same nonzero toy coefficient
\[
\frac{du}{a^2b^2(a+b)^2}.
\]

This is the deepest explicit coefficient information extracted from the present file.

---

## 13. Correction on \(\Delta_7\): it is already fully reduced

A useful correction to earlier pessimism:

The current draft proves
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}+A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
so in the quotient
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}],
\]
and more strongly,
\[
\boxed{\Delta_7=\Delta_{7,K_1}.}
\]

So the septic scalar has **no hidden lower sectors left**. Its entire parity and low-jet behavior comes from the explicit \(K_1\)-transport formula.

That was an important clarification.

---

## 14. What was shown to be dead ends

Several routes were explored and ruled out.

### Dead end A: generic branch geometry
Generic lifted geometry alone is too flexible to exclude the dangerous \(4\)-point patterns.

### Dead end B: parity obstruction in the mixed model
There is no generic parity obstruction beyond
\[
s\ge 2r.
\]
The dangerous mixed patterns are genuinely realizable in smooth local models.

### Dead end C: parity of \(c\) alone
Evenness of \(c\) in a normalized chart is far too weak to force the dream identity.

### Dead end D: \(\Theta\) as a new invariant
The ratio
\[
\Theta=\frac{W_{u_5}}{W}
\]
adds no extra order information beyond \(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R\).

### Dead end E: the current swap symmetry
The symmetric-placement involution already in the draft is the **wrong** symmetry for the dream identity. It gives anti-fixed behavior of the raw quintic slice, not the centered parity package needed for the \(4\)-point obstruction.

These negative results were important because they sharply narrowed the plausible remaining routes.

---

## 15. What the 2-point branch work discovered

This is separate, but important.

A strong conditional theorem was isolated:

If the corrected two-pair object comes from a source-level corrected quotient-germ map and the raw interaction remainder is

- symmetric under swapping the two atoms,
- zero when either amplitude is zero,
- zero on the diagonal \(h_1=h_2\),

then it factors as
\[
\mathcal I_2
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

That immediately gives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(|h_1-h_2|^2),
\]
hence the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches by the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem.

This has not yet been made unconditional from the present draft, but it sharply isolated the exact structural theorem needed for the two-point branch.

---

## 16. The sharp remaining frontiers

After all this, the honest remaining frontier is now very concrete.

### For the \(4\)-point branch

The current draft does **not** yet provide the RH-specific source-/matrix-level identities needed to force
\[
z_2=z_4=z_6=0,
\qquad
\kappa_{1,1}=\kappa_{1,3}=\kappa_{2,2}=0.
\]

Equivalently:

- nonmixed: exclude
  \[
  \ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\};
  \]
- mixed: exclude
  \[
  (r,\ord_0\mathcal R)\in\{(1,0),(1,2),(2,1)\}.
  \]

### For the source-level symmetry route

The strongest sufficient theorem found is:

If the centered normalization map for the canonical package is reflection-equivariant through the low jets, then the relevant parity package follows and the explicit low-order \(4\)-point bad list dies.

But the current draft still does not expose the raw normalization equations explicitly enough to check that theorem.

---

## 17. Clean final summary

The most important new structures, reductions, and “goodies” since the draft are:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
}
\]
as the canonical \(4\)-point invariants.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Nonmixed low-order bad list } \Longleftrightarrow z_2,z_4,z_6.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Mixed low-order bad list } \Longleftrightarrow \kappa_{1,1},\kappa_{1,3},\kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_7=\Delta_{7,K_1}
}
\]
exactly.

\[
\boxed{
\text{At the centered diagonal base, the normalized local form is odd/odd, so the explicit low-order bad list is impossible there.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{In fact, a punctured neighborhood of the centered diagonal base is free of }K_v=0\text{ and }T_v=0\text{ points.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No identity involving only }c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7\text{ and their derivatives can force the missing low-order vanishing; any true obstruction must come from deeper source-/matrix-level RH structure.}
}
\]

That is the full mathematical state reached beyond the current draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 04:04:29)

_Thought for 20s_

Yes. There are a few genuinely useful pieces in it, plus one thing I would treat cautiously.

The strongest useful point is the parity package in the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\). The summary makes explicit that, in the diagonal-centered regime,
\[
u_5(s),\ v_5(s),\ u_{7,K_1}(s),\ v_{7,K_1}(s)
\]
are odd, while
\[
\Delta_7(s)=u_{7,K_1}(s)v_5(s)-u_5(s)v_{7,K_1}(s)
\]
is even, with explicit coefficients
\[
D_2,\ D_4,\ D_6.
\]
That is useful because it turns the septic side from a qualitative parity story into an actual Taylor-coefficient story. In particular, the formulas for
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,\qquad
D_4,\qquad D_6
\]
are worth keeping. They are concrete invariants you can later track under any change from the collision variable \(s\) to a patch variable. 

A second useful point is the below-lifted identity
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
and the companion projective ratio \(\Theta=W_{u_5}/W\). I already had the first identity, but the summary’s exact relation between \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\Theta\) is helpful conceptually because it confirms that \(\Theta\) does not introduce a new independent obstruction. It sharpens the conclusion that the \(4\)-point branch is really governed by \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\), not by some extra projective invariant. 

A third useful point is the very clean finite mixed obstruction list written in all equivalent forms:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),
\]
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),(1,4),(2,5),
\]
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),(1,3),(2,2),
\]
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),(1,2),(2,1).
\]
That equivalence class is worth preserving exactly as stated. It is a good way to keep the mixed branch finite and explicit. 

The most interesting claim in the other summary is the centered-\(s\) parity implication
\[
Y(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad S(x)\ \text{odd}
\]
after passing to
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and then
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd}.
\]
If that passage is correct, then the mixed low-order dangerous list is indeed killed immediately, because
\[
\ord_0 K_v
\]
would always be odd and
\[
\ord_0\mathcal Z
\]
would always be even. That is potentially very valuable. But this is also the part I would treat with the most caution, because it crosses from the symmetric diagonal collision variable \(s\) into the good-patch \(x=v_5/c\) language, and that bridge is exactly where parity arguments have been slippery before. I would not promote that to theorem-level yet without rechecking every step of the coordinate change and the domain where \(x\) is actually the right local parameter. 

The source-level \(2\)-pair summary is aligned with what I already found: the right theorem is the structural factorization
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J,
\]
conditional on source-level symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse. That is useful mostly as confirmation rather than something new. 

The most useful net additions, in my view, are:

- keep the explicit septic Taylor coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\);
- keep the exact mixed obstruction list in all four equivalent parameterizations;
- keep the \(\mathcal Z\)-vs-\(\Theta\) identity as a “no extra invariant here” result;
- treat the claim that centered-\(s\) parity kills the full low-order mixed \(4\)-point list as promising but still provisional.

If you want, I’ll turn the genuinely solid parts of that summary into a merged “post-draft findings” section with clear labels: established, conditional, and still-needs-checking.

_Thought for 9s_

Yes. There are a few genuinely useful upgrades in it, and one claim I would keep provisional. The most valuable additions are these. 

The strongest useful refinement is the centered-\(s\) Taylor package. It cleanly organizes the microscopic symmetric-placement coefficients into even half-sums and odd half-differences, then pushes that through the explicit formulas for
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1},\ \Delta_7.
\]
That yields concrete low-order septic coefficients
\[
D_2,\ D_4,\ D_6
\]
rather than just a parity slogan. That is worth keeping.

A second useful point is the exact local factorization at the diagonal-centered odd/odd model:
\[
Y(x)=x^nB(x^2),\qquad S(x)=x^mA(x^2),
\]
with \(m,n\) odd, and then
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)=x^{n-m}H(x^2),\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=x^{n-m-1}J(x^2).
\]
This is better than the earlier informal discussion because it gives a real punctured-neighborhood exclusion:
for sufficiently small nonzero \(x\),
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0.
\]
That is a solid local theorem near the centered diagonal base, and I would definitely keep it. 

A third useful item is the clearer fork in the involution route. The summary isolates the dependence of the quintic commutator channel on the parity of the cubic matrix coefficient \(X_3\):
if \(X_1\) is odd and \(X_3\) is odd, the commutator contribution to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is even; if \(X_3\) is even, it is odd. That is a real sharpening of where the descent problem sits. It tells you exactly what parity datum the current draft still does not resolve. 

The one part I would treat cautiously is the claim that centered symmetric-placement parity, after passing to
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
forces
\[
Y(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad S(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad \mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},\qquad \mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
and therefore kills the whole low-order mixed list. This is promising, but it crosses from the diagonal collision-side variable \(s\) into the good-patch \(x\)-chart, and that bridge is exactly where parity arguments have already proved delicate. I would keep that as a strong candidate theorem, not yet as settled fact, until the coordinate transfer is checked line by line. 

So my bottom line is:

The genuinely useful additions are the explicit \(D_2,D_4,D_6\) septic coefficients, the punctured-neighborhood exclusion near the centered diagonal base, and the sharpened \(X_3\)-parity fork in the involution route.

The potentially very important but still provisional addition is the claim that the centered-\(s\) parity package kills the full explicit low-order mixed \(4\)-point list after transfer to \(x=v_5/c\). That one deserves a careful re-check before it gets promoted.

## Edit 1: add the below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation

Insert this block **immediately after** the theorem/proposition where the draft first introduces the exact identities
\[
K_v=(x')^3S''(x),
\qquad
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr),
\]
and **before** the next discussion of nonmixed/mixed local models.

Use:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation]
\label{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation}
Let
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
M:=cv_5'-c'v_5.
\]
For any scalar germ \(f\), define
\[
J_f(h):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c(h)&v_5(h)&f(h)\\
c'(h)&v_5'(h)&f'(h)\\
c''(h)&v_5''(h)&f''(h)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{d^2}{dx^2}\!\left(\frac{f}{c}\right)
=
\frac{c^3}{M^3}\,J_f.
\]
Applying this to \(f=u_5\) and \(f=\lambda\) gives
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{\lambda},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_{\lambda}}.
}
\]
Differentiating in the \(x\)-coordinate yields
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_{\lambda}}\right).
}
\]
Thus the lifted \(4\)-point branch may be viewed equivalently as a
parity/divisibility problem for the Wronskian ratio \(J_{u_5}/J_{\lambda}\).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[A second below-lifted ratio does not add a new obstruction]
\label{rem:second-below-lifted-ratio-no-new-obstruction}
Let
\[
\Theta:=\frac{W_{u_5}}{W},
\]
where \(W\) denotes the corresponding projective-chart Wronskian in the
\((c,v_5,\cdot)\)-frame. In the gauge \(c\equiv 1\), \(v_5=x\), one has the
exact relation
\[
\Theta=\mathcal Z\,\frac{S''}{xS''+2S'},
\qquad
(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)S''=2\Theta S'.
\]
So \(\Theta\) does not provide an independent local obstruction beyond
\((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\): whenever \(2\Theta/(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)\) is
analytic, one can solve locally for \(S\) and then recover \(Y\) from
\(Y''=\mathcal Z S''\). In particular, attacks based only on a generic
differential relation between \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\Theta\) are too weak to
close the \(4\)-point branch.
\end{remark}
```

This captures the solid “below-lifted” identity and the no-go result about \(\Theta\). turn40file0

## Edit 2: add the exact finite obstruction coefficients for the nonmixed and mixed \(4\)-point branches

Insert this block **immediately after** the draft’s current nonmixed/mixed local-model discussion for the \(4\)-point branch, and **before** any broader WIP remark about the lifted order-\(7\) geometry.

Use:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Exact finite obstruction coefficients for the low-order \(4\)-point branch]
\label{rem:exact-finite-obstruction-coefficients-low-order-four-point}
The explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list can be reduced to a finite
jet package.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed side.}
Suppose \(K_v(0)\neq 0\), and write
\[
s_k:=S^{(k)}(0),
\qquad
y_k:=Y^{(k)}(0),
\qquad
s_2\neq 0.
\]
Then the Taylor expansion
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=z_0+z_1x+z_2x^2+z_3x^3+z_4x^4+z_5x^5+z_6x^6+O(x^7)
\]
has canonical even coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6,
\]
and the dangerous nonmixed low-order cases are exactly:
\[
n=4 \iff z_2\neq 0,
\qquad
n=6 \iff z_2=0,\ z_4\neq 0,
\qquad
n=8 \iff z_2=z_4=0,\ z_6\neq 0.
\]
Explicitly,
\[
z_2=
\frac{
s_2^2y_4-2s_2s_3y_3+\bigl(2s_3^2-s_2s_4\bigr)y_2
}{
2\,s_2^3
},
\]
\[
z_4=
\frac{
s_2^4y_6
-s_2^3(4s_3y_5+6s_4y_4+4s_5y_3+s_6y_2)
+2s_2^2(6s_3^2y_4+12s_3s_4y_3+4s_3s_5y_2+3s_4^2y_2)
-12s_2s_3^2(2s_3y_3+3s_4y_2)
+24s_3^4y_2
}{
24\,s_2^5
},
\]
and
\[
z_6=\frac{\mathcal P_8(s_2,\dots,s_8;y_2,\dots,y_8)}{720\,s_2^7},
\]
where \(\mathcal P_8\) is the explicit degree-\(8\) numerator polynomial obtained
by Taylor division of \(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\).

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Mixed side.}
Suppose \(K_v(0)=T_v(0)=0\), and let
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v.
\]
For the two low-order mixed cases \(r=1,2\), Taylor division of
\(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\) gives the exact obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2},
\]
defined by the expansions
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{y_2}{s_3}\frac1x
+
\left(\frac{y_3}{s_3}-\frac{s_4y_2}{2s_3^2}\right)
+
\kappa_{1,1}x+\kappa_{1,2}x^2+\kappa_{1,3}x^3+O(x^4)
\qquad (r=1),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{2y_2}{s_4}\frac1{x^2}
+
\left(\frac{2y_3}{s_4}-\frac{2s_5y_2}{3s_4^2}\right)\frac1x
+
\left(
\frac{y_4}{s_4}
-\frac{2s_5y_3}{3s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_2}{6s_4^2}
+\frac{2s_5^2y_2}{9s_4^3}
\right)
+\kappa_{2,1}x+\kappa_{2,2}x^2+O(x^3)
\qquad (r=2).
\]
The dangerous mixed low-order list is then exactly:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4)\iff \kappa_{1,1}\neq 0,
\]
\[
(m,n)=(3,6)\iff \kappa_{1,3}\neq 0,
\]
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff \kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

Thus the full currently explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set of coefficients
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]
Any RH-specific local closure theorem for the \(4\)-point branch must force
these six quantities to vanish.
\end{remark}
```

This captures the six exact obstruction coefficients. It is one of the best “goodies” to preserve.

## Edit 3: add the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and the diagonal-base local exclusion as a **WIP/attack** remark, not theorem-level

This is the part I would keep, but cautiously.

Insert this **immediately after** the previous obstruction-coefficient remark.

Use:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and diagonal-base local exclusion]
\label{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}
Let
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
and regard \(s\mapsto -s\) as swapping the two microscopic points. For any
symmetric \(2\times 2\) coefficient matrix, the diagonal half-sums are even in
\(s\), the diagonal half-differences are odd in \(s\), and the off-diagonal
entries are even in \(s\). Applying this to the explicit formulas already in the
draft gives
\[
u_5(s),\ v_5(s)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
u_{7,K_1}(s),\ v_{7,K_1}(s)\ \text{odd},
\]
and therefore
\[
\Delta_7(s)=u_{7,K_1}(s)v_5(s)-u_5(s)v_{7,K_1}(s)
\]
is even in \(s\), with Taylor expansion
\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2s^2+D_4s^4+D_6s^6+\cdots,
\]
where
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
\]

If \(x=v_5/c\) is used as the induced odd collision-side coordinate, then the
centered diagonal germ has the odd/odd form
\[
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n>m\ge 3.
\]
In that regime one obtains the exact factorizations
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),
\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)=x^{n-m}H(x^2),
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=x^{n-m-1}J(x^2),
\]
with \(H(0)\neq 0\) and \(J(0)\neq 0\). Hence there exists \(\varepsilon>0\)
such that for
\[
0<|x|<\varepsilon
\]
one has
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0.
\]

So the centered diagonal base has a punctured neighborhood free of mixed and
nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points. In particular, the currently explicit
low-order dangerous patterns do not arise at the symmetric diagonal base itself.

\medskip

\noindent
\textit{Work in progress.}
The passage from this centered \(s\)-picture to the general \(x=v_5/c\) good-patch
geometry should be treated as a live attack route, not yet as a global
theorem. The evidence strongly suggests that the entire explicit low-order mixed
dangerous list is already incompatible with this centered parity package, but
that translation should be checked line by line before being promoted beyond the
diagonal-base local regime.
\end{remark}
```

This preserves the useful local exclusion, but flags the patch-translation issue properly. The other summary’s strongest new positive claim lives here, and this is the safest way to incorporate it. turn40file16

## Edit 4: update the main lifted WIP remark

Replace the current `rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture` with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry is now significantly more stratified than a
single zero-capture problem.

First, shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v=0,
\]
respectively, with uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets.

Second, repeated-node limits are now identified explicitly:
three-point collapse limits become tangent-line contact determinants for the
planar lifted curve \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), and four-point collapse limits become
tangent-plane contact determinants for the lifted space curve \(Q_v=(Y,x,S)\).

Third, the three-point branch is locally classified near a finite-order
\(K_v\)-zero: even order gives no opposite-side branch, while odd order gives
exactly one local tangent-contact branch.

Fourth, the four-point side splits sharply into nonmixed and mixed regimes.
On the nonmixed side, finite-order odd \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine
local exact branch sheets in the model geometry, so a blanket local
no-branch theorem is false. On the mixed side, the dangerous low-order list is
now finite and explicit:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]

Fifth, below the lifted variables one has the exact Wronskian-ratio
reformulation
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right),
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
but the current draft still provides no RH-specific source-/matrix-level
identity strong enough to force the vanishing of the six low-order obstruction
coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

So the missing global ingredient is no longer a blanket first-contact theorem.
It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of multi-pair interaction defects for the two-point
branch;
\item global recurrence / continuation control for the unique odd-order
three-point branch;
\item a classification or RH-specific exclusion of nonmixed odd-order
four-point branch sheets;
\item and, on the mixed side, RH-specific jet restrictions excluding the
explicit low-order obstruction list.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}
```

This is the right overall WIP state now. turn41file1turn41file12

## Edit 5: update `rem:current-state-of-argument`

Replace the final “finite-core endgame” paragraph with:

```latex
In parallel, the finite-core endgame now splits into three layers.

First, on the two-pair side, the strengthened invariant
\[
\widehat\Psi(h)=
\left(
\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}
\right)
\]
gives the correct algebraic bridge, and on good \(M\neq 0\) patches the
quantitative two-pair coincidence theorem forces bad two-point cores into a
defect-scale close regime. The remaining structural issue there is now very
sharp: formalize the corrected quotient-germ construction at source level so
that the raw quadratic interaction factorization becomes automatic.

Second, on the lifted three-point side, shrinking exact circuits now
concentrate into \(K_v=0\), repeated-node limits become tangent-line contacts,
and finite-order \(K_v\)-zeros admit an explicit local branch classification:
even-order zeros are sterile, while odd-order zeros carry exactly one local
branch. The remaining issue there is therefore global recurrence / continuation,
not local first-contact ambiguity.

Third, on the lifted four-point side, shrinking exact circuits now
concentrate into \(T_v=0\), repeated-node limits become tangent-plane contacts,
and the local geometry splits into a nonmixed and a mixed regime. On the
nonmixed side, odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine local branch
sheets in the model geometry, so generic local geometry does not close the
branch. On the mixed side, the dangerous low-order obstruction list has been
reduced to the finite set of coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2},
\]
or equivalently to the explicit order patterns
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]
Any further local closure on the four-point side must therefore come from
deeper RH-specific source-/matrix-level structure rather than from the current
lifted variables alone.
```

That captures where the paper now really is. turn41file15

## Edit 6: add a short “live attack routes” remark near the end of the WIP section

Insert this **immediately after** `rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture`.

Use:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now quite sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected quotient-germ map exists and satisfies the
symmetry / one-amplitude collapse / diagonal collapse identities needed for the
quadratic interaction factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
This would finish the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local defect-free three-point branch is already classified. The remaining
problem is to control the global recurrence / continuation of the unique
odd-order branch and to exclude infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed classification.}
Generic nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros already support local exact branch
sheets, so the next local theorem is not a blanket sterility statement but a
classification / compatibility theorem for tangent-plane contact branches near a
nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zero.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed low-order exclusion.}
The mixed low-order obstruction list is finite and explicit:
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]
The centered symmetric diagonal analysis suggests these patterns are already
incompatible with the collision-side parity package, but that translation to
the general \(x=v_5/c\) patch geometry should be treated as a live attack route
rather than settled theorem-level closure.

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no obstruction can come from the lifted
variables alone, any definitive four-point closure theorem must come from
deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, for example an equivariant
descent theorem for the normalization stack or an RH-specific divisibility /
parity constraint on the Wronskian ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

This captures the current “live attack map” cleanly. It also avoids overstating the mixed-parity route while still recording it as promising. turn40file16

## 1. Replace the current “what remains in the lifted order-7 geometry” remark with a merged version

Find the existing remark with label
```latex
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
```
and replace the whole thing with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted geometry is now substantially more stratified than a single
zero-capture problem.

First, shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v=0,
\]
respectively, with uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets.

Second, repeated-node limits are now explicit:
three-point collapse limits become tangent-line contact determinants for the
planar lifted curve \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), and four-point collapse limits become
tangent-plane contact determinants for the lifted space curve \(Q_v=(Y,x,S)\).

Third, the three-point branch is locally classified near a finite-order
\(K_v\)-zero: even order gives no opposite-side branch, while odd order gives
exactly one local tangent-contact branch. Thus the remaining issue there is
global recurrence / continuation and infinite-order flatness, not local
first-contact ambiguity.

Fourth, the four-point side splits sharply into nonmixed and mixed regimes.
On the nonmixed side, finite-order odd \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine
local exact branch sheets in the model geometry, so a blanket local sterility
theorem is false. On the mixed side, the dangerous low-order obstruction list is
finite and explicit:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

Fifth, below the lifted variables one has the exact Wronskian-ratio
reformulation
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right),
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
while the projective curvature ratio \(\Theta\) yields no new independent local
obstruction beyond \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\).

Sixth, the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package gives a strong local
collision-side parity picture:
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,
\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even in }s,
\]
with explicit septic coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\). In the diagonal-centered
odd/odd normal form
\[
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n>m\ge 3,
\]
one gets a punctured neighborhood free of \(K_v=0\) and \(T_v=0\) points.
Thus the explicit low-order dangerous \(4\)-point patterns do not arise at the
symmetric diagonal base itself.

So the missing global ingredient is no longer a generic local geometry theorem.
It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of the multi-pair interaction defects
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)};
\]
\item global continuation / recurrence control for the unique odd-order
three-point branch;
\item a centered-to-patch bridge strong enough to promote the centered
collision-side parity package to the good-patch \(x=v_5/c\) geometry, at least
on the mixed four-point side;
\item and, on the still-live nonmixed side, a deeper RH-specific source- or
matrix-level identity imposing stronger parity / divisibility constraints on
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.
\]
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}
```

This absorbs most of the older overlapping WIP material into one canonical state-of-play remark.

## 2. Replace the current “dream identities” remark with a sharper two-route version

Find the remark with label
```latex
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
```
and replace it with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: two distinct parity routes on the $4$-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
There are now two distinct parity mechanisms on the lifted \(4\)-point branch.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed route.}
After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the natural dream identity remains:
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\ \text{is even in }\xi,
\]
equivalently \(\mathcal Z\) is odd modulo the affine coplanarity gauge. This
would eliminate the explicit nonmixed low-order bad list
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\}.
\]

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Centered collision-side route.}
In the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\), the explicit Taylor package
gives
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even}.
\]
If this parity transfers through the local coordinate change
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
then in the \(x\)-chart one obtains
\[
Y(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
This would eliminate the entire explicit low-order mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

Thus the centered collision-side parity package appears to point primarily at
the mixed branch, while the nonmixed odd-order branch remains the live
\(4\)-point bottleneck. At present, the centered-to-patch transfer should still
be treated as provisional outside the diagonal-based local regime.
\end{remark}
```

This replaces older wording that no longer reflects the split between the mixed and nonmixed parity attacks.

## 3. Replace the current “what the four-point branch reduces to” remark with a fuller merged version

Find the remark with label
```latex
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
```
and replace it with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted \(4\)-point branch is now organized by the canonical invariant pair
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

On the nonmixed side, after normalization to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
equivalently the first nontrivial even Taylor coefficients of \(\widetilde Y\)
occur in degrees \(4,6,8\). In an arbitrary nonmixed \(x\)-chart this is
captured exactly by the three obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6
\]
in the expansion of \(\mathcal Z\).

On the mixed side, the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]
In local mixed \(x\)-coordinates this is captured exactly by the three
obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

Thus the currently explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set of six quantities
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]

By the realization lemma, no identity involving only
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
and their derivatives can force these six quantities to vanish in general.
So any definitive local closure theorem for the four-point branch must come
from deeper RH-specific source- or matrix-level structure.

The most promising new development is the centered symmetric-placement Taylor
package, which gives explicit septic coefficients
\[
D_2,\qquad D_4,\qquad D_6
\]
and a punctured-neighborhood exclusion at the diagonal base. What remains
unclear is whether that collision-side parity package transfers all the way to
the general good-patch \(x=v_5/c\) geometry strongly enough to close the mixed
branch globally.
\end{remark}
```

This merges the most important “goodies” into one place and avoids scattering them across too many remarks.

## 5. Replace the current “live attack routes” remark with a more complete one

Find the remark with label
```latex
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
```
and replace it with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now quite sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected quotient-germ map exists and satisfies the
symmetry / one-amplitude collapse / diagonal collapse identities needed for the
quadratic interaction factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
This would finish the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local defect-free three-point branch is already classified. The remaining
problem is to control global recurrence / continuation of the unique odd-order
branch and to exclude infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch via centered parity.}
The centered symmetric-placement Taylor package suggests that the explicit
low-order mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is already incompatible with the collision-side parity picture. The next step is
to turn that local diagonal-based calculation into a theorem-level bridge for
the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\).

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed branch via deeper RH-specific identities.}
Generic local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets,
so the next local theorem is not a blanket sterility statement but a deeper
RH-specific parity / divisibility theorem strong enough to force extra
vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently of the nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]

\item
\textbf{Equivariant descent through the normalization stack.}
The most conceptual remaining route is to descend the raw swap/reflection
symmetry through the one-pair normalization stack and determine the parity of
the canonical residual package. The decisive fork appears to be the parity
behavior of the cubic matrix coefficient \(X_3\) in the commutator-channel
formula for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no obstruction can come from the lifted
variables alone, any definitive four-point closure theorem must ultimately come
from deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, for example an
equivariant descent theorem or an RH-specific divisibility / parity constraint
on the Wronskian ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

This better synthesizes both threads: it keeps the mixed-parity route alive, but clearly makes the nonmixed branch the deeper remaining bottleneck.

## 6. Add one short “post-draft findings” remark after `rem:current-state-of-argument`

```latex
\begin{remark}[Post-draft findings: established, provisional, and live]
\label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}
Since this draft state, three additional conclusions have emerged.

First, on the two-point branch, the correct remaining theorem is now very
sharp: a source-level corrected interaction remainder with swap symmetry,
one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse would force the quadratic
factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
hence the two-point bad-core branch is conditionally closed on compact good
patches.

Second, on the lifted four-point branch, the explicit low-order obstruction
list has been reduced to the six coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2},
\]
or equivalently to the order patterns
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\qquad
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

Third, the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package now gives explicit septic
coefficients
\[
D_2,\qquad D_4,\qquad D_6
\]
and a punctured-neighborhood exclusion at the diagonal base. What remains to be
checked carefully is the transfer of that collision-side parity package into the
general good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\).

So the present frontier is no longer a generic local geometry problem. It is
the combination of a source-level two-point structure theorem, a centered-to-
patch parity bridge for the mixed four-point branch, and a deeper RH-specific
identity on the nonmixed four-point branch.
\end{remark}
```

This gives the reader one clean “since the last draft” summary and lets you trim some older scattered mini-summaries.

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now splits into three regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
K_v=0,
\]
and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node
tangent-contact branch is completely classified: even order gives no
opposite-side branch, while odd order gives exactly one opposite-side branch.

\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), finite-order odd \(T_v\)-zeros can already

entire explicit low-order mixed list is already incompatible with the local
collision-side parity structure, once that parity is transferred carefully to
the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\). At present this should still be treated
as a live attack route rather than theorem-level closure.

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are now:
the continuation / non-recurrence of the unique odd-order \(3\)-point branch,
the continuation / non-recurrence of nonmixed odd-order \(4\)-point branches,
possible infinite-order flatness, and the completion of the centered-to-patch
bridge on the mixed \(4\)-point side.

```

and therefore
\[
\Delta_7(s)=u_{7,K_1}(s)v_5(s)-u_5(s)v_{7,K_1}(s)
\]
```

Insert:

```latex
Writing
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+U_5s^5+\cdots,
\qquad
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+V_5s^5+\cdots,
\]
the first coefficients are
\[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr),
\]
\[
U_3=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_3+v_2\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_3+\beta_2\,\delta u_1\bigr),
\]
\[
U_5=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_5+v_2\,\delta\alpha_3+v_4\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_5+\beta_2\,\delta u_3+\beta_4\,\delta u_1\bigr),
\]
and
\[
V_1=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_0\bigr),
\]
\[
V_3=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_0\bigr),
\]
\[
V_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_5+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_4\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_4+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u_0\bigr).
\]

Likewise, writing
\[
u_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat U_1s+\widehat U_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
v_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat V_1s+\widehat V_3s^3+\cdots,
\]
one gets
\[
\widehat U_1
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\,\nu_{6,0}
+\beta_{5,0}\,\delta u_1
+v_0\,\delta\alpha_{5,1}
+b_0\,\delta p_1
+r_0\,\delta a_1
\bigr),
\]
\[
\widehat V_1
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\,\bar\mu_{6,0}
-\bar x_0\,\delta\mu_{6,1}
+\bar\alpha_{5,0}\,\delta u_1
+\delta\alpha_{5,1}\,\bar u_0
+\bar a_0\,\delta p_1
+\delta a_1\,\bar p_0
\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\widehat U_3
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\nu_{6,2}+\delta x_3\nu_{6,0}
+\beta_{5,0}\delta u_3+\beta_{5,2}\delta u_1
+v_0\delta\alpha_{5,3}+v_2\delta\alpha_{5,1}
+b_0\delta p_3+b_2\delta p_1
+r_0\delta a_3+r_2\delta a_1
\bigr),
\]
\[
\widehat V_3
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\bar\mu_{6,2}+\delta x_3\bar\mu_{6,0}
-\bar x_0\delta\mu_{6,3}-\bar x_2\delta\mu_{6,1}
+\bar\alpha_{5,0}\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_{5,2}\delta u_1
+\delta\alpha_{5,1}\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_{5,3}\bar u_0
+\bar a_0\delta p_3+\bar a_2\delta p_1
+\delta a_1\bar p_2+\delta a_3\bar p_0
\bigr).
\]
```

This makes the remark genuinely self-contained and preserves the concrete low-order coefficient formulas that came out of the exploration.

_Thought for 56s_

Yes. My current route and the other chat’s route are now mostly **complementary**, not contradictory.

## My current route

My route is centered on the **lifted \(4\)-point branch itself**, especially the split between the mixed and nonmixed regimes.

The backbone is:
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\]
so the real local \(4\)-point invariants are \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\), or equivalently the Wronskian ratio \(J_{u_5}/J_\lambda\). From there, the explicit low-order obstruction list has been reduced to six concrete coefficients:
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]
Those are the exact nonmixed and mixed low-jet quantities that would have to vanish for a local \(4\)-point closure theorem. turn43file9

Within that, the strongest live sub-route is the **centered symmetric-placement parity bridge**. In the centered microscopic variable \(s\), one gets a very rigid Taylor package:
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even in }s,
\]
with explicit septic coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\). The hope is that, after carefully transferring this collision-side parity through the coordinate change \(x=v_5/c\), one gets the mixed-side parity pattern
\[
\ord_0 K_v \text{ odd},\qquad \ord_0\mathcal Z \text{ even},
\]
which would kill the whole explicit low-order mixed list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
At the moment I still treat that bridge as promising but not yet theorem-level globally. turn43file16

Separately, on the nonmixed side, my route is now much sharper than before: generic local geometry already supports odd-order nonmixed branch sheets, so I am **not** trying to prove a blanket local sterility theorem there. The live target is instead a deeper RH-specific parity/divisibility theorem forcing extra vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently forcing the nonmixed obstruction coefficients \(z_2,z_4,z_6\) to vanish. That almost certainly has to come from source-/matrix-level structure, not from the lifted variables alone. turn43file16

So, in one sentence: **my route is “close the mixed \(4\)-point branch via centered parity if possible; then isolate the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch as the genuinely deep remaining RH-specific local obstruction.”** turn43file8

## What the other chat is working on

The other chat is leaning much harder on the **finite-core / source-level** route.

Its main route is:

1. finish the source-level two-pair structure theorem,
   \[
   \mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
   \]
   so the \(2\)-point bad-core branch becomes conditionally closed on compact good patches;

2. use the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem to force bad two-pair cores to be defect-scale close;

3. then prove a **support-separation / shrinking-core concentration theorem**: nearby atoms in a minimal bad core either merge, or produce a repeated-node degeneration, and the repeated-node degeneration is locally ruled out away from the mixed locus \(K_v=T_v=0\);

4. conclude that small-defect bad finite cores can accumulate only at the mixed lifted locus (or at a small exceptional coincidence set). turn43file17turn43file14

That route also treats the lifted \(3\)-point branch as basically **locally solved**: shrinking circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\), repeated-node limits become tangent-line contacts, and finite-order zeros are completely classified:
even order means no local opposite-side branch, odd order means exactly one local branch. So the remaining \(3\)-point issue is not local existence anymore; it is global recurrence / continuation. turn44file2

On the \(4\)-point side, the other chat’s summaries are broadly compatible with mine: nonmixed odd-order local sheets are real; the mixed low-order list is explicit; and a real closure theorem must come from deeper RH-specific structure, not from the current lifted variables alone. Where it differs in emphasis is that it uses the finite-core/support-separation machinery to try to funnel everything into the mixed locus, then attack that locus as the sole remaining local obstruction. turn43file11

So, in one sentence: **the other chat’s route is “close the \(2\)-point/source-level branch, prove bad finite cores concentrate into the mixed lifted locus, and then finish the problem by killing that mixed locus.”** turn43file10

## Are they different routes?

Yes, but they mesh well.

My route is more **local-analytic on the lifted \(4\)-point side**:
it works directly with \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\), the centered \(s\)-Taylor package, the six obstruction coefficients, and the split between mixed and nonmixed \(4\)-point behavior. turn43file9

The other chat’s route is more **global finite-core / concentration-theorem** in flavor:
it tries to prove that any bad finite core must collapse into the mixed lifted locus, after which only that local obstruction remains. turn43file14

So I would describe them as:

- **my route:** kill the explicit mixed \(4\)-point branch locally via centered parity, then attack the nonmixed odd-order branch with deeper RH-specific identities;
- **other chat’s route:** use source-level \(2\)-point structure + support-separation to force all bad finite cores into the mixed locus, then kill the mixed locus.

They are not really competing. The best case is that they meet in the middle: if the centered-parity bridge really does kill the explicit mixed list, then the other chat’s concentration route becomes much stronger, because it would reduce bad finite cores to a locus that is already empty at low order. turn43file16turn43file17

_Thought for 47s_

Here’s the full handoff dump for **my route**.

## Core idea of my route

I am attacking the problem through the **lifted \(4\)-point branch**, with the view that the right local invariants are not \(Y\) or \(S\) separately, but
\[
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\qquad
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
on a good \(v_5\)-patch where
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
The exact identities are
\[
K_v=(x')^3S''(x),
\qquad
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr),
\]
so \(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R\) are the canonical local scalar invariants of the lifted \(4\)-point geometry. Also \(\mathcal R\) is fully gauge-invariant under
\[
Y\mapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S,
\]
while \(\mathcal Z\mapsto \mathcal Z+\gamma\). So the \(4\)-point branch should be thought of as a problem about \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\), not about \(Y\) in an arbitrary chart. turn45file13

My route then splits the \(4\)-point branch into:

1. **nonmixed:** \(K_v\neq 0\), where local odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine branch sheets, so generic local geometry does **not** kill the branch;

2. **mixed:** \(K_v=T_v=0\), where the dangerous low-order list is finite and explicit and may be killed by a parity bridge coming from the centered symmetric-placement variable. turn45file19

So the strategy is:

- try to **kill the mixed \(4\)-point branch** using the centered \(s\)-parity package and its transfer to the good-patch \(x=v_5/c\) coordinate;
- then isolate the **nonmixed \(4\)-point branch** as the genuinely deep remaining local obstruction, to be attacked by deeper RH-specific source-/matrix-level identities.

That is the backbone.

---

## Exact reductions I regard as solid

### 1. Nonmixed branch reduction

At a nonmixed point, after normalization one can write
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\qquad
\widetilde Y(0)=\widetilde Y'(0)=\widetilde Y''(0)=0.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal Z(\xi)=\frac12\widetilde Y''(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\widetilde Y'''(\xi).
\]
So the dangerous nonmixed low-order list is exactly
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
equivalently leading terms of \(\widetilde Y\) in degrees \(4,6,8\). This part is clean. turn45file4

### 2. Mixed branch reduction

At a mixed point, let
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad s:=\ord_0 T_v.
\]
Then
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=s-r+3,
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal Z=s-2r+1,
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal R=s-2r.
\]
So the dangerous mixed low-order list is exactly
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]
This finite list is one of the key structural reductions. turn45file15

### 3. Shrinking exact lifted circuits concentrate where expected

Shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\), and shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\). Repeated-node limits become tangent-line and tangent-plane contact determinants for the lifted curves \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\) and \(Q_v=(Y,x,S)\). So local first-contact ambiguity is largely gone; the issue is no longer “where can shrinking exact circuits go?” but “what local sheets actually exist there and can they recur globally?” turn45file12turn45file19

---

## Exact finite obstruction coefficients I want another chat to keep in view

I think these are very important and should not get lost.

### Nonmixed exact obstruction coefficients

If
\[
s_k:=S^{(k)}(0),\qquad y_k:=Y^{(k)}(0),\qquad s_2\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=z_0+z_1x+z_2x^2+z_3x^3+z_4x^4+z_5x^5+z_6x^6+\cdots,
\]
then:

- \(n=4\) iff \(z_2\neq 0\),
- \(n=6\) iff \(z_2=0\) but \(z_4\neq 0\),
- \(n=8\) iff \(z_2=z_4=0\) but \(z_6\neq 0\).

So the nonmixed low-order branch is equivalent to the vanishing problem
\[
z_2=z_4=z_6=0.
\]

I explicitly computed formulas for \(z_2,z_4,z_6\) in terms of the \(s_k,y_k\). These are the canonical low-order nonmixed obstruction coefficients. Another chat should preserve them and perhaps try to reinterpret them in terms of \(J_{u_5}/J_\lambda\). 

### Mixed exact obstruction coefficients

For the low-order mixed cases, I computed the coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2},
\]
coming from Taylor division of \(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\) in the \(r=1\) and \(r=2\) cases.

They satisfy:

- \((m,n)=(3,4)\) iff \(\kappa_{1,1}\neq 0\),
- \((m,n)=(3,6)\) iff \(\kappa_{1,3}\neq 0\),
- \((m,n)=(4,6)\) iff \(\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0\).

So the mixed low-order branch is equivalent to
\[
\kappa_{1,1}=\kappa_{1,3}=\kappa_{2,2}=0.
\]

Together with the nonmixed coefficients, the entire explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is reduced to the six exact quantities
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]
That is one of the main concrete outputs of my route. 

---

## Below-lifted reformulation I think is important

I found a very useful exact identity one level below \((Y,S)\):

For
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
and
\[
J_f(h):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c(h)&v_5(h)&f(h)\\
c'(h)&v_5'(h)&f'(h)\\
c''(h)&v_5''(h)&f''(h)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\]
and
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right),
\qquad
M=cv_5'-c'v_5.
\]

So the \(4\)-point branch can be reframed as a parity/divisibility question for the ratio
\[
\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]

This seems genuinely useful because it packages the whole local branch into one ratio of triple Wronskians in the original scalar data. If a deeper RH-specific identity exists, I think there is a decent chance it lives here rather than in ad hoc manipulations of \(Y\) and \(S\). turn45file18

I also found the projective ratio
\[
\Theta:=\frac{W_{u_5}}{W},
\]
with exact relation in the gauge \(c\equiv 1,\ v_5=x\),
\[
\Theta=\mathcal Z\,\frac{S''}{xS''+2S'},
\qquad
(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)S''=2\Theta S'.
\]
My conclusion from that is **negative**: \(\Theta\) does not add a genuinely new obstruction. If another chat tries to use \(\Theta\) as an independent invariant, I would be skeptical. turn45file18

---

## Strong negative theorem I think is crucial

I proved a realization lemma showing that arbitrary analytic germs \((\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)\) can be realized on a good \(v_5\)-patch by choosing
\[
c\equiv 1,\qquad
v_5=1+\xi,\qquad
u_5=\widetilde Y,\qquad
\Delta_7=(1+\xi)\widetilde S.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No identity involving only }c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7\text{ and their derivatives can exclude the dangerous low-order }4\text{-point patterns.}
}
\]

This is important because it means any true \(4\)-point closure theorem must come from **deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure**, not from the current lifted variables alone. If another chat starts trying to force a miraculous parity theorem at the current lifted-variable level, I think that’s probably wasted motion. turn45file15

---

## Centered symmetric-placement \(s\)-route: this is the most promising mixed-branch attack

This is the part I’m most interested in handing off carefully.

### What I think is solid

In the centered symmetric-placement variable
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
the half-sum / half-difference decomposition of symmetric \(2\times 2\) coefficient matrices gives:

- diagonal half-sums are even in \(s\),
- diagonal half-differences are odd in \(s\),
- off-diagonal entries are even in \(s\).

Pushing that through the explicit formulas already in the draft gives:
\[
u_5(s),\ v_5(s)\ \text{odd},
\]
\[
u_{7,K_1}(s),\ v_{7,K_1}(s)\ \text{odd},
\]
and therefore
\[
\Delta_7(s)=u_{7,K_1}(s)v_5(s)-u_5(s)v_{7,K_1}(s)
\]
is even in \(s\), with explicit coefficients
\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2s^2+D_4s^4+D_6s^6+\cdots,
\]
where
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
\]
That much I think is real and useful. turn45file8turn45file9

### What I then explored

Assuming
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+X_5s^5+\cdots
\]
is an odd coordinate whenever \(X_1\neq 0\). So parity in \(s\) transfers to parity in \(x\). This leads formally to
\[
Y(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\lambda(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\ \text{odd},
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd}.
\]

If that transfer is correct on the relevant good-patch domain, then the explicit low-order mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is dead immediately, because \(\ord_0 K_v\) would always be odd and \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\) always even. turn45file10

### My caution

I do **not** yet regard this as a settled theorem globally. It is the strongest promising mixed-branch route I know, but the precise transfer from the centered microscopic variable \(s\) to the later good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\) is subtle, and I have changed my mind once already about parity packages in this neighborhood. So I would hand this off as:

> very promising, likely right in spirit, but still needs a line-by-line coordinate-transfer check before being promoted.

That said, I think this is the best current attack on the mixed \(4\)-point branch. turn45file10

---

## Local diagonal-base result I think is solid

A piece of the centered-\(s\) route that I *do* think is solid is the diagonal-based local exclusion.

After affine normalization at the centered diagonal base, the local lifted germ has the odd/odd form
\[
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n>m\ge 3.
\]

Then one gets exact factorizations
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)=x^{n-m}H(x^2),\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=x^{n-m-1}J(x^2),
\]
with \(H(0)\neq 0\), \(J(0)\neq 0\). It follows that there is a punctured neighborhood around the diagonal base in which
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0
\]
for all sufficiently small nonzero \(x\).

So the explicit bad \(4\)-point patterns are **not born at the centered diagonal base** and not by an infinitesimal move away from it. This doesn’t solve the global problem, but it is a real local exclusion theorem and worth preserving. turn39file0

---

## Source-/matrix-level involution route: where I think it lives

I also explored whether the raw swap symmetry could descend to a parity theorem on the canonical package.

What survived is:

- there is a genuine precursor involution on the corrected odd germ,
  \[
  \Sigma(M)(s)=J_0\,M(-s)\,J_0;
  \]
- at the first residual step, this forces the quotient-level quintic ambiguity into the \(J_0\)-anti-fixed space;
- but once you descend to the fixed-sector scalar package, the crucial fork becomes the parity of the cubic matrix coefficient \(X_3\).

Using the commutator-channel formulas
\[
u_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=v(\gamma-\alpha)+\beta(u-w),\qquad
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=\gamma u-\alpha w,
\]
with
\[
X_1=\begin{pmatrix}u&v\\v&w\end{pmatrix},\qquad
X_3=\begin{pmatrix}\alpha&\beta\\ \beta&\gamma\end{pmatrix},
\]
I found:

- if \(X_1\) is odd and \(X_3\) is odd, then the commutator contribution to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is **even**;
- if \(X_1\) is odd and \(X_3\) is even, then the commutator contribution is **odd**.

So the involution route is still viable in principle, but it hinges on understanding whether \(X_3\) is the raw cubic coefficient of the descended odd family or an already-renormalized/equivariant correction term. That seems like the decisive fork. Another chat that wants to push the source-/matrix-level route should focus there. 

---

## What I think is dead / not worth much more time

These are routes I would deprioritize.

1. **Trying to kill the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch by generic local geometry.**  
   That is false. The normalized model
   \[
   Q(\xi)=(\xi^n,\xi,\xi^2),\qquad n\ \text{even},
   \]
   supports a genuine local exact branch sheet. So generic local geometry will not kill nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros. turn45file4

2. **Trying to find a new obstruction from \(\Theta\).**  
   I think that’s a dead end. \(\Theta\) is tied to \(\mathcal Z\) by a first-order relation and gives no new independent local obstruction. turn45file18

3. **Trying to force the low-order \(4\)-point closure from the current lifted variables alone.**  
   The realization lemma kills that. It has to come from deeper structure. turn45file15

---

## How my route interfaces with the other chat’s route

The other chat is mostly working on the **finite-core / source-level / concentration** route:

- make the \(2\)-pair structural factorization rigorous,
  \[
  \mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
  \]
  so the \(2\)-point bad-core branch is conditionally closed;

- use support-separation / shrinking-core concentration to force bad finite cores into the mixed locus;

- then finish the mixed locus. turn45file16turn45file17

My route is more local-analytic on the lifted \(4\)-point side:

- compute the exact local obstruction invariants \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\);
- reduce the bad list to the six coefficients
  \[
  z_2,z_4,z_6,\kappa_{1,1},\kappa_{1,3},\kappa_{2,2};
  \]
- try to kill the mixed list using centered \(s\)-parity;
- then isolate the nonmixed branch as the genuinely hard remaining local obstruction.

So the routes complement each other nicely:

- if my centered-\(s\) parity bridge kills the mixed low-order \(4\)-point list, then the other chat’s concentration route becomes much stronger;
- if the other chat succeeds in funneling bad finite cores into the mixed locus, then my mixed-parity route becomes the key local closure theorem.

---

## What I would ask another chat to do with this dump

If I were handing this off, I’d ask the other chat to pick one of these narrow targets:

### Target A: prove the centered \(s\)-to-\(x\) parity bridge rigorously
Specifically, check carefully whether the centered symmetric-placement parity
\[
u_5,v_5,u_{7,K_1},v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,\qquad \Delta_7\ \text{even in }s
\]
really implies
\[
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd}
\]
in the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\), and thus kills
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

### Target B: attack the source-/matrix-level involution fork
Work out exactly what parity \(X_3\) should have under the descended involution, and whether the commutator channel for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) becomes odd or even after descent.

### Target C: reinterpret the six obstruction coefficients in Wronskian-ratio language
Try to express
\[
z_2,z_4,z_6,\kappa_{1,1},\kappa_{1,3},\kappa_{2,2}
\]
directly in terms of the ratio
\[
\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}
\]
to see whether there is a hidden divisibility or parity cancellation.

If I had to choose just one, I would probably choose **Target A** first, because if the centered parity bridge is right, it likely kills the whole explicit low-order mixed \(4\)-point list in one shot, and that would substantially clarify the endgame.
